text-indent:-18.0pt;} ol {margin-bottom:0cm;} ul {margin-bottom:0cm;} -->

Enterprise Mitigations

Mitigations represent security concepts and classes of technologies that can be used to prevent a technique or sub-technique from being successfully executed.

Mitigations: 43

**ID**

**Name**

**Description**

[M1036](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1036)

[Account Use Policies](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1036)

Configure features related to account use like login attempt lockouts, specific login times, etc.

[M1015](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1015)

[Active Directory Configuration](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1015)

Configure Active Directory to prevent use of certain techniques; use SID Filtering, etc.

[M1049](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1049)

[Antivirus/Antimalware](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1049)

Use signatures or heuristics to detect malicious software.

[M1013](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1013)

[Application Developer Guidance](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1013)

This mitigation describes any guidance or training given to developers of applications to avoid introducing security weaknesses that an adversary may be able to take advantage of.

[M1048](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1048)

[Application Isolation and Sandboxing](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1048)

Restrict execution of code to a virtual environment on or in transit to an endpoint system.

[M1047](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1047)

[Audit](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1047)

Perform audits or scans of systems, permissions, insecure software, insecure configurations, etc. to identify potential weaknesses.

[M1040](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1040)

[Behavior Prevention on Endpoint](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1040)

Use capabilities to prevent suspicious behavior patterns from occurring on endpoint systems. This could include suspicious process, file, API call, etc. behavior.

[M1046](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1046)

[Boot Integrity](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1046)

Use secure methods to boot a system and verify the integrity of the operating system and loading mechanisms.

[M1045](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1045)

[Code Signing](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1045)

Enforce binary and application integrity with digital signature verification to prevent untrusted code from executing.

[M1043](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1043)

[Credential Access Protection](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1043)

Use capabilities to prevent successful credential access by adversaries; including blocking forms of credential dumping.

[M1053](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1053)

[Data Backup](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1053)

Take and store data backups from end user systems and critical servers. Ensure backup and storage systems are hardened and kept separate from the corporate network to prevent compromise.

[M1057](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1057)

[Data Loss Prevention](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1057)

Use a data loss prevention (DLP) strategy to categorize sensitive data, identify data formats indicative of personal identifiable information (PII), and restrict exfiltration of sensitive data.

[M1042](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1042)

[Disable or Remove Feature or Program](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1042)

Remove or deny access to unnecessary and potentially vulnerable software to prevent abuse by adversaries.

[M1055](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1055)

[Do Not Mitigate](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1055)

This category is to associate techniques that mitigation might increase risk of compromise and therefore mitigation is not recommended.

[M1041](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1041)

[Encrypt Sensitive Information](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1041)

Protect sensitive information with strong encryption.

[M1039](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1039)

[Environment Variable Permissions](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1039)

Prevent modification of environment variables by unauthorized users and groups.

[M1038](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1038)

[Execution Prevention](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1038)

Block execution of code on a system through application control, and/or script blocking.

[M1050](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1050)

[Exploit Protection](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1050)

Use capabilities to detect and block conditions that may lead to or be indicative of a software exploit occurring.

[M1037](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1037)

[Filter Network Traffic](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1037)

Use network appliances to filter ingress or egress traffic and perform protocol-based filtering. Configure software on endpoints to filter network traffic.

[M1035](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1035)

[Limit Access to Resource Over Network](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1035)

Prevent access to file shares, remote access to systems, unnecessary services. Mechanisms to limit access may include use of network concentrators, RDP gateways, etc.

[M1034](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1034)

[Limit Hardware Installation](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1034)

Block users or groups from installing or using unapproved hardware on systems, including USB devices.

[M1033](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1033)

[Limit Software Installation](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1033)

Block users or groups from installing unapproved software.

[M1032](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1032)

[Multi-factor Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1032)

Use two or more pieces of evidence to authenticate to a system; such as username and password in addition to a token from a physical smart card or token generator.

[M1031](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1031)

[Network Intrusion Prevention](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1031)

Use intrusion detection signatures to block traffic at network boundaries.

[M1030](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1030)

[Network Segmentation](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1030)

Architect sections of the network to isolate critical systems, functions, or resources. Use physical and logical segmentation to prevent access to potentially sensitive systems and information. Use a DMZ to contain any internet-facing services that should not be exposed from the internal network. Configure separate virtual private cloud (VPC) instances to isolate critical cloud systems.

[M1028](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1028)

[Operating System Configuration](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1028)

Make configuration changes related to the operating system or a common feature of the operating system that result in system hardening against techniques.

[M1027](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1027)

[Password Policies](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1027)

Set and enforce secure password policies for accounts.

[M1056](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1056)

[Pre-compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1056)

This category is used for any applicable mitigation activities that apply to techniques occurring before an adversary gains Initial Access, such as Reconnaissance and Resource Development techniques.

[M1026](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1026)

[Privileged Account Management](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1026)

Manage the creation, modification, use, and permissions associated to privileged accounts, including SYSTEM and root.

[M1025](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1025)

[Privileged Process Integrity](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1025)

Protect processes with high privileges that can be used to interact with critical system components through use of protected process light, anti-process injection defenses, or other process integrity enforcement measures.

[M1029](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1029)

[Remote Data Storage](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1029)

Use remote security log and sensitive file storage where access can be controlled better to prevent exposure of intrusion detection log data or sensitive information.

[M1022](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1022)

[Restrict File and Directory Permissions](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1022)

Restrict access by setting directory and file permissions that are not specific to users or privileged accounts.

[M1044](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1044)

[Restrict Library Loading](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1044)

Prevent abuse of library loading mechanisms in the operating system and software to load untrusted code by configuring appropriate library loading mechanisms and investigating potential vulnerable software.

[M1024](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1024)

[Restrict Registry Permissions](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1024)

Restrict the ability to modify certain hives or keys in the Windows Registry.

[M1021](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1021)

[Restrict Web-Based Content](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1021)

Restrict use of certain websites, block downloads/attachments, block Javascript, restrict browser extensions, etc.

[M1054](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1054)

[Software Configuration](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1054)

Implement configuration changes to software (other than the operating system) to mitigate security risks associated to how the software operates.

[M1020](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1020)

[SSL/TLS Inspection](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1020)

Break and inspect SSL/TLS sessions to look at encrypted web traffic for adversary activity.

[M1019](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1019)

[Threat Intelligence Program](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1019)

A threat intelligence program helps an organization generate their own threat intelligence information and track trends to inform defensive priorities to mitigate risk.

[M1051](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1051)

[Update Software](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1051)

Perform regular software updates to mitigate exploitation risk.

[M1052](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1052)

[User Account Control](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1052)

Configure Windows User Account Control to mitigate risk of adversaries obtaining elevated process access.

[M1018](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1018)

[User Account Management](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1018)

Manage the creation, modification, use, and permissions associated to user accounts.

[M1017](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1017)

[User Training](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1017)

Train users to be aware of access or manipulation attempts by an adversary to reduce the risk of successful spearphishing, social engineering, and other techniques that involve user interaction.

[M1016](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1016)

[Vulnerability Scanning](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1016)

Vulnerability scanning is used to find potentially exploitable software vulnerabilities to remediate them.

Account Use Policies
====================

Configure features related to account use like login attempt lockouts, specific login times, etc.

ID:M1036

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:21 October 2022

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1036/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1110](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110)

[Brute Force](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110)

Set account lockout policies after a certain number of failed login attempts to prevent passwords from being guessed. Too strict a policy may create a denial of service condition and render environments un-usable, with all accounts used in the brute force being locked-out. Use conditional access policies to block logins from non-compliant devices or from outside defined organization IP ranges.[\[1\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/active-directory/conditional-access/concept-conditional-access-policy-common)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/001)

[Password Guessing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/001)

Set account lockout policies after a certain number of failed login attempts to prevent passwords from being guessed. Too strict a policy may create a denial of service condition and render environments un-usable, with all accounts used in the brute force being locked-out. Use conditional access policies to block logins from non-compliant devices or from outside defined organization IP ranges.[\[1\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/active-directory/conditional-access/concept-conditional-access-policy-common)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/003)

[Password Spraying](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/003)

Set account lockout policies after a certain number of failed login attempts to prevent passwords from being guessed. Too strict a policy may create a denial of service condition and render environments un-usable, with all accounts used in the brute force being locked-out. Use conditional access policies to block logins from non-compliant devices or from outside defined organization IP ranges.[\[1\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/active-directory/conditional-access/concept-conditional-access-policy-common)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/004)

Set account lockout policies after a certain number of failed login attempts to prevent passwords from being guessed. Too strict a policy may create a denial of service condition and render environments un-usable, with all accounts used in the brute force being locked-out. Use conditional access policies to block logins from non-compliant devices or from outside defined organization IP ranges.[\[1\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/active-directory/conditional-access/concept-conditional-access-policy-common)

Enterprise

[T1621](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1621)

[Multi-Factor Authentication Request Generation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1621)

Enable account restrictions to prevent login attempts, and the subsequent 2FA/MFA service requests, from being initiated from suspicious locations or when the source of the login attempts do not match the location of the 2FA/MFA smart device. Use conditional access policies to block logins from non-compliant devices or from outside defined organization IP ranges.[\[1\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/active-directory/conditional-access/concept-conditional-access-policy-common)

Enterprise

[T1078](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/004)

[Cloud Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/004)

Active Directory Configuration
==============================

Configure Active Directory to prevent use of certain techniques; use SID Filtering, etc.

ID:M1015

Version:1.1

Created:06 June 2019

Last Modified:29 May 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1015/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1134](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/005)

[Access Token Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134):[SID-History Injection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/005)

Clean up SID-History attributes after legitimate account migration is complete.

Consider applying SID Filtering to interforest trusts, such as forest trusts and external trusts, to exclude SID-History from requests to access domain resources. SID Filtering ensures that any authentication requests over a trust only contain SIDs of security principals from the trusted domain (i.e preventing the trusted domain from claiming a user has membership in groups outside of the domain).

SID Filtering of forest trusts is enabled by default, but may have been disabled in some cases to allow a child domain to transitively access forest trusts. SID Filtering of external trusts is automatically enabled on all created external trusts using Server 2003 or later domain controllers.[\[1\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/cc755321.aspx)[\[2\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/cc794757.aspx)However note that SID Filtering is not automatically applied to legacy trusts or may have been deliberately disabled to allow inter-domain access to resources.

SID Filtering can be applied by:[\[3\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/cc835085.aspx)

 Disabling SIDHistory on forest trusts using the netdom tool (`netdom trust /domain: /EnableSIDHistory:no`on the domain controller)

 Applying SID Filter Quarantining to external trusts using the netdom tool (`netdom trust/domain:/quarantine:yes`on the domain controller)

 Applying SID Filtering to domain trusts within a single forest is not recommended as it is an unsupported configuration and can cause breaking changes.[\[3\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/cc835085.aspx)[\[4\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=1640)If a domain within a forest is untrustworthy then it should not be a member of the forest. In this situation it is necessary to first split the trusted and untrusted domains into separate forests where SID Filtering can be applied to an interforest trust

Enterprise

[T1606](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606/002)

[Forge Web Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606):[SAML Tokens](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606/002)

For containing the impact of a previously forged SAML token, rotate the token-signing AD FS certificate in rapid succession twice, which will invalidate any tokens generated using the previous certificate.[\[5\]](https://www.mandiant.com/resources/blog/remediation-and-hardening-strategies-for-microsoft-365-to-defend-against-unc2452)

Enterprise

[T1003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

[OS Credential Dumping](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

Manage the access control list for "Replicating Directory Changes" and other permissions associated with domain controller replication.[\[6\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=1729)[\[7\]](https://support.microsoft.com/help/303972/how-to-grant-the-replicating-directory-changes-permission-for-the-micr)Consider adding users to the "Protected Users" Active Directory security group. This can help limit the caching of users' plaintext credentials.[\[8\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/security/credentials-protection-and-management/protected-users-security-group)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/005)

[Cached Domain Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/005)

Consider adding users to the "Protected Users" Active Directory security group. This can help limit the caching of users' plaintext credentials.[\[8\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/security/credentials-protection-and-management/protected-users-security-group)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/006)

[DCSync](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/006)

Manage the access control list for "Replicating Directory Changes" and other permissions associated with domain controller replication.[\[9\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=1729)[\[7\]](https://support.microsoft.com/help/303972/how-to-grant-the-replicating-directory-changes-permission-for-the-micr)

Enterprise

[T1072](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

[Software Deployment Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

Ensure proper system and access isolation for critical network systems through use of group policy.

Enterprise

[T1649](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1649)

[Steal or Forge Authentication Certificates](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1649)

Ensure certificate authorities (CA) are properly secured, including treating CA servers (and other resources hosting CA certificates) as tier 0 assets. Harden abusable CA settings and attributes.

For example, consider disabling the usage of AD CS certificate SANs within relevant authentication protocol settings to enforce strict user mappings and prevent certificates from authenticating as other identifies.[\[10\]](https://www.specterops.io/assets/resources/Certified_Pre-Owned.pdf)Also consider enforcing CA Certificate Manager approval for the templates that include SAN as an issuance requirement.

Enterprise

[T1558](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558)

[Steal or Forge Kerberos Tickets](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558)

For containing the impact of a previously generated golden ticket, reset the built-in KRBTGT account password twice, which will invalidate any existing golden tickets that have been created with the KRBTGT hash and other Kerberos tickets derived from it. For each domain, change the KRBTGT account password once, force replication, and then change the password a second time. Consider rotating the KRBTGT account password every 180 days.[\[11\]](https://www.stigviewer.com/stig/windows_server_2016/2019-12-12/finding/V-91779)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/001)

[Golden Ticket](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/001)

For containing the impact of a previously generated golden ticket, reset the built-in KRBTGT account password twice, which will invalidate any existing golden tickets that have been created with the KRBTGT hash and other Kerberos tickets derived from it. For each domain, change the KRBTGT account password once, force replication, and then change the password a second time. Consider rotating the KRBTGT account password every 180 days.[\[11\]](https://www.stigviewer.com/stig/windows_server_2016/2019-12-12/finding/V-91779)

Enterprise

[T1552](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

[Unsecured Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

Remove vulnerable Group Policy Preferences.[\[12\]](http://support.microsoft.com/kb/2962486)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/006)

[Group Policy Preferences](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/006)

Remove vulnerable Group Policy Preferences.[\[12\]](http://support.microsoft.com/kb/2962486)

Enterprise

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/003)

[Pass the Ticket](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/003)

To contain the impact of a previously generated golden ticket, reset the built-in KRBTGT account password twice, which will invalidate any existing golden tickets that have been created with the KRBTGT hash and other Kerberos tickets derived from it.[\[13\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=483)For each domain, change the KRBTGT account password once, force replication, and then change the password a second time. Consider rotating the KRBTGT account password every 180 days.[\[11\]](https://www.stigviewer.com/stig/windows_server_2016/2019-12-12/finding/V-91779)

Enterprise

[T1078](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

6.  [Intel\_Acquisition\_Team. (2018, March 1). Credential Harvesting and Malicious File Delivery using Microsoft Office Template Injection. Retrieved July 20, 2018.](https://forum.anomali.com/t/credential-harvesting-and-malicious-file-delivery-using-microsoft-office-template-injection/2104)

Application Developer Guidance
==============================

This mitigation describes any guidance or training given to developers of applications to avoid introducing security weaknesses that an adversary may be able to take advantage of.

ID:M1013

Version:1.1

Created:25 October 2017

Last Modified:27 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1013/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1212](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1212)

[Exploitation for Credential Access](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1212)

Application developers should consider taking measures to validate authentication requests by enabling one-time passwords, providing timestamps or sequence numbers for messages sent, using digital signatures, and/or using random session keys.[\[1\]](https://www.comparitech.com/blog/information-security/what-is-a-replay-attack/)[\[2\]](https://www.bugcrowd.com/glossary/replay-attack/)

Enterprise

[T1564](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564)

[Hide Artifacts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564)

Application developers should consider limiting the requirements for custom or otherwise difficult to manage file/folder exclusions. Where possible, install applications to trusted system folder paths that are already protected by restricted file and directory permissions.

[.009](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/009)

[Resource Forking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/009)

Configure applications to use the application bundle structure which leverages the`/Resources`folder location.[\[3\]](https://support.apple.com/guide/security/app-security-overview-sec35dd877d0/1/web/1)

[.012](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/012)

[File/Path Exclusions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/012)

Application developers should consider limiting the requirements for custom or otherwise difficult to manage file/folder exclusions. Where possible, install applications to trusted system folder paths that are already protected by restricted file and directory permissions.

Enterprise

[T1574](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

[Hijack Execution Flow](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

When possible, include hash values in manifest files to help prevent side-loading of malicious libraries.[\[4\]](https://www.fireeye.com/content/dam/fireeye-www/global/en/current-threats/pdfs/rpt-dll-sideloading.pdf)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/002)

[DLL Side-Loading](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/002)

When possible, include hash values in manifest files to help prevent side-loading of malicious libraries.[\[4\]](https://www.fireeye.com/content/dam/fireeye-www/global/en/current-threats/pdfs/rpt-dll-sideloading.pdf)

Enterprise

[T1559](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559)

[Inter-Process Communication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559)

Enable the Hardened Runtime capability when developing applications. Do not include the`com.apple.security.get-task-allow`entitlement with the value set to any variation of true.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559/003)

[XPC Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559/003)

Enable the Hardened Runtime capability when developing applications. Do not include the`com.apple.security.get-task-allow`entitlement with the value set to any variation of true.

Enterprise

[T1647](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1647)

[Plist File Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1647)

Ensure applications are using Apple's developer guidance which enables hardened runtime.[\[5\]](https://developer.apple.com/documentation/security/hardened_runtime)

Enterprise

[T1593](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1593)

[Search Open Websites/Domains](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1593)

Application developers uploading to public code repositories should be careful to avoid publishing sensitive information such as credentials and API keys.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1593/003)

[Code Repositories](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1593/003)

Application developers uploading to public code repositories should be careful to avoid publishing sensitive information such as credentials and API keys.

Enterprise

[T1195](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195)

[Supply Chain Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195)

Application developers should be cautious when selecting third-party libraries to integrate into their application. Additionally, where possible, developers should lock software dependencies to specific versions rather than pulling the latest version on build.[\[6\]](https://www.cidersecurity.io/top-10-cicd-security-risks/)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/001)

[Compromise Software Dependencies and Development Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/001)

Application developers should be cautious when selecting third-party libraries to integrate into their application. Additionally, where possible, developers should lock software dependencies to specific versions rather than pulling the latest version on build.[\[6\]](https://www.cidersecurity.io/top-10-cicd-security-risks/)

Enterprise

[T1550](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

[Use Alternate Authentication Material](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

Consider implementing token binding strategies, such as Azure AD token protection or OAuth Proof of Possession, that cryptographically bind a token to a secret. This may prevent the token from being used without knowledge of the secret or possession of the device the token is tied to.[\[7\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/entra/identity/conditional-access/concept-token-protection)[\[8\]](https://www.okta.com/blog/2023/06/a-leap-forward-in-token-security-okta-adds-support-for-dpop/)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/001)

[Application Access Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/001)

Consider implementing token binding strategies, such as Azure AD token protection or OAuth Proof of Possession, that cryptographically bind a token to a secret. This may prevent the token from being used without knowledge of the secret or possession of the device the token is tied to.[\[7\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/entra/identity/conditional-access/concept-token-protection)[\[8\]](https://www.okta.com/blog/2023/06/a-leap-forward-in-token-security-okta-adds-support-for-dpop/)

Enterprise

[T1078](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

[Valid Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

Ensure that applications do not store sensitive data or credentials insecurely. (e.g. plaintext credentials in code, published credentials in repositories, or credentials in public cloud storage).

Mobile

[T1626](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1626)

[Abuse Elevation Control Mechanism](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1626)

Applications very rarely require administrator permission. Developers should be cautioned against using this higher degree of access to avoid being flagged as a potentially malicious application.

Mobile

[T1517](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1517)

[Access Notifications](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1517)

Application developers could be encouraged to avoid placing sensitive data in notification text.

Mobile

[T1513](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1513)

[Screen Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1513)

Application developers can apply the`FLAG_SECURE`property to sensitive screens within their apps to make it more difficult for the screen contents to be captured.[\[9\]](https://wwws.nightwatchcybersecurity.com/2016/04/13/research-securing-android-applications-from-screen-capture/)

Mobile

[T1635](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635)

[Steal Application Access Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635)

Developers should use Android App Links[\[10\]](https://developer.android.com/training/app-links/verify-site-associations)and iOS Universal Links[\[11\]](https://developer.apple.com/ios/universal-links/)to provide a secure binding between URIs and applications, preventing malicious applications from intercepting redirections. Additionally, for OAuth use cases, PKCE[\[12\]](https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7636)should be used to prevent use of stolen authorization codes.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635/001)

[URI Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635/001)

Developers should use Android App Links[\[10\]](https://developer.android.com/training/app-links/verify-site-associations)and iOS Universal Links[\[11\]](https://developer.apple.com/ios/universal-links/)to provide a secure binding between URIs and applications, preventing malicious applications from intercepting redirections. Additionally, for OAuth use cases, PKCE[\[12\]](https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7636)should be used to prevent use of stolen authorization codes.

Mobile

[T1474](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1474)

[Supply Chain Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1474)

Application developers should be cautious when selecting third-party libraries to integrate into their application.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1474/001)

[Compromise Software Dependencies and Development Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1474/001)

Application developers should be cautious when selecting third-party libraries to integrate into their application.

Application Isolation and Sandboxing
====================================

Restrict execution of code to a virtual environment on or in transit to an endpoint system.

ID:M1048

Version:1.1

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:31 March 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1048/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1189](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1189)

[Drive-by Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1189)

Browser sandboxes can be used to mitigate some of the impact of exploitation, but sandbox escapes may still exist.[\[1\]](https://blogs.windows.com/msedgedev/2017/03/23/strengthening-microsoft-edge-sandbox/)[\[2\]](https://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2017/03/hack-that-escapes-vm-by-exploiting-edge-browser-fetches-105000-at-pwn2own/)

Other types of virtualization and application microsegmentation may also mitigate the impact of client-side exploitation. The risks of additional exploits and weaknesses in implementation may still exist for these types of systems.[\[2\]](https://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2017/03/hack-that-escapes-vm-by-exploiting-edge-browser-fetches-105000-at-pwn2own/)

Enterprise

[T1611](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1611)

[Escape to Host](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1611)

Consider utilizing seccomp, seccomp-bpf, or a similar solution that restricts certain system calls such as mount. In Kubernetes environments, consider defining Pod Security Standards that limit container access to host process namespaces, the host network, and the host file system.[\[3\]](https://media.defense.gov/2022/Aug/29/2003066362/-1/-1/0/CTR_KUBERNETES_HARDENING_GUIDANCE_1.2_20220829.PDF)

Enterprise

[T1190](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1190)

[Exploit Public-Facing Application](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1190)

Application isolation will limit what other processes and system features the exploited target can access.

Enterprise

[T1203](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1203)

[Exploitation for Client Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1203)

Browser sandboxes can be used to mitigate some of the impact of exploitation, but sandbox escapes may still exist.[\[1\]](https://blogs.windows.com/msedgedev/2017/03/23/strengthening-microsoft-edge-sandbox/)[\[2\]](https://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2017/03/hack-that-escapes-vm-by-exploiting-edge-browser-fetches-105000-at-pwn2own/)

Other types of virtualization and application microsegmentation may also mitigate the impact of client-side exploitation. Risks of additional exploits and weaknesses in those systems may still exist.[\[2\]](https://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2017/03/hack-that-escapes-vm-by-exploiting-edge-browser-fetches-105000-at-pwn2own/)

Enterprise

[T1212](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1212)

[Exploitation for Credential Access](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1212)

Make it difficult for adversaries to advance their operation through exploitation of undiscovered or unpatched vulnerabilities by using sandboxing. Other types of virtualization and application microsegmentation may also mitigate the impact of some types of exploitation. Risks of additional exploits and weaknesses in these systems may still exist.[\[2\]](https://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2017/03/hack-that-escapes-vm-by-exploiting-edge-browser-fetches-105000-at-pwn2own/)

Enterprise

Enterprise

[T1068](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1068)

Other types of virtualization and application microsegmentation may also mitigate the impact of some types of exploitation. Risks of additional exploits and weaknesses in these systems may still exist.[\[2\]](https://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2017/03/hack-that-escapes-vm-by-exploiting-edge-browser-fetches-105000-at-pwn2own/)

[T1210](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1210)

Other types of virtualization and application microsegmentation may also mitigate the impact of some types of exploitation. Risks of additional exploits and weaknesses in these systems may still exist.[\[2\]](https://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2017/03/hack-that-escapes-vm-by-exploiting-edge-browser-fetches-105000-at-pwn2own/)

Enterprise

[Inter-Process Communication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559)

Audit
=====

Perform audits or scans of systems, permissions, insecure software, insecure configurations, etc. to identify potential weaknesses.

ID:M1047

Version:1.2

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:31 March 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1047/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1548](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

[Abuse Elevation Control Mechanism](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

Check for common UAC bypass weaknesses on Windows systems to be aware of the risk posture and address issues where appropriate.[\[1\]](https://github.com/hfiref0x/UACME)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/002)

[Bypass User Account Control](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/002)

Check for common UAC bypass weaknesses on Windows systems to be aware of the risk posture and address issues where appropriate.[\[1\]](https://github.com/hfiref0x/UACME)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/006)

[TCC Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/006)

Routinely check applications using Automation under Security & Privacy System Preferences. To reset permissions, user's can utilize the`tccutil reset`command. When using Mobile Device Management (MDM), review the list of enabled or disabled applications in the`MDMOverrides.plist`which overrides the TCC database.[\[2\]](https://www.sentinelone.com/labs/bypassing-macos-tcc-user-privacy-protections-by-accident-and-design/)

Enterprise

[T1087](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087/004)

[Account Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087):[Cloud Account](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087/004)

Routinely check user permissions to ensure only the expected users have the ability to list IAM identities or otherwise discover cloud accounts.

Enterprise

[T1560](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1560)

[Archive Collected Data](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1560)

System scans can be performed to identify unauthorized archival utilities.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1560/001)

[Archive via Utility](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1560/001)

System scans can be performed to identify unauthorized archival utilities.

Enterprise

[T1176](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1176)

[Browser Extensions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1176)

Ensure extensions that are installed are the intended ones as many malicious extensions will masquerade as legitimate ones.

Enterprise

[T1612](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1612)

[Build Image on Host](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1612)

Audit images deployed within the environment to ensure they do not contain any malicious components.

Enterprise

[T1059](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/006)

[Command and Scripting Interpreter](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059):[Python](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/006)

Inventory systems for unauthorized Python installations.

Enterprise

[T1543](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543)

[Create or Modify System Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543)

Use auditing tools capable of detecting privilege and service abuse opportunities on systems within an enterprise and correct them.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/003)

[Windows Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/003)

Use auditing tools capable of detecting privilege and service abuse opportunities on systems within an enterprise and correct them.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/004)

[Launch Daemon](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/004)

Use auditing tools capable of detecting folder permissions abuse opportunities on systems, especially reviewing changes made to folders by third-party software.

Enterprise

[T1530](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1530)

[Data from Cloud Storage](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1530)

Frequently check permissions on cloud storage to ensure proper permissions are set to deny open or unprivileged access to resources.[\[3\]](https://aws.amazon.com/premiumsupport/knowledge-center/secure-s3-resources/)

Enterprise

[T1213](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213)

[Data from Information Repositories](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213)

Consider periodic review of accounts and privileges for critical and sensitive repositories.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/001)

[Confluence](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/001)

Consider periodic review of accounts and privileges for critical and sensitive Confluence repositories.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/002)

[Sharepoint](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/002)

Consider periodic review of accounts and privileges for critical and sensitive SharePoint repositories.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/003)

[Code Repositories](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/003)

Consider periodic reviews of accounts and privileges for critical and sensitive code repositories. Scan code repositories for exposed credentials or other sensitive information.

Enterprise

[T1610](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1610)

[Deploy Container](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1610)

Scan images before deployment, and block those that are not in compliance with security policies. In Kubernetes environments, the admission controller can be used to validate images after a container deployment request is authenticated but before the container is deployed.[\[4\]](https://media.defense.gov/2022/Aug/29/2003066362/-1/-1/0/CTR_KUBERNETES_HARDENING_GUIDANCE_1.2_20220829.PDF)

Enterprise

[T1484](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1484)

[Domain or Tenant Policy Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1484)

Identify and correct GPO permissions abuse opportunities (ex: GPO modification privileges) using auditing tools such as[BloodHound](https://attack.mitre.org/software/S0521)(version 1.5.1 and later)[\[5\]](https://github.com/BloodHoundAD/BloodHound).

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1484/001)

[Group Policy Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1484/001)

Identify and correct GPO permissions abuse opportunities (ex: GPO modification privileges) using auditing tools such as[BloodHound](https://attack.mitre.org/software/S0521)(version 1.5.1 and later).[\[5\]](https://github.com/BloodHoundAD/BloodHound)

Enterprise

[T1114](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114)

[Email Collection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114)

Enterprise email solutions have monitoring mechanisms that may include the ability to audit auto-forwarding rules on a regular basis.

In an Exchange environment, Administrators can use Get-InboxRule to discover and remove potentially malicious auto-forwarding rules.[\[6\]](https://blogs.technet.microsoft.com/timmcmic/2015/06/08/exchange-and-office-365-mail-forwarding-2/)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114/003)

[Email Forwarding Rule](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114/003)

Enterprise email solutions have monitoring mechanisms that may include the ability to audit auto-forwarding rules on a regular basis.

In an Exchange environment, Administrators can use`Get-InboxRule`/`Remove-InboxRule`and`Get-TransportRule`/`Remove-TransportRule`to discover and remove potentially malicious auto-fowarding and transport rules.[\[6\]](https://blogs.technet.microsoft.com/timmcmic/2015/06/08/exchange-and-office-365-mail-forwarding-2/)[\[7\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/exchange/security-and-compliance/mail-flow-rules/manage-mail-flow-rules)[\[8\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/powershell/module/exchange/get-inboxrule?view=exchange-ps)In addition to this, a MAPI Editor can be utilized to examine the underlying database structure and discover any modifications/tampering of the properties of auto-forwarding rules.[\[9\]](https://blog.compass-security.com/2018/09/hidden-inbox-rules-in-microsoft-exchange/)

[T1606](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606)

[Forge Web Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606)

Administrators should perform an audit of all access lists and the permissions they have been granted to access web applications and services. This should be done extensively on all resources in order to establish a baseline, followed up on with periodic audits of new or updated resources. Suspicious accounts/credentials should be investigated and removed.

Enable advanced auditing on ADFS. Check the success and failure audit options in the ADFS Management snap-in. Enable Audit Application Generated events on the AD FS farm via Group Policy Object.[\[10\]](https://www.troopers.de/troopers19/agenda/fpxwmn/)

Enterprise

[T1574](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

[Hijack Execution Flow](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

Use auditing tools capable of detecting hijacking opportunities on systems within an enterprise and correct them. Toolkits like the PowerSploit framework contain PowerUp modules that can be used to explore systems for hijacking weaknesses.[\[11\]](https://github.com/mattifestation/PowerSploit)

Use the program sxstrace.exe that is included with Windows along with manual inspection to check manifest files for side-loading vulnerabilities in software.

Find and eliminate path interception weaknesses in program configuration files, scripts, the PATH environment variable, services, and in shortcuts by surrounding PATH variables with quotation marks when functions allow for them. Be aware of the search order Windows uses for executing or loading binaries and use fully qualified paths wherever appropriate.

Clean up old Windows Registry keys when software is uninstalled to avoid keys with no associated legitimate binaries. Periodically search for and correct or report path interception weaknesses on systems that may have been introduced using custom or available tools that report software using insecure path configurations.[\[12\]](http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/ms682425)[\[13\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/dlls/dynamic-link-library-security?redirectedfrom=MSDN)[\[14\]](https://skanthak.homepage.t-online.de/sentinel.html)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/001)

[DLL Search Order Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/001)

Use auditing tools capable of detecting DLL search order hijacking opportunities on systems within an enterprise and correct them. Toolkits like the PowerSploit framework contain PowerUp modules that can be used to explore systems for DLL hijacking weaknesses.[\[11\]](https://github.com/mattifestation/PowerSploit)

Use the program sxstrace.exe that is included with Windows along with manual inspection to check manifest files for side-by-side problems in software.[\[15\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows-server/administration/windows-commands/sxstrace)

[T1562](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/002)

[Disable Windows Event Logging](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/002)

Consider periodic review of`auditpol`settings for Administrator accounts and perform dynamic baselining on SIEM(s) to investigate potential malicious activity. Also ensure that the EventLog service and its threads are properly running.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/004)

[Disable or Modify System Firewall](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/004)

Routinely check account role permissions to ensure only expected users and roles have permission to modify system firewalls.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/007)

[Disable or Modify Cloud Firewall](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/007)

Routinely check account role permissions to ensure only expected users and roles have permission to modify cloud firewalls.

[.012](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/012)

[Disable or Modify Linux Audit System](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/012)

Routinely check account role permissions to ensure only expected users and roles have permission to modify logging settings.

To ensure Audit rules can not be modified at runtime, add the`auditctl -e 2`as the last command in the audit.rules files. Once started, any attempt to change the configuration in this mode will be audited and denied. The configuration can only be changed by rebooting the machine.

Enterprise

[T1556](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

[Modify Authentication Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

Review authentication logs to ensure that mechanisms such as enforcement of MFA are functioning as intended.

Periodically review the hybrid identity solution in use for any discrepancies. For example, review all Pass Through Authentication (PTA) agents in the Azure Management Portal to identify any unwanted or unapproved ones.[\[16\]](https://www.mandiant.com/resources/detecting-microsoft-365-azure-active-directory-backdoors)If ADFS is in use, review DLLs and executable files in the AD FS and Global Assembly Cache directories to ensure that they are signed by Microsoft. Note that in some cases binaries may be catalog-signed, which may cause the file to appear unsigned when viewing file properties.[\[17\]](https://www.microsoft.com/security/blog/2022/08/24/magicweb-nobeliums-post-compromise-trick-to-authenticate-as-anyone/)

Periodically review for new and unknown network provider DLLs within the Registry (`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Services\<NetworkProviderName>\NetworkProvider\ProviderPath`). Ensure only valid network provider DLLs are registered. The name of these can be found in the Registry key at`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\NetworkProvider\Order`, and have corresponding service subkey pointing to a DLL at`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentC ontrolSet\Services\<NetworkProviderName>\NetworkProvider`.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/006)

[Multi-Factor Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/006)

Review MFA actions alongside authentication logs to ensure that MFA-based logins are functioning as intended. Review user accounts to ensure that all accounts have MFA enabled.[\[18\]](https://www.mandiant.com/resources/blog/cloud-bad-log-configurations)

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/007)

[Hybrid Identity](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/007)

Periodically review the hybrid identity solution in use for any discrepancies. For example, review all PTA agents in the Azure Management Portal to identify any unwanted or unapproved ones.[\[16\]](https://www.mandiant.com/resources/detecting-microsoft-365-azure-active-directory-backdoors)If ADFS is in use, review DLLs and executable files in the AD FS and Global Assembly Cache directories to ensure that they are signed by Microsoft. Note that in some cases binaries may be catalog-signed, which may cause the file to appear unsigned when viewing file properties.[\[17\]](https://www.microsoft.com/security/blog/2022/08/24/magicweb-nobeliums-post-compromise-trick-to-authenticate-as-anyone/)

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/008)

[Network Provider DLL](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/008)

Periodically review for new and unknown network provider DLLs within the Registry (`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Services\<NetworkProviderName>\NetworkProvider\ProviderPath`).

Ensure only valid network provider DLLs are registered. The name of these can be found in the Registry key at`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\NetworkProvider\Order`, and have corresponding service subkey pointing to a DLL at`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentC ontrolSet\Services\<NetworkProviderName>\NetworkProvider`.

[T1053](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053)

[Scheduled Task/Job](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053)

Toolkits like the PowerSploit framework contain PowerUp modules that can be used to explore systems for permission weaknesses in scheduled tasks that could be used to escalate privileges.[\[11\]](https://github.com/mattifestation/PowerSploit)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/002)

[At](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/002)

Toolkits like the PowerSploit framework contain PowerUp modules that can be used to explore systems for permission weaknesses in scheduled tasks that could be used to escalate privileges.[\[11\]](https://github.com/mattifestation/PowerSploit)Windows operating system also creates a registry key specifically associated with the creation of a scheduled task on the destination host at: Microsoft\\Windows NT\\CurrentVersion\\Schedule\\TaskCache\\Tree\\At1.[\[22\]](https://www.secureworks.com/blog/where-you-at-indicators-of-lateral-movement-using-at-exe-on-windows-7-systems)In Linux and macOS environments, scheduled tasks using`[at](https://attack.mitre.org/software/S0110)`can be audited locally, or through centrally collected logging, using syslog, or auditd events from the host.[\[23\]](https://kifarunix.com/scheduling-tasks-using-at-command-in-linux/)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/003)

[Cron](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/003)

Review changes to the`cron`schedule.`cron`execution can be reviewed within the`/var/log`directory. To validate the location of the`cron`log file, check the syslog config at`/etc/rsyslog.conf`or`/etc/syslog.conf`

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/005)

[Scheduled Task](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/005)

Toolkits like the PowerSploit framework contain PowerUp modules that can be used to explore systems for permission weaknesses in scheduled tasks that could be used to escalate privileges.[\[11\]](https://github.com/mattifestation/PowerSploit)

[T1528](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1528)

[T1649](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1649)

[Steal or Forge Authentication Certificates](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1649)

Check and remediate unneeded existing authentication certificates as well as common abusable misconfigurations of CA settings and permissions, such as AD CS certificate enrollment permissions and published overly permissive certificate templates (which define available settings for created certificates). For example, available AD CS certificate templates can be checked via the Certificate Authority MMC snap-in (`certsrv.msc`).`certutil.exe`can also be used to examine various information within an AD CS CA database.[\[24\]](https://web.archive.org/web/20220818094600/https:/specterops.io/assets/resources/Certified_Pre-Owned.pdf)[\[25\]](https://github.com/GhostPack/PSPKIAudit)[\[26\]](https://github.com/GhostPack/Certify/)

[T1558](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558)

[Steal or Forge Kerberos Tickets](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558)

Perform audits or scans of systems, permissions, insecure software, insecure configurations, etc. to identify potential weaknesses.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/004)

[AS-REP Roasting](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/004)

Kerberos preauthentication is enabled by default. Older protocols might not support preauthentication therefore it is possible to have this setting disabled. Make sure that all accounts have preauthentication whenever possible and audit changes to setting. Windows tools such as PowerShell may be used to easily find which accounts have preauthentication disabled.[\[27\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/windows/it-pro/windows-2000-server/cc961961(v=technet.10)?redirectedfrom=MSDN)[\[28\]](https://blog.stealthbits.com/cracking-active-directory-passwords-with-as-rep-roasting/)

[T1552](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/001)

[Credentials In Files](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/001)

Preemptively search for files containing passwords and take actions to reduce the exposure risk when found.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/002)

[Credentials in Registry](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/002)

Proactively search for credentials within the Registry and attempt to remediate the risk.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/004)

[Private Keys](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/004)

Ensure only authorized keys are allowed access to critical resources and audit access lists regularly.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/006)

[Group Policy Preferences](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/006)

Search SYSVOL for any existing GGPs that may contain credentials and remove them.[\[29\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2288)

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/008)

[Chat Messages](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/008)

Preemptively search through communication services to find shared unsecured credentials. Searching for common patterns like "`password is`", "`password=`" and take actions to reduce exposure when found.

Enterprise

[T1550](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

[Use Alternate Authentication Material](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

Perform audits or scans of systems, permissions, insecure software, insecure configurations, etc. to identify potential weaknesses.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/001)

[Application Access Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/001)

Administrators should audit all cloud and container accounts to ensure that they are necessary and that the permissions granted to them are appropriate. Where possible, the ability to request temporary account tokens on behalf of another accounts should be disabled. Additionally, administrators can leverage audit tools to monitor actions that can be conducted as a result of OAuth 2.0 access. For instance, audit reports enable admins to identify privilege escalation actions such as role creations or policy modifications, which could be actions performed after initial access.

Enterprise

[T1204](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/003)

[User Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204):[Malicious Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/003)

Audit images deployed within the environment to ensure they do not contain any malicious components.

Behavior Prevention on Endpoint
===============================

Use capabilities to prevent suspicious behavior patterns from occurring on endpoint systems. This could include suspicious process, file, API call, etc. behavior.

ID:M1040

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:11 June 2019

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1040/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1059](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

[Command and Scripting Interpreter](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

On Windows 10, enable Attack Surface Reduction (ASR) rules to prevent[Visual Basic](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/005)and[JavaScript](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/007)scripts from executing potentially malicious downloaded content[\[1\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/security/defender-endpoint/attack-surface-reduction).

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/005)

[Visual Basic](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/005)

Enterprise

[T1204](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204)

[User Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204)

On Windows 10, enable Attack Surface Reduction (ASR) rules to prevent executable files from running unless they meet a prevalence, age, or trusted list criteria and to prevent Office applications from creating potentially malicious executable content by blocking malicious code from being written to disk. Note: cloud-delivered protection must be enabled to use certain rules.[\[1\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/security/defender-endpoint/attack-surface-reduction)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/002)

[Malicious File](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/002)

On Windows 10, various Attack Surface Reduction (ASR) rules can be enabled to prevent the execution of potentially malicious executable files (such as those that have been downloaded and executed by Office applications/scripting interpreters/email clients or that do not meet specific prevalence, age, or trusted list criteria). Note: cloud-delivered protection must be enabled for certain rules.[\[1\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/security/defender-endpoint/attack-surface-reduction)

Enterprise

[T1047](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1047)

[Windows Management Instrumentation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1047)

On Windows 10, enable Attack Surface Reduction (ASR) rules to block processes created by WMI commands from running. Note: many legitimate tools and applications utilize WMI for command execution.[\[1\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/security/defender-endpoint/attack-surface-reduction)

Boot Integrity
==============

Use secure methods to boot a system and verify the integrity of the operating system and loading mechanisms.

ID:M1046

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:19 May 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1046/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1495](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1495)

[Firmware Corruption](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1495)

Check the integrity of the existing BIOS and device firmware to determine if it is vulnerable to modification.

Enterprise

[T1601](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601)

[Modify System Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601)

Some vendors of embedded network devices provide cryptographic signing to ensure the integrity of operating system images at boot time. Implement where available, following vendor guidelines.[\[1\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#35)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601/001)

[Patch System Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601/001)

Some vendors of embedded network devices provide cryptographic signing to ensure the integrity of operating system images at boot time. Implement where available, following vendor guidelines.[\[1\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#35)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601/002)

[Downgrade System Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601/002)

Some vendors of embedded network devices provide cryptographic signing to ensure the integrity of operating system images at boot time. Implement where available, following vendor guidelines.[\[1\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#35)

Enterprise

[T1542](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542)

[Pre-OS Boot](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542)

Use Trusted Platform Module technology and a secure or trusted boot process to prevent system integrity from being compromised. Check the integrity of the existing BIOS or EFI to determine if it is vulnerable to modification.[\[2\]](http://www.trustedcomputinggroup.org/wp-content/uploads/Trusted-Platform-Module-Summary_04292008.pdf)[\[3\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/information-protection/secure-the-windows-10-boot-process)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/001)

[System Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/001)

Check the integrity of the existing BIOS or EFI to determine if it is vulnerable to modification. Use Trusted Platform Module technology.[\[2\]](http://www.trustedcomputinggroup.org/wp-content/uploads/Trusted-Platform-Module-Summary_04292008.pdf)Move system's root of trust to hardware to prevent tampering with the SPI flash memory.[\[4\]](https://www.welivesecurity.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/ESET-LoJax.pdf)Technologies such as Intel Boot Guard can assist with this.[\[5\]](https://www.intel.com/content/dam/www/public/us/en/documents/white-papers/security-technologies-4th-gen-core-retail-paper.pdf)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/003)

[Bootkit](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/003)

Use Trusted Platform Module technology and a secure or trusted boot process to prevent system integrity from being compromised.[\[2\]](http://www.trustedcomputinggroup.org/wp-content/uploads/Trusted-Platform-Module-Summary_04292008.pdf)[\[3\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/information-protection/secure-the-windows-10-boot-process)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/004)

[ROMMONkit](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/004)

Enable secure boot features to validate the digital signature of the boot environment and system image using a special purpose hardware device. If the validation check fails, the device will fail to boot preventing loading of unauthorized software.[\[1\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#35)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/005)

[TFTP Boot](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/005)

Enable secure boot features to validate the digital signature of the boot environment and system image using a special purpose hardware device. If the validation check fails, the device will fail to boot preventing loading of unauthorized software.[\[1\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#35)

Enterprise

[T1553](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/006)

[Subvert Trust Controls](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553):[Code Signing Policy Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/006)

Use of Secure Boot may prevent some implementations of modification to code signing policies.[\[6\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-hardware/drivers/install/the-testsigning-boot-configuration-option)

Enterprise

[T1195](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195)

[Supply Chain Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195)

Use secure methods to boot a system and verify the integrity of the operating system and loading mechanisms.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/003)

[Compromise Hardware Supply Chain](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/003)

Use Trusted Platform Module technology and a secure or trusted boot process to prevent system integrity from being compromised. Check the integrity of the existing BIOS or EFI to determine if it is vulnerable to modification.[\[2\]](http://www.trustedcomputinggroup.org/wp-content/uploads/Trusted-Platform-Module-Summary_04292008.pdf)[\[3\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/information-protection/secure-the-windows-10-boot-process)

Code Signing
============

Enforce binary and application integrity with digital signature verification to prevent untrusted code from executing.

ID:M1045

Version:1.1

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:20 May 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1045/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1059](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

[Command and Scripting Interpreter](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

Where possible, only permit execution of signed scripts.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/001)

[PowerShell](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/001)

Set PowerShell execution policy to execute only signed scripts.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/002)

[AppleScript](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/002)

Require that all AppleScript be signed by a trusted developer ID before being executed - this will prevent random AppleScript code from executing.[\[1\]](https://www.engadget.com/2013/10/23/applescript-and-automator-gain-new-features-in-os-x-mavericks/)This subjects AppleScript code to the same scrutiny as other .app files passing through Gatekeeper.

Enterprise

[T1554](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1554)

[Compromise Host Software Binary](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1554)

Ensure all application component binaries are signed by the correct application developers.

Enterprise

[T1543](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543)

[Create or Modify System Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543)

Enforce registration and execution of only legitimately signed service drivers where possible.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/003)

[Windows Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/003)

Enforce registration and execution of only legitimately signed service drivers where possible.

Enterprise

[T1546](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/006)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546):[LC\_LOAD\_DYLIB Addition](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/006)

Enforce that all binaries be signed by the correct Apple Developer IDs.

[.013](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/013)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546):[PowerShell Profile](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/013)

Enforce execution of only signed PowerShell scripts. Sign profiles to avoid them from being modified.

Enterprise

[T1525](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1525)

[Implant Internal Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1525)

Several cloud service providers support content trust models that require container images be signed by trusted sources.[\[2\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/container-registry/container-registry-content-trust)[\[3\]](https://docs.docker.com/engine/security/trust/content_trust/)

Enterprise

[T1036](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036)

[Masquerading](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036)

Require signed binaries.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036/001)

[Invalid Code Signature](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036/001)

Require signed binaries.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036/005)

[Match Legitimate Name or Location](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036/005)

Require signed binaries and images.

Enterprise

[T1601](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601)

[Modify System Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601)

Many vendors provide digitally signed operating system images to validate the integrity of the software used on their platform. Make use of this feature where possible in order to prevent and/or detect attempts by adversaries to compromise the system image.[\[4\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#34)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601/001)

[Patch System Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601/001)

Many vendors provide digitally signed operating system images to validate the integrity of the software used on their platform. Make use of this feature where possible in order to prevent and/or detect attempts by adversaries to compromise the system image.[\[4\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#34)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601/002)

[Downgrade System Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601/002)

Many vendors provide digitally signed operating system images to validate the integrity of the software used on their platform. Make use of this feature where possible in order to prevent and/or detect attempts by adversaries to compromise the system image.[\[4\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#34)

Enterprise

[T1505](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505)

[Server Software Component](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505)

Ensure all application component binaries are signed by the correct application developers.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505/001)

[SQL Stored Procedures](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505/001)

Ensure all application component binaries are signed by the correct application developers.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505/002)

[Transport Agent](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505/002)

Ensure all application component binaries are signed by the correct application developers.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505/004)

[IIS Components](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505/004)

Ensure IIS DLLs and binaries are signed by the correct application developers.

Enterprise

[T1204](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/003)

[User Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204):[Malicious Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/003)

Utilize a trust model such as Docker Content Trust with digital signatures to ensure runtime verification of the integrity and publisher of specific image tags.[\[3\]](https://docs.docker.com/engine/security/trust/content_trust/)[\[2\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/container-registry/container-registry-content-trust)
