Credential Access Protection
============================

Use capabilities to prevent successful credential access by adversaries; including blocking forms of credential dumping.

ID:M1043

Version:1.1

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:21 October 2022

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1043/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1547](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547)

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/008)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[LSASS Driver](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/008)

On Windows 10 and Server 2016, enable Windows Defender Credential Guard[\[1\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/access-protection/credential-guard/credential-guard-manage)to run lsass.exe in an isolated virtualized environment without any device drivers.[\[2\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/access-protection/credential-guard/credential-guard-how-it-works)

Enterprise

[T1601](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601)

[Modify System Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601)

Some embedded network devices are capable of storing passwords for local accounts in either plain-text or encrypted formats. Ensure that, where available, local passwords are always encrypted, per vendor recommendations.[\[3\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#40)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601/001)

[Patch System Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601/001)

Some embedded network devices are capable of storing passwords for local accounts in either plain-text or encrypted formats. Ensure that, where available, local passwords are always encrypted, per vendor recommendations.[\[3\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#40)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601/002)

[Downgrade System Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601/002)

Some embedded network devices are capable of storing passwords for local accounts in either plain-text or encrypted formats. Ensure that, where available, local passwords are always encrypted, per vendor recommendations.[\[3\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#40)

Enterprise

[T1599](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1599)

[Network Boundary Bridging](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1599)

Some embedded network devices are capable of storing passwords for local accounts in either plain-text or encrypted formats. Ensure that, where available, local passwords are always encrypted, per vendor recommendations.[\[4\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#38)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1599/001)

[Network Address Translation Traversal](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1599/001)

Some embedded network devices are capable of storing passwords for local accounts in either plain-text or encrypted formats. Ensure that, where available, local passwords are always encrypted, per vendor recommendations.[\[4\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#38)

Enterprise

[T1003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

[OS Credential Dumping](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

With Windows 10, Microsoft implemented new protections called Credential Guard to protect the LSA secrets that can be used to obtain credentials through forms of credential dumping. It is not configured by default and has hardware and firmware system requirements.[\[5\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/itpro/windows/keep-secure/credential-guard)It also does not protect against all forms of credential dumping.[\[6\]](https://github.com/iadgov/Secure-Host-Baseline/tree/master/Credential%20Guard)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/001)

[LSASS Memory](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/001)

With Windows 10, Microsoft implemented new protections called Credential Guard to protect the LSA secrets that can be used to obtain credentials through forms of credential dumping. It is not configured by default and has hardware and firmware system requirements. It also does not protect against all forms of credential dumping.[\[5\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/itpro/windows/keep-secure/credential-guard)[\[6\]](https://github.com/iadgov/Secure-Host-Baseline/tree/master/Credential%20Guard)

Data Backup
===========

Take and store data backups from end user systems and critical servers. Ensure backup and storage systems are hardened and kept separate from the corporate network to prevent compromise.

ID:M1053

Version:1.1

Created:19 July 2019

Last Modified:31 March 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1053/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1485](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1485)

[Data Destruction](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1485)

Consider implementing IT disaster recovery plans that contain procedures for taking regular data backups that can be used to restore organizational data.[\[1\]](https://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/IT)Ensure backups are stored off system and is protected from common methods adversaries may use to gain access and destroy the backups to prevent recovery.

Enterprise

[T1486](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1486)

[Data Encrypted for Impact](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1486)

Consider implementing IT disaster recovery plans that contain procedures for regularly taking and testing data backups that can be used to restore organizational data.[\[1\]](https://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/IT)Ensure backups are stored off system and is protected from common methods adversaries may use to gain access and destroy the backups to prevent recovery. Consider enabling versioning in cloud environments to maintain backup copies of storage objects.[\[2\]](https://rhinosecuritylabs.com/aws/s3-ransomware-part-2-prevention-and-defense/)

Enterprise

[T1491](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1491)

[Defacement](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1491)

Consider implementing IT disaster recovery plans that contain procedures for taking regular data backups that can be used to restore organizational data.[\[1\]](https://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/IT)Ensure backups are stored off system and is protected from common methods adversaries may use to gain access and destroy the backups to prevent recovery.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1491/001)

[Internal Defacement](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1491/001)

Consider implementing IT disaster recovery plans that contain procedures for taking regular data backups that can be used to restore organizational data.[\[1\]](https://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/IT)Ensure backups are stored off system and is protected from common methods adversaries may use to gain access and destroy the backups to prevent recovery.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1491/002)

Consider implementing IT disaster recovery plans that contain procedures for taking regular data backups that can be used to restore organizational data.[\[1\]](https://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/IT)Ensure backups are stored off system and is protected from common methods adversaries may use to gain access and destroy the backups to prevent recovery.

Consider implementing IT disaster recovery plans that contain procedures for taking regular data backups that can be used to restore organizational data.[\[1\]](https://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/IT)Ensure backups are stored off system and is protected from common methods adversaries may use to gain access and destroy the backups to prevent recovery.

Consider implementing IT disaster recovery plans that contain procedures for taking regular data backups that can be used to restore organizational data.[\[1\]](https://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/IT)Ensure backups are stored off system and is protected from common methods adversaries may use to gain access and destroy the backups to prevent recovery.

Enterprise

[T1490](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1490)

[Inhibit System Recovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1490)

Consider implementing IT disaster recovery plans that contain procedures for taking regular data backups that can be used to restore organizational data.[\[1\]](https://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/IT)Ensure backups are stored off system and is protected from common methods adversaries may use to gain access and destroy the backups to prevent recovery. In cloud environments, enable versioning on storage objects where possible, and copy backups to other accounts or regions to isolate them from the original copies.[\[3\]](https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/ransomware-in-public-clouds/)

Data Loss Prevention
====================

Use a data loss prevention (DLP) strategy to categorize sensitive data, identify data formats indicative of personal identifiable information (PII), and restrict exfiltration of sensitive data.[\[1\]](https://purplesec.us/data-loss-prevention/)

ID:M1057

Version:1.0

Created:04 August 2021

Last Modified:30 August 2021

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1057/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1005)

[Data from Local System](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1005)

Data loss prevention can restrict access to sensitive data and detect sensitive data that is unencrypted.

Enterprise

[T1025](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1025)

[Data from Removable Media](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1025)

Data loss prevention can restrict access to sensitive data and detect sensitive data that is unencrypted.

Enterprise

[T1048](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048)

[Exfiltration Over Alternative Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048)

Data loss prevention can detect and block sensitive data being uploaded via web browsers.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048/002)

[Exfiltration Over Asymmetric Encrypted Non-C2 Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048/002)

Data loss prevention can detect and block sensitive data being uploaded via web browsers.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048/003)

[Exfiltration Over Unencrypted Non-C2 Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048/003)

Data loss prevention can detect and block sensitive data being sent over unencrypted protocols.

Enterprise

[T1041](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1041)

[Exfiltration Over C2 Channel](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1041)

Data loss prevention can detect and block sensitive data being sent over unencrypted protocols.

Enterprise

[T1052](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1052)

[Exfiltration Over Physical Medium](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1052)

Data loss prevention can detect and block sensitive data being copied to physical mediums.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1052/001)

[Exfiltration over USB](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1052/001)

Data loss prevention can detect and block sensitive data being copied to USB devices.

Enterprise

[T1567](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567)

[Exfiltration Over Web Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567)

Data loss prevention can be detect and block sensitive data being uploaded to web services via web browsers.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567/004)

[Exfiltration Over Webhook](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567/004)

Data loss prevention can be detect and block sensitive data being uploaded to web services via web browsers.

Enterprise

[T1537](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1537)

[Transfer Data to Cloud Account](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1537)

Data loss prevention can prevent and block sensitive data from being shared with individuals outside an organization.[\[2\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/purview/dlp-learn-about-dlp)[\[3\]](https://support.google.com/a/answer/9646351)

**References**
--------------

1.  [Michael Swanagan. (2020, October 24). 7 Data Loss Prevention Best Practices & Strategies. Retrieved August 30, 2021.](https://purplesec.us/data-loss-prevention/)
2.  [Microsoft. (2024, January 9). Learn about data loss prevention. Retrieved March 4, 2024.](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/purview/dlp-learn-about-dlp)

3.  [Google. (n.d.). Use Workspace DLP to prevent data loss. Retrieved March 4, 2024.](https://support.google.com/a/answer/9646351)

Disable or Remove Feature or Program
====================================

Remove or deny access to unnecessary and potentially vulnerable software to prevent abuse by adversaries.

ID:M1042

Version:1.1

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:31 March 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1042/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1098](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/002)

[Account Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098):[Additional Email Delegate Permissions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/002)

If email delegation is not required, disable it. In Google Workspace this can be accomplished through the Google Admin console.[\[1\]](https://support.google.com/a/answer/7223765?hl=en)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/004)

[Account Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098):[SSH Authorized Keys](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/004)

Disable SSH if it is not necessary on a host or restrict SSH access for specific users/groups using`/etc/ssh/sshd_config`.

Enterprise

[T1595](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1595)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1595/003)

[Active Scanning](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1595):[Wordlist Scanning](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1595/003)

Remove or disable access to any systems, resources, and infrastructure that are not explicitly required to be available externally.

Enterprise

[T1557](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)

[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)

Disable legacy network protocols that may be used to intercept network traffic if applicable, especially those that are not needed within an environment.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/001)

[LLMNR/NBT-NS Poisoning and SMB Relay](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/001)

Disable LLMNR and NetBIOS in local computer security settings or by group policy if they are not needed within an environment.[\[2\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=3299)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/002)

[ARP Cache Poisoning](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/002)

Consider disabling updating the ARP cache on gratuitous ARP replies.

Enterprise

[T1547](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547)

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/007)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[Re-opened Applications](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/007)

This feature can be disabled entirely with the following terminal command:`defaults write -g ApplePersistence -bool no`.

Enterprise

[T1059](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

[Command and Scripting Interpreter](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

Disable or remove any unnecessary or unused shells or interpreters.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/001)

[PowerShell](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/001)

It may be possible to remove PowerShell from systems when not needed, but a review should be performed to assess the impact to an environment, since it could be in use for many legitimate purposes and administrative functions.

Disable/restrict the WinRM Service to help prevent uses of PowerShell for remote execution.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/005)

[Visual Basic](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/005)

Turn off or restrict access to unneeded VB components.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/007)

[JavaScript](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/007)

Turn off or restrict access to unneeded scripting components.

Enterprise

[T1092](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1092)

[Communication Through Removable Media](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1092)

Disable Autoruns if it is unnecessary.[\[3\]](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/kb/967715)

Enterprise

[T1609](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1609)

[Container Administration Command](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1609)

Remove unnecessary tools and software from containers.

Enterprise

[T1555](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555/004)

[Credentials from Password Stores](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555):[Windows Credential Manager](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555/004)

Consider enabling the "Network access: Do not allow storage of passwords and credentials for network authentication" setting that will prevent network credentials from being stored by the Credential Manager.[\[4\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/windows/it-pro/windows-server-2012-R2-and-2012/jj852185(v=ws.11)?redirectedfrom=MSDN)

Enterprise

[T1114](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114/003)

[Email Collection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114):[Email Forwarding Rule](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114/003)

Consider disabling external email forwarding.[\[5\]](https://www.microsoft.com/security/blog/2021/06/14/behind-the-scenes-of-business-email-compromise-using-cross-domain-threat-data-to-disrupt-a-large-bec-infrastructure/)

Enterprise

[T1611](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1611)

[Escape to Host](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1611)

Remove unnecessary tools and software from containers.

Enterprise

[T1546](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/002)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546):[Screensaver](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/002)

Use Group Policy to disable screensavers if they are unnecessary.[\[6\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/cc938799.aspx)

[.014](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/014)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546):[Emond](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/014)

Consider disabling emond by removing the[Launch Daemon](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/004)plist file.

Enterprise

[T1011](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1011)

[Exfiltration Over Other Network Medium](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1011)

Disable WiFi connection, modem, cellular data connection, Bluetooth, or another radio frequency (RF) channel in local computer security settings or by group policy if it is not needed within an environment.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1011/001)

[Exfiltration Over Bluetooth](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1011/001)

Disable Bluetooth in local computer security settings or by group policy if it is not needed within an environment.

Enterprise

[T1052](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1052)

[Exfiltration Over Physical Medium](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1052)

Disable Autorun if it is unnecessary.[\[3\]](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/kb/967715)Disallow or restrict removable media at an organizational policy level if they are not required for business operations.[\[7\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/cc772540(v=ws.10).aspx)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1052/001)

[Exfiltration over USB](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1052/001)

Disable Autorun if it is unnecessary.[\[3\]](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/kb/967715)Disallow or restrict removable media at an organizational policy level if they are not required for business operations.[\[7\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/cc772540(v=ws.10).aspx)

Enterprise

[T1210](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1210)

[Exploitation of Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1210)

Minimize available services to only those that are necessary.

Enterprise

[T1133](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1133)

[External Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1133)

Disable or block remotely available services that may be unnecessary.

Enterprise

[T1564](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/006)

[Hide Artifacts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564):[Run Virtual Instance](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/006)

Disable Hyper-V if not necessary within a given environment.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/007)

[Hide Artifacts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564):[VBA Stomping](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/007)

Turn off or restrict access to unneeded VB components.[\[8\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/office/troubleshoot/office-developer/turn-off-visual-basic-for-application)

Enterprise

[T1562](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562)

[.010](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/010)

[Impair Defenses](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562):[Downgrade Attack](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/010)

Consider removing previous versions of tools that are unnecessary to the environment when possible.

Enterprise

[T1559](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559)

[Inter-Process Communication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559)

Registry keys specific to Microsoft Office feature control security can be set to disable automatic DDE/OLE execution.[\[9\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/security/4053440)[\[10\]](https://www.bleepingcomputer.com/news/microsoft/microsoft-disables-dde-feature-in-word-to-prevent-further-malware-attacks/)[\[11\]](https://gist.github.com/wdormann/732bb88d9b5dd5a66c9f1e1498f31a1b)Microsoft also created, and enabled by default, Registry keys to completely disable DDE execution in Word and Excel.[\[12\]](https://portal.msrc.microsoft.com/security-guidance/advisory/ADV170021)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559/002)

[Dynamic Data Exchange](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559/002)

Registry keys specific to Microsoft Office feature control security can be set to disable automatic DDE/OLE execution.[\[9\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/security/4053440)[\[10\]](https://www.bleepingcomputer.com/news/microsoft/microsoft-disables-dde-feature-in-word-to-prevent-further-malware-attacks/)[\[11\]](https://gist.github.com/wdormann/732bb88d9b5dd5a66c9f1e1498f31a1b)Microsoft also created, and enabled by default, Registry keys to completely disable DDE execution in Word and Excel.[\[12\]](https://portal.msrc.microsoft.com/security-guidance/advisory/ADV170021)

Enterprise

[T1046](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1046)

[Network Service Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1046)

Ensure that unnecessary ports and services are closed to prevent risk of discovery and potential exploitation.

Enterprise

[T1137](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137)

[Office Application Startup](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137)

Follow Office macro security best practices suitable for your environment. Disable Office VBA macros from executing.

Disable Office add-ins. If they are required, follow best practices for securing them by requiring them to be signed and disabling user notification for allowing add-ins. For some add-ins types (WLL, VBA) additional mitigation is likely required as disabling add-ins in the Office Trust Center does not disable WLL nor does it prevent VBA code from executing.[\[13\]](https://labs.mwrinfosecurity.com/blog/add-in-opportunities-for-office-persistence/)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137/001)

[Office Template Macros](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137/001)

Follow Office macro security best practices suitable for your environment. Disable Office VBA macros from executing.

Disable Office add-ins. If they are required, follow best practices for securing them by requiring them to be signed and disabling user notification for allowing add-ins. For some add-ins types (WLL, VBA) additional mitigation is likely required as disabling add-ins in the Office Trust Center does not disable WLL nor does it prevent VBA code from executing.[\[13\]](https://labs.mwrinfosecurity.com/blog/add-in-opportunities-for-office-persistence/)

Enterprise

[T1219](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1219)

[Remote Access Software](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1219)

Consider disabling unnecessary remote connection functionality, including both unapproved software installations and specific features built into supported applications.

Enterprise

[T1563](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563)

[Remote Service Session Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563)

Disable the remote service (ex: SSH, RDP, etc.) if it is unnecessary.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/001)

[SSH Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/001)

Ensure that agent forwarding is disabled on systems that do not explicitly require this feature to prevent misuse.[\[14\]](https://www.symantec.com/connect/articles/ssh-and-ssh-agent)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/002)

[RDP Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/002)

Disable the RDP service if it is unnecessary.

Enterprise

[T1021](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021)

If remote services, such as the ability to make direct connections to cloud virtual machines, are not required, disable these connection types where feasible.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/001)

[Remote Desktop Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/001)

Disable the RDP service if it is unnecessary.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/003)

[Distributed Component Object Model](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/003)

Consider disabling DCOM through Dcomcnfg.exe.[\[15\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/cc771387.aspx)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/004)

[SSH](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/004)

Disable the SSH daemon on systems that do not require it. For macOS ensure Remote Login is disabled under Sharing Preferences.[\[16\]](https://sarah-edwards-xzkc.squarespace.com/blog/2020/4/30/analysis-of-apple-unified-logs-quarantine-edition-entry-6-working-from-home-remote-logins)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/005)

[VNC](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/005)

Uninstall any VNC server software where not required.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/006)

[Windows Remote Management](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/006)

Disable the WinRM service.

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/008)

[Direct Cloud VM Connections](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/008)

If direct virtual machine connections are not required for administrative use, disable these connection types where feasible.

Enterprise

[T1091](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1091)

[Replication Through Removable Media](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1091)

Disable Autorun if it is unnecessary.[\[3\]](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/kb/967715)Disallow or restrict removable media at an organizational policy level if it is not required for business operations.[\[7\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/cc772540(v=ws.10).aspx)

Enterprise

[T1505](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505)

[Server Software Component](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505)

Consider disabling software components from servers when possible to prevent abuse by adversaries.[\[17\]](https://itsyndicate.org/blog/disabling-dangerous-php-functions/)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505/003)

[Web Shell](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505/003)

Consider disabling functions from web technologies such as PHPs`evaI()`that may be abused for web shells.[\[17\]](https://itsyndicate.org/blog/disabling-dangerous-php-functions/)

Enterprise

[T1649](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1649)

[Steal or Forge Authentication Certificates](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1649)

Consider disabling old/dangerous authentication protocols (e.g. NTLM), as well as unnecessary certificate features, such as potentially vulnerable AD CS web and other enrollment server roles.[\[18\]](https://web.archive.org/web/20220818094600/https:/specterops.io/assets/resources/Certified_Pre-Owned.pdf)

Enterprise

[T1553](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/005)

[Subvert Trust Controls](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553):[Mark-of-the-Web Bypass](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/005)

Consider disabling auto-mounting of disk image files (i.e., .iso, .img, .vhd, and .vhdx). This can be achieved by modifying the Registry values related to the Windows Explorer file associations in order to disable the automatic Explorer "Mount and Burn" dialog for these file extensions. Note: this will not deactivate the mount functionality itself.[\[19\]](https://gist.github.com/wdormann/fca29e0dcda8b5c0472e73e10c78c3e7)

Enterprise

[T1218](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218)

[System Binary Proxy Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218)

Many native binaries may not be necessary within a given environment.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/003)

[CMSTP](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/003)

CMSTP.exe may not be necessary within a given environment (unless using it for VPN connection installation).

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/004)

[InstallUtil](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/004)

InstallUtil may not be necessary within a given environment.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/005)

[Mshta](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/005)

Mshta.exe may not be necessary within a given environment since its functionality is tied to older versions of Internet Explorer that have reached end of life.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/007)

[Msiexec](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/007)

Consider disabling the`AlwaysInstallElevated`policy to prevent elevated execution of Windows Installer packages.[\[20\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/msi/alwaysinstallelevated)

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/008)

[Odbcconf](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/008)

Odbcconf.exe may not be necessary within a given environment.

[.009](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/009)

[Regsvcs/Regasm](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/009)

Regsvcs and Regasm may not be necessary within a given environment.

[.012](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/012)

[Verclsid](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/012)

Consider removing verclsid.exe if it is not necessary within a given environment.

[.013](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/013)

[Mavinject](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/013)

Consider removing mavinject.exe if Microsoft App-V is not used within a given environment.

[.014](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/014)

[MMC](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/014)

MMC may not be necessary within a given environment since it is primarily used by system administrators, not regular users or clients.

[.015](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/015)

[Electron Applications](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/015)

Remove or deny access to unnecessary and potentially vulnerable software and features to prevent abuse by adversaries. Many native binaries may not be necessary within a given environment: for example, consider disabling the Node.js integration in all renderers that display remote content to protect users by limiting adversaries power to plant malicious JavaScript within Electron applications.[\[21\]](https://stackoverflow.com/questions/48854265/why-do-i-see-an-electron-security-warning-after-updating-my-electron-project-t)

Enterprise

[T1221](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1221)

[Template Injection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1221)

Consider disabling Microsoft Office macros/active content to prevent the execution of malicious payloads in documents[\[22\]](https://support.office.com/article/enable-or-disable-macros-in-office-files-12b036fd-d140-4e74-b45e-16fed1a7e5c6), though this setting may not mitigate the[Forced Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1187)use for this technique.

Enterprise

[T1205](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1205)

[Traffic Signaling](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1205)

Disable Wake-on-LAN if it is not needed within an environment.

Enterprise

[T1127](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1127)

[Trusted Developer Utilities Proxy Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1127)

Specific developer utilities may not be necessary within a given environment and should be removed if not used.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1127/001)

[MSBuild](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1127/001)

MSBuild.exe may not be necessary within an environment and should be removed if not being used.

Enterprise

[T1552](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/005)

[Unsecured Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552):[Cloud Instance Metadata API](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/005)

Disable unnecessary metadata services and restrict or disable insecure versions of metadata services that are in use to prevent adversary access.[\[23\]](https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/security/defense-in-depth-open-firewalls-reverse-proxies-ssrf-vulnerabilities-ec2-instance-metadata-service/)

Do Not Mitigate
===============

This category is to associate techniques that mitigation might increase risk of compromise and therefore mitigation is not recommended.

ID:M1055

Version:1.0

Created:19 July 2019

Last Modified:23 July 2019

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1055/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1480](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1480)

[Execution Guardrails](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1480)

[Execution Guardrails](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1480)likely should not be mitigated with preventative controls because it may protect unintended targets from being compromised. If targeted, efforts should be focused on preventing adversary tools from running earlier in the chain of activity and on identifying subsequent malicious behavior if compromised.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1480/001)

[Environmental Keying](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1480/001)

[Environmental Keying](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1480/001)likely should not be mitigated with preventative controls because it may protect unintended targets from being compromised via confusion of keys by the adversary. Mitigation of this technique is also unlikely to be feasible within most contexts because there are no standard attributes from which an adversary may derive keys. If targeted, efforts should be focused on preventing adversary tools from running earlier in the chain of activity and on identifying subsequent malicious behavior if compromised.

Encrypt Sensitive Information
=============================

Protect sensitive information with strong encryption.

ID:M1041

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:11 June 2019

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1041/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1557](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)

[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)

Ensure that all wired and/or wireless traffic is encrypted appropriately. Use best practices for authentication protocols, such as Kerberos, and ensure web traffic that may contain credentials is protected by SSL/TLS.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/002)

[ARP Cache Poisoning](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/002)

Ensure that all wired and/or wireless traffic is encrypted appropriately. Use best practices for authentication protocols, such as Kerberos, and ensure web traffic that may contain credentials is protected by SSL/TLS.

Enterprise

[T1119](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1119)

[Automated Collection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1119)

Encryption and off-system storage of sensitive information may be one way to mitigate collection of files, but may not stop an adversary from acquiring the information if an intrusion persists over a long period of time and the adversary is able to discover and access the data through other means. Strong passwords should be used on certain encrypted documents that use them to prevent offline cracking through[Brute Force](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110)techniques.

Enterprise

[T1020](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1020)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1020/001)

[Automated Exfiltration](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1020):[Traffic Duplication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1020/001)

Ensure that all wired and/or wireless traffic is encrypted appropriately. Use best practices for authentication protocols, such as Kerberos, and ensure web traffic that may contain credentials is protected by SSL/TLS.

Enterprise

[T1659](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1659)

[Content Injection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1659)

Where possible, ensure that online traffic is appropriately encrypted through services such as trusted VPNs.

Enterprise

[T1530](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1530)

[Data from Cloud Storage](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1530)

Encrypt data stored at rest in cloud storage.[\[1\]](https://aws.amazon.com/premiumsupport/knowledge-center/secure-s3-resources/)[\[2\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/storage/common/storage-security-guide)Managed encryption keys can be rotated by most providers. At a minimum, ensure an incident response plan to storage breach includes rotating the keys and test for impact on client applications.[\[3\]](https://cloud.google.com/kms/docs/key-rotation)

Enterprise

[T1602](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602)

[Data from Configuration Repository](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602)

Configure SNMPv3 to use the highest level of security (authPriv) available.[\[4\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/TA17-156A)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/001)

[SNMP (MIB Dump)](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/001)

Configure SNMPv3 to use the highest level of security (authPriv) available.[\[4\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/TA17-156A)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/002)

[Network Device Configuration Dump](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/002)

Configure SNMPv3 to use the highest level of security (authPriv) available.[\[4\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/TA17-156A)

Enterprise

[T1565](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565)

[Data Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565)

Consider encrypting important information to reduce an adversarys ability to perform tailored data modifications.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565/001)

[Stored Data Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565/001)

Consider encrypting important information to reduce an adversarys ability to perform tailored data modifications.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565/002)

[Transmitted Data Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565/002)

Encrypt all important data flows to reduce the impact of tailored modifications on data in transit.

Enterprise

[T1114](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114)

[Email Collection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114)

Use of encryption provides an added layer of security to sensitive information sent over email. Encryption using public key cryptography requires the adversary to obtain the private certificate along with an encryption key to decrypt messages.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114/001)

[Local Email Collection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114/001)

Use of encryption provides an added layer of security to sensitive information sent over email. Encryption using public key cryptography requires the adversary to obtain the private certificate along with an encryption key to decrypt messages.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114/002)

[Remote Email Collection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114/002)

Use of encryption provides an added layer of security to sensitive information sent over email. Encryption using public key cryptography requires the adversary to obtain the private certificate along with an encryption key to decrypt messages.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114/003)

[Email Forwarding Rule](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114/003)

Use of encryption provides an added layer of security to sensitive information sent over email. Encryption using public key cryptography requires the adversary to obtain the private certificate along with an encryption key to decrypt messages.

Enterprise

[T1070](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070)

[Indicator Removal](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070)

Obfuscate/encrypt event files locally and in transit to avoid giving feedback to an adversary.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/001)

[Clear Windows Event Logs](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/001)

Obfuscate/encrypt event files locally and in transit to avoid giving feedback to an adversary.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/002)

[Clear Linux or Mac System Logs](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/002)

Obfuscate/encrypt event files locally and in transit to avoid giving feedback to an adversary.

Enterprise

[T1040](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1040)

[Network Sniffing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1040)

Ensure that all wired and/or wireless traffic is encrypted appropriately. Use best practices for authentication protocols, such as Kerberos, and ensure web traffic that may contain credentials is protected by SSL/TLS.

Enterprise

[T1003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

[OS Credential Dumping](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

Ensure Domain Controller backups are properly secured.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/003)

[NTDS](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/003)

Ensure Domain Controller backups are properly secured.[\[5\]](http://adsecurity.org/?p=1275)

Enterprise

[T1649](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1649)

[Steal or Forge Authentication Certificates](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1649)

Ensure certificates as well as associated private keys are appropriately secured. Consider utilizing additional hardware credential protections such as trusted platform modules (TPM) or hardware security modules (HSM). Enforce HTTPS and enable Extended Protection forAuthentication.[\[6\]](https://web.archive.org/web/20220818094600/https:/specterops.io/assets/resources/Certified_Pre-Owned.pdf)

Enterprise

[T1558](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558)

[Steal or Forge Kerberos Tickets](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558)

Enable AES Kerberos encryption (or another stronger encryption algorithm), rather than RC4, where possible.[\[7\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2293)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/002)

[Silver Ticket](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/002)

Enable AES Kerberos encryption (or another stronger encryption algorithm), rather than RC4, where possible.[\[7\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2293)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/003)

[Kerberoasting](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/003)

Enable AES Kerberos encryption (or another stronger encryption algorithm), rather than RC4, where possible.[\[7\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2293)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/004)

[AS-REP Roasting](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/004)

Enable AES Kerberos encryption (or another stronger encryption algorithm), rather than RC4, where possible.[\[7\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2293)

Enterprise

[T1552](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

[Unsecured Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

When possible, store keys on separate cryptographic hardware instead of on the local system.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/004)

[Private Keys](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/004)

When possible, store keys on separate cryptographic hardware instead of on the local system. For example, on Windows systems use a TPM to secure keys and other sensitive credential material.[\[8\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/active-directory/devices/concept-primary-refresh-token)

Enterprise

[T1550](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/001)

[Use Alternate Authentication Material](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550):[Application Access Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/001)

File encryption should be enforced across email communications containing sensitive information that may be obtained through access to email services.

Execution Prevention
====================

Block execution of code on a system through application control, and/or script blocking.

ID:M1038

Version:1.2

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:28 February 2022

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1038/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1548](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

[Abuse Elevation Control Mechanism](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

System settings can prevent applications from running that haven't been downloaded from legitimate repositories which may help mitigate some of these issues. Not allowing unsigned applications from being run may also mitigate some risk.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/004)

[Elevated Execution with Prompt](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/004)

System settings can prevent applications from running that haven't been downloaded through the Apple Store which may help mitigate some of these issues. Not allowing unsigned applications from being run may also mitigate some risk.

Enterprise

[T1547](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/004)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[Winlogon Helper DLL](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/004)

Identify and block potentially malicious software that may be executed through the Winlogon helper process by using application control[\[1\]](http://www.sans.org/reading-room/whitepapers/application/application-whitelisting-panacea-propaganda-33599)tools like AppLocker[\[2\]](https://blogs.jpcert.or.jp/en/2016/01/windows-commands-abused-by-attackers.html)[\[3\]](https://apps.nsa.gov/iaarchive/library/ia-guidance/tech-briefs/application-whitelisting-using-microsoft-applocker.cfm)that are capable of auditing and/or blocking unknown DLLs.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/006)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[Kernel Modules and Extensions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/006)

Application control and software restriction tools, such as SELinux, KSPP, grsecurity MODHARDEN, and Linux kernel tuning can aid in restricting kernel module loading.[\[4\]](https://patchwork.kernel.org/patch/8754821/)[\[5\]](https://en.wikibooks.org/wiki/Grsecurity/The_RBAC_System)[\[6\]](https://www.kernel.org/doc/html/latest/security/self-protection.html)[\[7\]](https://linux-audit.com/increase-kernel-integrity-with-disabled-linux-kernel-modules-loading/)[\[8\]](https://xorl.wordpress.com/2018/02/17/lkm-loading-kernel-restrictions/)

Enterprise

[T1176](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1176)

[Browser Extensions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1176)

Set a browser extension allow or deny list as appropriate for your security policy.[\[9\]](http://www.technospot.net/blogs/block-chrome-extensions-using-google-chrome-group-policy-settings/)

Enterprise

[T1059](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

[Command and Scripting Interpreter](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

Use application control where appropriate. For example, PowerShell Constrained Language mode can be used to restrict access to sensitive or otherwise dangerous language elements such as those used to execute arbitrary Windows APIs or files (e.g.,`Add-Type`).[\[10\]](https://devblogs.microsoft.com/powershell/powershell-constrained-language-mode/)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/001)

[PowerShell](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/001)

Use application control where appropriate. PowerShell Constrained Language mode can be used to restrict access to sensitive or otherwise dangerous language elements such as those used to execute arbitrary Windows APIs or files (e.g.,`Add-Type`).[\[10\]](https://devblogs.microsoft.com/powershell/powershell-constrained-language-mode/)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/002)

[AppleScript](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/002)

Use application control where appropriate.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/003)

[Windows Command Shell](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/003)

Use application control where appropriate.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/004)

[Unix Shell](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/004)

Use application control where appropriate.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/005)

[Visual Basic](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/005)

Use application control where appropriate. VBA macros obtained from the Internet, based on the file's Mark of the Web (MOTW) attribute, may be blocked from executing in Office applications (ex: Access, Excel, PowerPoint, Visio, and Word) by default starting in Windows Version 2203.[\[11\]](https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-365-blog/helping-users-stay-safe-blocking-internet-macros-by-default-in/ba-p/3071805)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/006)

[Python](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/006)

Denylist Python where not required.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/007)

[JavaScript](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/007)

Denylist scripting where appropriate.

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/008)

[Network Device CLI](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/008)

TACACS+ can keep control over which commands administrators are permitted to use through the configuration of authentication and command authorization.[\[12\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#39)

[.009](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/009)

[Cloud API](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/009)

Use application control where appropriate to block use of PowerShell CmdLets or other host based resources to access cloud API resources.

[.010](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/010)

[AutoHotKey & AutoIT](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/010)

Use application control to prevent execution of`AutoIt3.exe`,`AutoHotkey.exe`, and other related features that may not be required for a given system or network to prevent potential misuse by adversaries.

Enterprise

[T1609](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1609)

[Container Administration Command](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1609)

Use read-only containers, read-only file systems, and minimal images when possible to prevent the execution of commands.[\[13\]](https://media.defense.gov/2022/Aug/29/2003066362/-1/-1/0/CTR_KUBERNETES_HARDENING_GUIDANCE_1.2_20220829.PDF)Where possible, also consider using application control and software restriction tools (such as those provided by SELinux) to restrict access to files, processes, and system calls in containers.[\[14\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/tasks/configure-pod-container/security-context/)

Enterprise

Use read-only containers, read-only file systems, and minimal images when possible to prevent the running of commands.[\[13\]](https://media.defense.gov/2022/Aug/29/2003066362/-1/-1/0/CTR_KUBERNETES_HARDENING_GUIDANCE_1.2_20220829.PDF)Where possible, also consider using application control and software restriction tools (such as those provided by SELinux) to restrict access to files, processes, and system calls in containers.[\[14\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/tasks/configure-pod-container/security-context/)

Enterprise

[T1546](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546)

Block .scr files from being executed from non-standard locations.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/006)

Allow applications via known hashes.

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/008)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546):[Accessibility Features](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/008)

Adversaries can replace accessibility features binaries with alternate binaries to execute this technique. Identify and block potentially malicious software executed through accessibility features functionality by using application control[\[1\]](http://www.sans.org/reading-room/whitepapers/application/application-whitelisting-panacea-propaganda-33599)tools, like Windows Defender Application Control[\[15\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/threat-protection/windows-defender-application-control/windows-defender-application-control), AppLocker,[\[2\]](https://blogs.jpcert.or.jp/en/2016/01/windows-commands-abused-by-attackers.html)[\[3\]](https://apps.nsa.gov/iaarchive/library/ia-guidance/tech-briefs/application-whitelisting-using-microsoft-applocker.cfm)or Software Restriction Policies[\[16\]](http://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/magazine/2008.06.srp.aspx)where appropriate.[\[17\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/ee791851.aspx)

[.009](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/009)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546):[AppCert DLLs](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/009)

Adversaries install new AppCertDLL binaries to execute this technique. Identify and block potentially malicious software executed through AppCertDLLs functionality by using application control[\[1\]](http://www.sans.org/reading-room/whitepapers/application/application-whitelisting-panacea-propaganda-33599)tools, like Windows Defender Application Control[\[15\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/threat-protection/windows-defender-application-control/windows-defender-application-control), AppLocker,[\[2\]](https://blogs.jpcert.or.jp/en/2016/01/windows-commands-abused-by-attackers.html)[\[3\]](https://apps.nsa.gov/iaarchive/library/ia-guidance/tech-briefs/application-whitelisting-using-microsoft-applocker.cfm)or Software Restriction Policies[\[16\]](http://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/magazine/2008.06.srp.aspx)where appropriate.[\[17\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/ee791851.aspx)

[.010](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/010)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546):[AppInit DLLs](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/010)

Adversaries can install new AppInit DLLs binaries to execute this technique. Identify and block potentially malicious software executed through AppInit DLLs functionality by using application control[\[1\]](http://www.sans.org/reading-room/whitepapers/application/application-whitelisting-panacea-propaganda-33599)tools, like Windows Defender Application Control[\[15\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/threat-protection/windows-defender-application-control/windows-defender-application-control), AppLocker,[\[2\]](https://blogs.jpcert.or.jp/en/2016/01/windows-commands-abused-by-attackers.html)[\[3\]](https://apps.nsa.gov/iaarchive/library/ia-guidance/tech-briefs/application-whitelisting-using-microsoft-applocker.cfm)or Software Restriction Policies[\[16\]](http://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/magazine/2008.06.srp.aspx)where appropriate.[\[17\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/ee791851.aspx)

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/007)

[Path Interception by PATH Environment Variable](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/007)

Adversaries will likely need to place new binaries in locations to be executed through this weakness. Identify and block potentially malicious software executed path interception by using application control tools, like Windows Defender Application Control, AppLocker, or Software Restriction Policies where appropriate.[\[19\]](https://www.sans.org/reading-room/whitepapers/application/application-whitelisting-panacea-propaganda-33599)[\[15\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/threat-protection/windows-defender-application-control/windows-defender-application-control)[\[2\]](https://blogs.jpcert.or.jp/en/2016/01/windows-commands-abused-by-attackers.html)[\[3\]](https://apps.nsa.gov/iaarchive/library/ia-guidance/tech-briefs/application-whitelisting-using-microsoft-applocker.cfm)[\[20\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/technet-magazine/cc510322(v=msdn.10)?redirectedfrom=MSDN)[\[21\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/windows/it-pro/windows-server-2012-R2-and-2012/ee791851(v=ws.11)?redirectedfrom=MSDN)

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/008)

[Path Interception by Search Order Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/008)

Adversaries will likely need to place new binaries in locations to be executed through this weakness. Identify and block potentially malicious software executed path interception by using application control tools, like Windows Defender Application Control, AppLocker, or Software Restriction Policies where appropriate.[\[19\]](https://www.sans.org/reading-room/whitepapers/application/application-whitelisting-panacea-propaganda-33599)[\[15\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/threat-protection/windows-defender-application-control/windows-defender-application-control)[\[2\]](https://blogs.jpcert.or.jp/en/2016/01/windows-commands-abused-by-attackers.html)[\[3\]](https://apps.nsa.gov/iaarchive/library/ia-guidance/tech-briefs/application-whitelisting-using-microsoft-applocker.cfm)[\[20\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/technet-magazine/cc510322(v=msdn.10)?redirectedfrom=MSDN)[\[21\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/windows/it-pro/windows-server-2012-R2-and-2012/ee791851(v=ws.11)?redirectedfrom=MSDN)

[T1562](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562)

[Impair Defenses](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562)

Use application control where appropriate, especially regarding the execution of tools outside of the organization's security policies (such as rootkit removal tools) that have been abused to impair system defenses. Ensure that only approved security applications are used and running on enterprise systems.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/001)

[Disable or Modify Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/001)

Use application control where appropriate, especially regarding the execution of tools outside of the organization's security policies (such as rootkit removal tools) that have been abused to impair system defenses. Ensure that only approved security applications are used and running on enterprise systems.

[Match Legitimate Name or Location](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036/005)

Use tools that restrict program execution via application control by attributes other than file name for common operating system utilities that are needed.

[Masquerade File Type](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036/008)

Ensure that input sanitization is performed and that files are validated properly before execution; furthermore, implement a strict allow list to ensure that only authorized file types are processed.[\[22\]](https://blog.yeswehack.com/yeswerhackers/file-upload-attacks-part-2/)Restrict and/or block execution of files where headers and extensions do not match.

Enterprise

[T1553](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553)

[Subvert Trust Controls](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553)

System settings can prevent applications from running that haven't been downloaded through the Apple Store (or other legitimate repositories) which can help mitigate some of these issues. Also enable application control solutions such as AppLocker and/or Device Guard to block the loading of malicious content.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/001)

[Gatekeeper Bypass](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/001)

System settings can prevent applications from running that haven't been downloaded through the Apple Store which can help mitigate some of these issues.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/003)

[SIP and Trust Provider Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/003)

Enable application control solutions such as AppLocker and/or Device Guard to block the loading of malicious SIP DLLs.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/005)

[Mark-of-the-Web Bypass](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/005)

Consider blocking container file types at web and/or email gateways. Consider unregistering container file extensions in Windows File Explorer.[\[24\]](https://insights.sei.cmu.edu/cert/2019/09/the-dangers-of-vhd-and-vhdx-files.html)

[T1218](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218)

[System Binary Proxy Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218)

Consider using application control to prevent execution of binaries that are susceptible to abuse and not required for a given system or network.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/001)

[Compiled HTML File](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/001)

Consider using application control to prevent execution of hh.exe if it is not required for a given system or network to prevent potential misuse by adversaries.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/002)

[Control Panel](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/002)

Identify and block potentially malicious and unknown .cpl files by using application control[\[1\]](http://www.sans.org/reading-room/whitepapers/application/application-whitelisting-panacea-propaganda-33599)tools, like Windows Defender Application Control[\[15\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/threat-protection/windows-defender-application-control/windows-defender-application-control), AppLocker,[\[2\]](https://blogs.jpcert.or.jp/en/2016/01/windows-commands-abused-by-attackers.html)[\[3\]](https://apps.nsa.gov/iaarchive/library/ia-guidance/tech-briefs/application-whitelisting-using-microsoft-applocker.cfm)or Software Restriction Policies[\[16\]](http://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/magazine/2008.06.srp.aspx)where appropriate.[\[17\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/ee791851.aspx)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/003)

[CMSTP](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/003)

Consider using application control configured to block execution of CMSTP.exe if it is not required for a given system or network to prevent potential misuse by adversaries.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/004)

[InstallUtil](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/004)

Use application control configured to block execution of InstallUtil.exe if it is not required for a given system or network to prevent potential misuse by adversaries.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/005)

[Mshta](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/005)

Use application control configured to block execution of`mshta.exe`if it is not required for a given system or network to prevent potential misuse by adversaries. For example, in Windows 10 and Windows Server 2016 and above, Windows Defender Application Control (WDAC) policy rules may be applied to block the`mshta.exe`application and to prevent abuse.[\[25\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/security/threat-protection/windows-defender-application-control/microsoft-recommended-block-rules)

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/008)

[Odbcconf](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/008)

Use application control configured to block execution of Odbcconf.exe if it is not required for a given system or network to prevent potential misuse by adversaries.

[.009](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/009)

[Regsvcs/Regasm](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/009)

Block execution of Regsvcs.exe and Regasm.exe if they are not required for a given system or network to prevent potential misuse by adversaries.

[.012](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/012)

[Verclsid](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/012)

Use application control configured to block execution of verclsid.exe if it is not required for a given system or network to prevent potential misuse by adversaries.

[.013](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/013)

[Mavinject](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/013)

Use application control configured to block execution of mavinject.exe if it is not required for a given system or network to prevent potential misuse by adversaries.

[.014](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/014)

[MMC](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/014)

Use application control configured to block execution of MMC if it is not required for a given system or network to prevent potential misuse by adversaries.

[.015](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/015)

[Electron Applications](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/015)

Where possible, enforce binary and application integrity with digital signature verification to prevent untrusted code from executing. For example, do not use`shell.openExternal`with untrusted content.

Where possible, set`nodeIntegration`to false, which disables access to the Node.js function.[\[26\]](https://medium.com/certik/vulnerability-in-electron-based-application-unintentionally-giving-malicious-code-room-to-run-e2e1447d01b8)By disabling access to the Node.js function, this may limit the ability to execute malicious commands by injecting JavaScript code.

Do not disable`webSecurity`, which may allow for users of the application to invoke malicious content from online sources.

Exploit Protection
==================

Use capabilities to detect and block conditions that may lead to or be indicative of a software exploit occurring.

ID:M1050

Version:1.1

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:20 June 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1050/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1189](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1189)

[Drive-by Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1189)

Security applications that look for behavior used during exploitation such as Windows Defender Exploit Guard (WDEG) and the Enhanced Mitigation Experience Toolkit (EMET) can be used to mitigate some exploitation behavior.[\[1\]](https://blogs.technet.microsoft.com/srd/2017/08/09/moving-beyond-emet-ii-windows-defender-exploit-guard/)Control flow integrity checking is another way to potentially identify and stop a software exploit from occurring.[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control-flow_integrity)Many of these protections depend on the architecture and target application binary for compatibility.

Enterprise

[T1190](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1190)

[Exploit Public-Facing Application](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1190)

Web Application Firewalls may be used to limit exposure of applications to prevent exploit traffic from reaching the application.

Enterprise

[T1203](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1203)

[Exploitation for Client Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1203)

Security applications that look for behavior used during exploitation such as Windows Defender Exploit Guard (WDEG) and the Enhanced Mitigation Experience Toolkit (EMET) can be used to mitigate some exploitation behavior.[\[1\]](https://blogs.technet.microsoft.com/srd/2017/08/09/moving-beyond-emet-ii-windows-defender-exploit-guard/)Control flow integrity checking is another way to potentially identify and stop a software exploit from occurring.[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control-flow_integrity)Many of these protections depend on the architecture and target application binary for compatibility.

Enterprise

[T1212](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1212)

[Exploitation for Credential Access](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1212)

Security applications that look for behavior used during exploitation such as Windows Defender Exploit Guard (WDEG) and the Enhanced Mitigation Experience Toolkit (EMET) can be used to mitigate some exploitation behavior.[\[1\]](https://blogs.technet.microsoft.com/srd/2017/08/09/moving-beyond-emet-ii-windows-defender-exploit-guard/)Control flow integrity checking is another way to potentially identify and stop a software exploit from occurring.[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control-flow_integrity)Many of these protections depend on the architecture and target application binary for compatibility and may not work for software targeted for defense evasion.

Enterprise

[T1211](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1211)

[Exploitation for Defense Evasion](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1211)

Security applications that look for behavior used during exploitation such as Windows Defender Exploit Guard (WDEG) and the Enhanced Mitigation Experience Toolkit (EMET) can be used to mitigate some exploitation behavior.[\[1\]](https://blogs.technet.microsoft.com/srd/2017/08/09/moving-beyond-emet-ii-windows-defender-exploit-guard/)Control flow integrity checking is another way to potentially identify and stop a software exploit from occurring.[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control-flow_integrity)Many of these protections depend on the architecture and target application binary for compatibility and may not work for software targeted for defense evasion.

Enterprise

[T1068](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1068)

[Exploitation for Privilege Escalation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1068)

Security applications that look for behavior used during exploitation such as Windows Defender Exploit Guard (WDEG) and the Enhanced Mitigation Experience Toolkit (EMET) can be used to mitigate some exploitation behavior.[\[1\]](https://blogs.technet.microsoft.com/srd/2017/08/09/moving-beyond-emet-ii-windows-defender-exploit-guard/)Control flow integrity checking is another way to potentially identify and stop a software exploit from occurring.[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control-flow_integrity)Many of these protections depend on the architecture and target application binary for compatibility and may not work for software components targeted for privilege escalation.

Enterprise

[T1210](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1210)

[Exploitation of Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1210)

Security applications that look for behavior used during exploitation such as Windows Defender Exploit Guard (WDEG) and the Enhanced Mitigation Experience Toolkit (EMET) can be used to mitigate some exploitation behavior.[\[1\]](https://blogs.technet.microsoft.com/srd/2017/08/09/moving-beyond-emet-ii-windows-defender-exploit-guard/)Control flow integrity checking is another way to potentially identify and stop a software exploit from occurring.[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control-flow_integrity)Many of these protections depend on the architecture and target application binary for compatibility and may not work for all software or services targeted.

Enterprise

[T1218](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218)

[System Binary Proxy Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218)

Microsoft's Enhanced Mitigation Experience Toolkit (EMET) Attack Surface Reduction (ASR) feature can be used to block methods of using using trusted binaries to bypass application control.

[.010](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/010)

[Regsvr32](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/010)

Microsoft's Enhanced Mitigation Experience Toolkit (EMET) Attack Surface Reduction (ASR) feature can be used to block regsvr32.exe from being used to bypass application control.[\[3\]](https://github.com/iadgov/Secure-Host-Baseline/tree/master/EMET)Identify and block potentially malicious software executed through regsvr32 functionality by using application control[\[4\]](http://www.sans.org/reading-room/whitepapers/application/application-whitelisting-panacea-propaganda-33599)tools, like Windows Defender Application Control[\[5\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/threat-protection/windows-defender-application-control/windows-defender-application-control), AppLocker,[\[6\]](https://blogs.jpcert.or.jp/en/2016/01/windows-commands-abused-by-attackers.html)[\[7\]](https://apps.nsa.gov/iaarchive/library/ia-guidance/tech-briefs/application-whitelisting-using-microsoft-applocker.cfm)or Software Restriction Policies[\[8\]](http://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/magazine/2008.06.srp.aspx)where appropriate.[\[9\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/ee791851.aspx)

[.011](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/011)

[Rundll32](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/011)

Microsoft's Enhanced Mitigation Experience Toolkit (EMET) Attack Surface Reduction (ASR) feature can be used to block methods of using rundll32.exe to bypass application control.

[.015](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/015)

[Electron Applications](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/015)

Microsoft's Enhanced Mitigation Experience Toolkit (EMET) Attack Surface Reduction (ASR) feature can be used to block methods of using trusted binaries to bypass application control. Ensure that Electron is updated to the latest version and critical vulnerabilities (such as nodeIntegration bypasses) are patched and cannot be exploited.

Enterprise

[T1080](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1080)

[Taint Shared Content](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1080)

Use utilities that detect or mitigate common features used in exploitation, such as the Microsoft Enhanced Mitigation Experience Toolkit (EMET).
