Filter Network Traffic
======================

Use network appliances to filter ingress or egress traffic and perform protocol-based filtering. Configure software on endpoints to filter network traffic.

ID:M1037

Version:1.1

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:20 June 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1037/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1557](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)

[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)

Use network appliances and host-based security software to block network traffic that is not necessary within the environment, such as legacy protocols that may be leveraged for AiTM conditions.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/001)

[LLMNR/NBT-NS Poisoning and SMB Relay](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/001)

Use host-based security software to block LLMNR/NetBIOS traffic. Enabling SMB Signing can stop NTLMv2 relay attacks.[\[1\]](https://byt3bl33d3r.github.io/practical-guide-to-ntlm-relaying-in-2017-aka-getting-a-foothold-in-under-5-minutes.html)[\[2\]](https://blog.secureideas.com/2018/04/ever-run-a-relay-why-smb-relays-should-be-on-your-mind.html)[\[3\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/system-center/operations-manager-2005/cc180803(v=technet.10))

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/002)

[ARP Cache Poisoning](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/002)

Consider enabling DHCP Snooping and Dynamic ARP Inspection on switches to create mappings between IP addresses requested via DHCP and ARP tables and tie the values to a port on the switch that may block bogus traffic.[\[4\]](https://www.cisco.com/c/en/us/products/collateral/switches/catalyst-6500-series-switches/white_paper_c11_603839.html)[\[5\]](https://www.juniper.net/documentation/en_US/junos/topics/task/configuration/understanding-and-using-dai.html)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/003)

[DHCP Spoofing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/003)

Consider filtering DHCP traffic on ports 67 and 68 to/from unknown or untrusted DHCP servers. Additionally, port security may also be enabled on layer switches. Furthermore, consider enabling DHCP snooping on layer 2 switches as it will prevent DHCP spoofing attacks and starvation attacks. Consider tracking available IP addresses through a script or a tool.

Additionally, block DHCPv6 traffic and incoming router advertisements, especially if IPv6 is not commonly used in the network.[\[6\]](https://dirkjanm.io/worst-of-both-worlds-ntlm-relaying-and-kerberos-delegation/)

Enterprise

[T1071](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1071)

[Application Layer Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1071)

Use network appliances to filter ingress or egress traffic and perform protocol-based filtering. Configure software on endpoints to filter network traffic.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1071/004)

[DNS](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1071/004)

Consider filtering DNS requests to unknown, untrusted, or known bad domains and resources. Resolving DNS requests with on-premise/proxy servers may also disrupt adversary attempts to conceal data within DNS packets.

Enterprise

[T1197](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1197)

[BITS Jobs](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1197)

Modify network and/or host firewall rules, as well as other network controls, to only allow legitimate BITS traffic.

Enterprise

[T1530](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1530)

[Data from Cloud Storage](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1530)

Cloud service providers support IP-based restrictions when accessing cloud resources. Consider using IP allowlisting along with user account management to ensure that data access is restricted not only to valid users but only from expected IP ranges to mitigate the use of stolen credentials to access data.

Enterprise

[T1602](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602)

[Data from Configuration Repository](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602)

Apply extended ACLs to block unauthorized protocols outside the trusted network.[\[7\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/TA17-156A)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/001)

[SNMP (MIB Dump)](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/001)

Apply extended ACLs to block unauthorized protocols outside the trusted network.[\[7\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/TA17-156A)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/002)

[Network Device Configuration Dump](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/002)

Apply extended ACLs to block unauthorized protocols outside the trusted network.[\[7\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/TA17-156A)

Enterprise

[T1499](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1499)

[Endpoint Denial of Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1499)

Leverage services provided by Content Delivery Networks (CDN) or providers specializing in DoS mitigations to filter traffic upstream from services.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)Filter boundary traffic by blocking source addresses sourcing the attack, blocking ports that are being targeted, or blocking protocols being used for transport. To defend against SYN floods, enable SYN Cookies.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1499/001)

[OS Exhaustion Flood](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1499/001)

Leverage services provided by Content Delivery Networks (CDN) or providers specializing in DoS mitigations to filter traffic upstream from services.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)Filter boundary traffic by blocking source addresses sourcing the attack, blocking ports that are being targeted, or blocking protocols being used for transport. To defend against SYN floods, enable SYN Cookies.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1499/002)

[Service Exhaustion Flood](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1499/002)

Leverage services provided by Content Delivery Networks (CDN) or providers specializing in DoS mitigations to filter traffic upstream from services.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)Filter boundary traffic by blocking source addresses sourcing the attack, blocking ports that are being targeted, or blocking protocols being used for transport.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1499/003)

[Application Exhaustion Flood](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1499/003)

Leverage services provided by Content Delivery Networks (CDN) or providers specializing in DoS mitigations to filter traffic upstream from services.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)Filter boundary traffic by blocking source addresses sourcing the attack, blocking ports that are being targeted, or blocking protocols being used for transport.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1499/004)

[Application or System Exploitation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1499/004)

Leverage services provided by Content Delivery Networks (CDN) or providers specializing in DoS mitigations to filter traffic upstream from services.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)Filter boundary traffic by blocking source addresses sourcing the attack, blocking ports that are being targeted, or blocking protocols being used for transport.

Enterprise

[T1048](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048)

[Exfiltration Over Alternative Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048)

Enforce proxies and use dedicated servers for services such as DNS and only allow those systems to communicate over respective ports/protocols, instead of all systems within a network. Cloud service providers support IP-based restrictions when accessing cloud resources. Consider using IP allowlisting along with user account management to ensure that data access is restricted not only to valid users but only from expected IP ranges to mitigate the use of stolen credentials to access data.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048/001)

[Exfiltration Over Symmetric Encrypted Non-C2 Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048/001)

Enforce proxies and use dedicated servers for services such as DNS and only allow those systems to communicate over respective ports/protocols, instead of all systems within a network.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048/002)

[Exfiltration Over Asymmetric Encrypted Non-C2 Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048/002)

Enforce proxies and use dedicated servers for services such as DNS and only allow those systems to communicate over respective ports/protocols, instead of all systems within a network.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048/003)

[Exfiltration Over Unencrypted Non-C2 Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048/003)

Enforce proxies and use dedicated servers for services such as DNS and only allow those systems to communicate over respective ports/protocols, instead of all systems within a network.

Enterprise

[T1187](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1187)

[Forced Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1187)

Block SMB traffic from exiting an enterprise network with egress filtering or by blocking TCP ports 139, 445 and UDP port 137. Filter or block WebDAV protocol traffic from exiting the network. If access to external resources over SMB and WebDAV is necessary, then traffic should be tightly limited with allowlisting.[\[9\]](https://www.us-cert.gov/ncas/current-activity/2017/01/16/SMB-Security-Best-Practices)[\[10\]](https://www.us-cert.gov/ncas/alerts/TA17-293A)

Enterprise

[T1570](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1570)

[Lateral Tool Transfer](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1570)

Consider using the host firewall to restrict file sharing communications such as SMB.[\[11\]](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/3185535/preventing-smb-traffic-from-lateral-connections)

Enterprise

[T1599](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1599)

[Network Boundary Bridging](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1599)

Upon identifying a compromised network device being used to bridge a network boundary, block the malicious packets using an unaffected network device in path, such as a firewall or a router that has not been compromised. Continue to monitor for additional activity and to ensure that the blocks are indeed effective.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1599/001)

[Network Address Translation Traversal](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1599/001)

Block Traffic Upon identifying a compromised network device being used to bridge a network boundary, block the malicious packets using an unaffected network device in path, such as a firewall or a router that has not been compromised. Continue to monitor for additional activity and to ensure that the blocks are indeed effective.

Enterprise

[T1498](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1498)

[Network Denial of Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1498)

When flood volumes exceed the capacity of the network connection being targeted, it is typically necessary to intercept the incoming traffic upstream to filter out the attack traffic from the legitimate traffic. Such defenses can be provided by the hosting Internet Service Provider (ISP) or by a 3rd party such as a Content Delivery Network (CDN) or providers specializing in DoS mitigations.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)

Depending on flood volume, on-premises filtering may be possible by blocking source addresses sourcing the attack, blocking ports that are being targeted, or blocking protocols being used for transport.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)

As immediate response may require rapid engagement of 3rd parties, analyze the risk associated to critical resources being affected by Network DoS attacks and create a disaster recovery plan/business continuity plan to respond to incidents.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1498/001)

[Direct Network Flood](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1498/001)

When flood volumes exceed the capacity of the network connection being targeted, it is typically necessary to intercept the incoming traffic upstream to filter out the attack traffic from the legitimate traffic. Such defenses can be provided by the hosting Internet Service Provider (ISP) or by a 3rd party such as a Content Delivery Network (CDN) or providers specializing in DoS mitigations.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)

Depending on flood volume, on-premises filtering may be possible by blocking source addresses sourcing the attack, blocking ports that are being targeted, or blocking protocols being used for transport.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)

As immediate response may require rapid engagement of 3rd parties, analyze the risk associated to critical resources being affected by Network DoS attacks and create a disaster recovery plan/business continuity plan to respond to incidents.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1498/002)

[Reflection Amplification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1498/002)

When flood volumes exceed the capacity of the network connection being targeted, it is typically necessary to intercept the incoming traffic upstream to filter out the attack traffic from the legitimate traffic. Such defenses can be provided by the hosting Internet Service Provider (ISP) or by a 3rd party such as a Content Delivery Network (CDN) or providers specializing in DoS mitigations.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)

Depending on flood volume, on-premises filtering may be possible by blocking source addresses sourcing the attack, blocking ports that are being targeted, or blocking protocols being used for transport.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)

As immediate response may require rapid engagement of 3rd parties, analyze the risk associated to critical resources being affected by Network DoS attacks and create a disaster recovery plan/business continuity plan to respond to incidents.[\[8\]](http://cert.europa.eu/static/WhitePapers/CERT-EU_Security_Whitepaper_DDoS_17-003.pdf)

Enterprise

[T1095](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1095)

[Non-Application Layer Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1095)

Filter network traffic to prevent use of protocols across the network boundary that are unnecessary.

Enterprise

[T1572](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1572)

[Protocol Tunneling](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1572)

Consider filtering network traffic to untrusted or known bad domains and resources.

Enterprise

[T1090](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1090)

[Proxy](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1090)

Traffic to known anonymity networks and C2 infrastructure can be blocked through the use of network allow and block lists. It should be noted that this kind of blocking may be circumvented by other techniques like[Domain Fronting](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1090/004).

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1090/003)

[Multi-hop Proxy](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1090/003)

Traffic to known anonymity networks and C2 infrastructure can be blocked through the use of network allow and block lists. It should be noted that this kind of blocking may be circumvented by other techniques like[Domain Fronting](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1090/004).

Enterprise

[T1219](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1219)

[Remote Access Software](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1219)

Properly configure firewalls, application firewalls, and proxies to limit outgoing traffic to sites and services used by remote access software.

Enterprise

[T1021](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/002)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021):[SMB/Windows Admin Shares](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/002)

Consider using the host firewall to restrict file sharing communications such as SMB.[\[11\]](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/3185535/preventing-smb-traffic-from-lateral-connections)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/005)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021):[VNC](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/005)

VNC defaults to TCP ports 5900 for the server, 5800 for browser access, and 5500 for a viewer in listening mode. Filtering or blocking these ports will inhibit VNC traffic utilizing default ports.

Enterprise

[T1218](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218)

[System Binary Proxy Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218)

Use network appliances to filter ingress or egress traffic and perform protocol-based filtering. Configure software on endpoints to filter network traffic.

[.012](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/012)

[Verclsid](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/012)

Consider modifying host firewall rules to prevent egress traffic from verclsid.exe.

Enterprise

[T1205](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1205)

[Traffic Signaling](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1205)

Mitigation of some variants of this technique could be achieved through the use of stateful firewalls, depending upon how it is implemented.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1205/001)

[Port Knocking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1205/001)

Mitigation of some variants of this technique could be achieved through the use of stateful firewalls, depending upon how it is implemented.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1205/002)

[Socket Filters](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1205/002)

Mitigation of some variants of this technique could be achieved through the use of stateful firewalls, depending upon how it is implemented.

Enterprise

[T1537](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1537)

[Transfer Data to Cloud Account](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1537)

Implement network-based filtering restrictions to prohibit data transfers to untrusted VPCs.

Enterprise

[T1552](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

[Unsecured Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

Limit access to the Instance Metadata API. A properly configured Web Application Firewall (WAF) may help prevent external adversaries from exploiting Server-side Request Forgery (SSRF) attacks that allow access to the Cloud Instance Metadata API.[\[12\]](https://redlock.io/blog/instance-metadata-api-a-modern-day-trojan-horse)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/005)

[Cloud Instance Metadata API](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/005)

Limit access to the Instance Metadata API. A properly configured Web Application Firewall (WAF) may help prevent external adversaries from exploiting Server-side Request Forgery (SSRF) attacks that allow access to the Cloud Instance Metadata API.[\[12\]](https://redlock.io/blog/instance-metadata-api-a-modern-day-trojan-horse)

Limit Access to Resource Over Network
=====================================

Prevent access to file shares, remote access to systems, unnecessary services. Mechanisms to limit access may include use of network concentrators, RDP gateways, etc.

ID:M1035

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:09 June 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1035/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1557](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)

[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)

Limit access to network infrastructure and resources that can be used to reshape traffic or otherwise produce AiTM conditions.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/002)

[ARP Cache Poisoning](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/002)

Create static ARP entries for networked devices. Implementing static ARP entries may be infeasible for large networks.

Enterprise

[T1612](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1612)

[Build Image on Host](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1612)

Limit communications with the container service to local Unix sockets or remote access via SSH. Require secure port access to communicate with the APIs over TLS by disabling unauthenticated access to the Docker API on port 2375. Instead, communicate with the Docker API over TLS on port 2376.[\[1\]](https://docs.docker.com/engine/security/protect-access/)

Enterprise

[T1609](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1609)

[Container Administration Command](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1609)

Limit communications with the container service to managed and secured channels, such as local Unix sockets or remote access via SSH. Require secure port access to communicate with the APIs over TLS by disabling unauthenticated access to the Docker API and Kubernetes API Server.[\[1\]](https://docs.docker.com/engine/security/protect-access/)[\[2\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/security/controlling-access/)In Kubernetes clusters deployed in cloud environments, use native cloud platform features to restrict the IP ranges that are permitted to access to API server.[\[3\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/security/overview/)Where possible, consider enabling just-in-time (JIT) access to the Kubernetes API to place additional restrictions on access.[\[4\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/aks/managed-aad)

Enterprise

[T1613](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1613)

[Container and Resource Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1613)

Limit communications with the container service to managed and secured channels, such as local Unix sockets or remote access via SSH. Require secure port access to communicate with the APIs over TLS by disabling unauthenticated access to the Docker API and Kubernetes API Server.[\[1\]](https://docs.docker.com/engine/security/protect-access/)[\[2\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/security/controlling-access/)In Kubernetes clusters deployed in cloud environments, use native cloud platform features to restrict the IP ranges that are permitted to access to API server.[\[3\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/security/overview/)Where possible, consider enabling just-in-time (JIT) access to the Kubernetes API to place additional restrictions on access.[\[4\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/aks/managed-aad)

Enterprise

[T1610](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1610)

[Deploy Container](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1610)

Limit communications with the container service to managed and secured channels, such as local Unix sockets or remote access via SSH. Require secure port access to communicate with the APIs over TLS by disabling unauthenticated access to the Docker API, Kubernetes API Server, and container orchestration web applications.[\[1\]](https://docs.docker.com/engine/security/protect-access/)[\[2\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/security/controlling-access/)In Kubernetes clusters deployed in cloud environments, use native cloud platform features to restrict the IP ranges that are permitted to access to API server.[\[3\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/security/overview/)Where possible, consider enabling just-in-time (JIT) access to the Kubernetes API to place additional restrictions on access.[\[4\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/aks/managed-aad)

[T1546](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546)

If possible, use a Remote Desktop Gateway to manage connections and security configuration of RDP within a network.[\[5\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/cc731150.aspx)

Enterprise

[T1133](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1133)

[External Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1133)

Limit access to remote services through centrally managed concentrators such as VPNs and other managed remote access systems.

Enterprise

[T1200](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1200)

[Hardware Additions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1200)

Establish network access control policies, such as using device certificates and the 802.1x standard.[\[6\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IEEE_802.1X)Restrict use of DHCP to registered devices to prevent unregistered devices from communicating with trusted systems.

Enterprise

[T1542](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/005)

[TFTP Boot](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/005)

Restrict use of protocols without encryption or authentication mechanisms. Limit access to administrative and management interfaces from untrusted network sources.

[T1563](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563)

===========================

Block users or groups from installing unapproved software.

ID:M1033

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:11 June 2019

**ATT&CK****Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1547](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547)

[.013](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/013)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[XDG Autostart Entries](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/013)

Restrict software installation to trusted repositories only and be cautious of orphaned software packages.

Enterprise

[T1176](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1176)

[Browser Extensions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1176)

Only install browser extensions from trusted sources that can be verified. Browser extensions for some browsers can be controlled through Group Policy. Change settings to prevent the browser from installing extensions without sufficient permissions.

Enterprise

Multi-factor Authentication
===========================

Use two or more pieces of evidence to authenticate to a system; such as username and password in addition to a token from a physical smart card or token generator.

ID:M1032

Version:1.0

Created:10 June 2019

Last Modified:21 October 2022

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1032/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1098](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098)

[Account Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098)

Use multi-factor authentication for user and privileged accounts.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/001)

[Additional Cloud Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/001)

Use multi-factor authentication for user and privileged accounts. Consider enforcing multi-factor authentication for the`CreateKeyPair`and`ImportKeyPair`API calls through IAM policies.[\[1\]](https://expel.io/blog/finding-evil-in-aws/)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/002)

[Additional Email Delegate Permissions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/002)

Use multi-factor authentication for user and privileged accounts.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/003)

[Additional Cloud Roles](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/003)

Use multi-factor authentication for user and privileged accounts.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/005)

[Device Registration](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/005)

Require multi-factor authentication to register devices in Azure AD.[\[2\]](https://www.microsoft.com/security/blog/2022/01/26/evolved-phishing-device-registration-trick-adds-to-phishers-toolbox-for-victims-without-mfa)Configure multi-factor authentication systems to disallow enrolling new devices for inactive accounts.[\[3\]](https://www.cisa.gov/uscert/ncas/alerts/aa22-074a)When first enrolling MFA, use conditional access policies to restrict device enrollment to trusted locations or devices, and consider using temporary access passes as an initial MFA solution to enroll a device.[\[4\]](https://www.mandiant.com/resources/blog/apt29-continues-targeting-microsoft)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/006)

[Additional Container Cluster Roles](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/006)

Require multi-factor authentication for user accounts integrated into container clusters through cloud deployments or via authentication protocols such as LDAP or SAML.

Enterprise

[T1110](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110)

[Brute Force](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110)

Use multi-factor authentication. Where possible, also enable multi-factor authentication on externally facing services.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/001)

[Password Guessing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/001)

Use multi-factor authentication. Where possible, also enable multi-factor authentication on externally facing services.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/002)

[Password Cracking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/002)

Use multi-factor authentication. Where possible, also enable multi-factor authentication on externally facing services.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/003)

[Password Spraying](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/003)

Use multi-factor authentication. Where possible, also enable multi-factor authentication on externally facing services.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/004)

[Credential Stuffing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/004)

Use multi-factor authentication. Where possible, also enable multi-factor authentication on externally facing services.

Enterprise

[T1136](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1136)

[Create Account](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1136)

Use multi-factor authentication for user and privileged accounts.

[T1530](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1530)

[Data from Cloud Storage](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1530)

Consider using multi-factor authentication to restrict access to resources and cloud storage APIs.[\[5\]](https://aws.amazon.com/premiumsupport/knowledge-center/secure-s3-resources/)

Enterprise

[T1213](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213)

[Data from Information Repositories](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213)

Use two or more pieces of evidence to authenticate to a system; such as username and password in addition to a token from a physical smart card or token generator.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/003)

[Code Repositories](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/003)

Use multi-factor authentication for logons to code repositories.

Enterprise

[T1114](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114)

[Email Collection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114)

Use of multi-factor authentication for public-facing webmail servers is a recommended best practice to minimize the usefulness of usernames and passwords to adversaries.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114/002)

[Remote Email Collection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1114/002)

Use of multi-factor authentication for public-facing webmail servers is a recommended best practice to minimize the usefulness of usernames and passwords to adversaries.

Enterprise

[T1133](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1133)

[External Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1133)

Use strong two-factor or multi-factor authentication for remote service accounts to mitigate an adversary's ability to leverage stolen credentials, but be aware of[Multi-Factor Authentication Interception](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1111)techniques for some two-factor authentication implementations.

Enterprise

[T1556](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

[Modify Authentication Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

Integrating multi-factor authentication (MFA) as part of organizational policy can greatly reduce the risk of an adversary gaining control of valid credentials that may be used for additional tactics such as initial access, lateral movement, and collecting information. MFA can also be used to restrict access to cloud resources and APIs.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/001)

[Domain Controller Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/001)

Integrating multi-factor authentication (MFA) as part of organizational policy can greatly reduce the risk of an adversary gaining control of valid credentials that may be used for additional tactics such as initial access, lateral movement, and collecting information. MFA can also be used to restrict access to cloud resources and APIs.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/003)

[Pluggable Authentication Modules](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/003)

Integrating multi-factor authentication (MFA) as part of organizational policy can greatly reduce the risk of an adversary gaining control of valid credentials that may be used for additional tactics such as initial access, lateral movement, and collecting information.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/004)

[Network Device Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/004)

Use multi-factor authentication for user and privileged accounts. Most embedded network devices support TACACS+ and/or RADIUS. Follow vendor prescribed best practices for hardening access control.[\[6\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#39)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/006)

[Multi-Factor Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/006)

Ensure that MFA and MFA policies and requirements are properly implemented for existing and deactivated or dormant accounts and devices. If possible, consider configuring MFA solutions to "fail closed" rather than grant access in case of serious errors.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/007)

[Hybrid Identity](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/007)

Integrating multi-factor authentication (MFA) as part of organizational policy can greatly reduce the risk of an adversary gaining control of valid credentials that may be used for additional tactics such as initial access, lateral movement, and collecting information. MFA can also be used to restrict access to cloud resources and APIs.

Enterprise

[T1601](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601)

[Modify System Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601)

Use multi-factor authentication for user and privileged accounts. Most embedded network devices support TACACS+ and/or RADIUS. Follow vendor prescribed best practices for hardening access control.[\[6\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#39)

[Downgrade System Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1601/002)

Use multi-factor authentication for user and privileged accounts. Most embedded network devices support TACACS+ and/or RADIUS. Follow vendor prescribed best practices for hardening access control.[\[6\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#39)

Enterprise

[T1621](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1621)

[Multi-Factor Authentication Request Generation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1621)

Implement more secure 2FA/MFA mechanisms in replacement of simple push or one-click 2FA/MFA options. For example, having users enter a one-time code provided by the login screen into the 2FA/MFA application or utilizing other out-of-band 2FA/MFA mechanisms (such as rotating code-based hardware tokens providing rotating codes that need an accompanying user pin) may be more secure. Furthermore, change default configurations and implement limits upon the maximum number of 2FA/MFA request prompts that can be sent to users in period of time.[\[7\]](https://portswigger.net/daily-swig/mfa-fatigue-attacks-users-tricked-into-allowing-device-access-due-to-overload-of-push-notifications)

Enterprise

[T1599](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1599)

[Network Boundary Bridging](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1599)

Use multi-factor authentication for user and privileged accounts. Most embedded network devices support TACACS+ and/or RADIUS. Follow vendor prescribed best practices for hardening access control.[\[6\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#39)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1599/001)

[Network Address Translation Traversal](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1599/001)

Use multi-factor authentication for user and privileged accounts. Most embedded network devices support TACACS+ and/or RADIUS. Follow vendor prescribed best practices for hardening access control.[\[6\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#39)

Enterprise

[T1040](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1040)

[Network Sniffing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1040)

Use multi-factor authentication wherever possible.

Enterprise

[T1021](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021)

Use multi-factor authentication on remote service logons where possible.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/001)

[Remote Desktop Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/001)

Use multi-factor authentication for remote logins.[\[8\]](https://security.berkeley.edu/node/94)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/004)

[SSH](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/004)

Require multi-factor authentication for SSH connections wherever possible, such as password protected SSH keys.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/007)

[Cloud Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/007)

Use multi-factor authentication on cloud services whenever possible.

Enterprise

[T1072](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

[Software Deployment Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

Ensure proper system and access isolation for critical network systems through use of multi-factor authentication.

Enterprise

[T1539](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1539)

[Steal Web Session Cookie](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1539)

A physical second factor key that uses the target login domain as part of the negotiation protocol will prevent session cookie theft through proxy methods.[\[9\]](https://breakdev.org/evilginx-2-next-generation-of-phishing-2fa-tokens/)

Enterprise

[T1199](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1199)

[Trusted Relationship](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1199)

Require MFA for all delegated administrator accounts.[\[10\]](https://www.microsoft.com/security/blog/2021/10/25/nobelium-targeting-delegated-administrative-privileges-to-facilitate-broader-attacks)

Enterprise

[T1078](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/002)

[Valid Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078):[Domain Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/002)

Integrating multi-factor authentication (MFA) as part of organizational policy can greatly reduce the risk of an adversary gaining control of valid credentials that may be used for additional tactics such as initial access, lateral movement, and collecting information. MFA can also be used to restrict access to cloud resources and APIs.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/004)

[Valid Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078):[Cloud Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/004)

Use multi-factor authentication for cloud accounts, especially privileged accounts. This can be implemented in a variety of forms (e.g. hardware, virtual, SMS), and can also be audited using administrative reporting features.[\[11\]](https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/security/newly-updated-features-in-the-aws-iam-console-help-you-adhere-to-iam-best-practices/)

Network Intrusion Prevention
============================

Use intrusion detection signatures to block traffic at network boundaries.

ID:M1031

Version:1.0

Created:10 June 2019

Last Modified:10 June 2019

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1031/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1557](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)

[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that can identify traffic patterns indicative of AiTM activity can be used to mitigate activity at the network level.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/001)

[LLMNR/NBT-NS Poisoning and SMB Relay](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/001)

Enterprise

[T1132](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1132)

[Data Encoding](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1132)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that use network signatures to identify traffic for specific adversary malware can be used to mitigate activity at the network level. Signatures are often for unique indicators within protocols and may be based on the specific obfuscation technique used by a particular adversary or tool, and will likely be different across various malware families and versions. Adversaries will likely change tool C2 signatures over time or construct protocols in such a way as to avoid detection by common defensive tools.[\[2\]](https://arxiv.org/ftp/arxiv/papers/1408/1408.1136.pdf)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1132/001)

[Standard Encoding](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1132/001)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that use network signatures to identify traffic for specific adversary malware can be used to mitigate activity at the network level. Signatures are often for unique indicators within protocols and may be based on the specific obfuscation technique used by a particular adversary or tool, and will likely be different across various malware families and versions. Adversaries will likely change tool C2 signatures over time or construct protocols in such a way as to avoid detection by common defensive tools.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1132/002)

[Non-Standard Encoding](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1132/002)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that use network signatures to identify traffic for specific adversary malware can be used to mitigate activity at the network level. Signatures are often for unique indicators within protocols and may be based on the specific obfuscation technique used by a particular adversary or tool, and will likely be different across various malware families and versions. Adversaries will likely change tool C2 signatures over time or construct protocols in such a way as to avoid detection by common defensive tools.

Enterprise

[T1568](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1568)

[Dynamic Resolution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1568)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that use network signatures to identify traffic for specific adversary malware can be used to mitigate activity at the network level. Malware researchers can reverse engineer malware variants that use dynamic resolution and determine future C2 infrastructure that the malware will attempt to contact, but this is a time and resource intensive effort.[\[5\]](http://go.cybereason.com/rs/996-YZT-709/images/Cybereason-Lab-Analysis-Dissecting-DGAs-Eight-Real-World-DGA-Variants.pdf)[\[6\]](https://umbrella.cisco.com/blog/2015/02/18/at-high-noon-algorithms-do-battle/)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1568/002)

[Domain Generation Algorithms](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1568/002)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that use network signatures to identify traffic for specific adversary malware can be used to mitigate activity at the network level. Malware researchers can reverse engineer malware variants that use DGAs and determine future domains that the malware will attempt to contact, but this is a time and resource intensive effort.[\[5\]](http://go.cybereason.com/rs/996-YZT-709/images/Cybereason-Lab-Analysis-Dissecting-DGAs-Eight-Real-World-DGA-Variants.pdf)[\[6\]](https://umbrella.cisco.com/blog/2015/02/18/at-high-noon-algorithms-do-battle/)Malware is also increasingly incorporating seed values that can be unique for each instance, which would then need to be determined to extract future generated domains. In some cases, the seed that a particular sample uses can be extracted from DNS traffic.[\[7\]](https://blogs.akamai.com/2018/01/a-death-match-of-domain-generation-algorithms.html)Even so, there can be thousands of possible domains generated per day; this makes it impractical for defenders to preemptively register all possible C2 domains due to the cost.

[Encrypted Channel](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1573)

Enterprise

[T1105](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1105)

[Ingress Tool Transfer](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1105)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that use network signatures to identify traffic for specific adversary malware or unusual data transfer over known protocols like FTP can be used to mitigate activity at the network level. Signatures are often for unique indicators within protocols and may be based on the specific obfuscation technique used by a particular adversary or tool, and will likely be different across various malware families and versions. Adversaries will likely change tool C2 signatures over time or construct protocols in such a way as to avoid detection by common defensive tools.[\[2\]](https://arxiv.org/ftp/arxiv/papers/1408/1408.1136.pdf)

Enterprise

[T1570](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1570)

[Lateral Tool Transfer](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1570)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that use network signatures to identify traffic for specific adversary malware or unusual data transfer over known tools and protocols like FTP can be used to mitigate activity at the network level. Signatures are often for unique indicators within protocols and may be based on the specific obfuscation technique used by a particular adversary or tool, and will likely be different across various malware families and versions.[\[2\]](https://arxiv.org/ftp/arxiv/papers/1408/1408.1136.pdf)

[T1090](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1090)

[Proxy](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1090)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that use network signatures to identify traffic for specific adversary malware can be used to mitigate activity at the network level. Signatures are often for unique indicators within protocols and may be based on the specific C2 protocol used by a particular adversary or tool, and will likely be different across various malware families and versions. Adversaries will likely change tool C2 signatures over time or construct protocols in such a way as to avoid detection by common defensive tools.[\[2\]](https://arxiv.org/ftp/arxiv/papers/1408/1408.1136.pdf)

Network Segmentation
====================

Architect sections of the network to isolate critical systems, functions, or resources. Use physical and logical segmentation to prevent access to potentially sensitive systems and information. Use a DMZ to contain any internet-facing services that should not be exposed from the internal network. Configure separate virtual private cloud (VPC) instances to isolate critical cloud systems.

ID:M1030

Version:1.1

Created:10 June 2019

Last Modified:14 May 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1030/)

Operating System Configuration
==============================

Make configuration changes related to the operating system or a common feature of the operating system that result in system hardening against techniques.

ID:M1028

Version:1.2

Created:06 June 2019

Last Modified:31 March 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1028/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1548](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

[Abuse Elevation Control Mechanism](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

Applications with known vulnerabilities or known shell escapes should not have the setuid or setgid bits set to reduce potential damage if an application is compromised. Additionally, the number of programs with setuid or setgid bits set should be minimized across a system. Ensuring that the sudo tty\_tickets setting is enabled will prevent this leakage across tty sessions.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/001)

[Setuid and Setgid](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/001)

Applications with known vulnerabilities or known shell escapes should not have the setuid or setgid bits set to reduce potential damage if an application is compromised. Additionally, the number of programs with setuid or setgid bits set should be minimized across a system.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/003)

[Sudo and Sudo Caching](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/003)

Ensuring that the`tty_tickets`setting is enabled will prevent this leakage across tty sessions.

Enterprise

[T1087](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087)

[Account Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087)

Prevent administrator accounts from being enumerated when an application is elevating through UAC since it can lead to the disclosure of account names. The Registry key is located`HKLM\ SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\CredUI\EnumerateAdministrators`. It can be disabled through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Administrative Templates > Windows Components > Credential User Interface: E numerate administrator accounts on elevation.[\[1\]](https://www.stigviewer.com/stig/microsoft_windows_server_2012_member_server/2013-07-25/finding/WN12-CC-000077)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087/001)

[Local Account](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087/001)

Prevent administrator accounts from being enumerated when an application is elevating through UAC since it can lead to the disclosure of account names. The Registry key is located at`HKLM\ SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\CredUI\EnumerateAdministrators`. It can be disabled through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Administrative Templates > Windows Components > Credential User Interface: Enumerate administrator accounts on elevation.[\[1\]](https://www.stigviewer.com/stig/microsoft_windows_server_2012_member_server/2013-07-25/finding/WN12-CC-000077)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087/002)

[Domain Account](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087/002)

Prevent administrator accounts from being enumerated when an application is elevating through UAC since it can lead to the disclosure of account names. The Registry key is located at`HKLM\ SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\CredUI\EnumerateAdministrators`. It can be disabled through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Administrative Templates > Windows Components > Credential User Interface: Enumerate administrator accounts on elevation.[\[1\]](https://www.stigviewer.com/stig/microsoft_windows_server_2012_member_server/2013-07-25/finding/WN12-CC-000077)

Enterprise

[T1098](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098)

[Account Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098)

Protect domain controllers by ensuring proper security configuration for critical servers to limit access by potentially unnecessary protocols and services, such as SMB file sharing.

Enterprise

[T1197](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1197)

[BITS Jobs](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1197)

Consider reducing the default BITS job lifetime in Group Policy or by editing the`JobInactivityTimeout`and`MaxDownloadTime`Registry values in`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\Software\Policies\Microsoft\Windows\BITS`.[\[2\]](https://msdn.microsoft.com/library/windows/desktop/bb968799.aspx)

Enterprise

[T1092](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1092)

[Communication Through Removable Media](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1092)

Disallow or restrict removable media at an organizational policy level if they are not required for business operations.[\[3\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/cc772540(v=ws.10).aspx)

Enterprise

[T1136](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1136)

[Create Account](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1136)

Protect domain controllers by ensuring proper security configuration for critical servers.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1136/002)

[Domain Account](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1136/002)

Protect domain controllers by ensuring proper security configuration for critical servers.

Enterprise

[T1543](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543)

[Create or Modify System Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543)

Ensure that Driver Signature Enforcement is enabled to restrict unsigned drivers from being installed.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/003)

[Windows Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/003)

Ensure that Driver Signature Enforcement is enabled to restrict unsigned drivers from being installed.

Enterprise

[T1546](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546)

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/008)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546):[Accessibility Features](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/008)

To use this technique remotely, an adversary must use it in conjunction with RDP. Ensure that Network Level Authentication is enabled to force the remote desktop session to authenticate before the session is created and the login screen displayed. It is enabled by default on Windows Vista and later.[\[4\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/cc732713.aspx)

Enterprise

[T1011](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1011)

[Exfiltration Over Other Network Medium](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1011)

Prevent the creation of new network adapters where possible.[\[5\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/dd252791.aspx)[\[6\]](https://www.techrepublic.com/blog/data-center/configuring-wireless-settings-via-group-policy/)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1011/001)

[Exfiltration Over Bluetooth](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1011/001)

Prevent the creation of new network adapters where possible.

Enterprise

[T1564](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/002)

[Hide Artifacts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564):[Hidden Users](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/002)

If the computer is domain joined, then group policy can help restrict the ability to create or hide users. Similarly, preventing the modification of the`/Library/Preferences/com.apple.loginwindow``Hide500Users`value will force all users to be visible.

Enterprise

[T1574](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/006)

[Hijack Execution Flow](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574):[Dynamic Linker Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/006)

When System Integrity Protection (SIP) is enabled in macOS, the aforementioned environment variables are ignored when executing protected binaries. Third-party applications can also leverage Apples Hardened Runtime, ensuring these environment variables are subject to imposed restrictions.[\[7\]](https://developer.apple.com/documentation/security/hardened_runtime)Admins can add restrictions to applications by setting the setuid and/or setgid bits, use entitlements, or have a \_\_RESTRICT segment in the Mach-O binary.

Enterprise

[T1562](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/003)

[Impair Defenses](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562):[Impair Command History Logging](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/003)

Make sure that the`HISTCONTROL`environment variable is set to "ignoredups" instead of "ignoreboth" or "ignorespace".

Enterprise

[T1490](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1490)

[Inhibit System Recovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1490)

Consider technical controls to prevent the disabling of services or deletion of files involved in system recovery. Additionally, ensure that WinRE is enabled using the following command:`reagentc /enable`.[\[8\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-hardware/manufacture/desktop/reagentc-command-line-options?view=windows-11)

Enterprise

[T1036](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036)

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036/007)

[Masquerading](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036):[Double File Extension](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036/007)

Disable the default to "hide file extensions for known file types" in Windows OS.[\[9\]](https://www.seqrite.com/blog/how-to-avoid-dual-attack-and-vulnerable-files-with-double-extension/)[\[10\]](https://www.howtogeek.com/205086/beginner-how-to-make-windows-show-file-extensions/)

Enterprise

[T1556](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

[Modify Authentication Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

Ensure only valid password filters are registered. Filter DLLs must be present in Windows installation directory (`C:\Windows\System32\`by default) of a domain controller and/or local computer with a corresponding entry in`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\Lsa\Notification Packages`.

Starting in Windows 11 22H2, the`EnableMPRNotifications`policy can be disabled through Group Policy or through a configuration service provider to prevent Winlogon from sending credentials to network providers.[\[11\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/client-management/mdm/policy-csp-windowslogon)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/002)

[Password Filter DLL](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/002)

Ensure only valid password filters are registered. Filter DLLs must be present in Windows installation directory (C:\\Windows\\System32\\ by default) of a domain controller and/or local computer with a corresponding entry in HKEY\_LOCAL\_MACHINE\\SYSTEM\\CurrentControlSet\\Control\\Lsa\\Notification Packages.

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/008)

[Network Provider DLL](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/008)

Starting in Windows 11 22H2, the`EnableMPRNotifications`policy can be disabled through Group Policy or through a configuration service provider to prevent Winlogon from sending credentials to network providers.[\[11\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/client-management/mdm/policy-csp-windowslogon)

Enterprise

[T1135](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1135)

[Network Share Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1135)

Enable Windows Group Policy "Do Not Allow Anonymous Enumeration of SAM Accounts and Shares" security setting to limit users who can enumerate network shares.[\[12\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/threat-protection/security-policy-settings/network-access-do-not-allow-anonymous-enumeration-of-sam-accounts-and-shares)

Enterprise

[T1003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

[OS Credential Dumping](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

Consider disabling or restricting NTLM.[\[13\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/jj865668.aspx)Consider disabling WDigest authentication.[\[14\]](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2871997/microsoft-security-advisory-update-to-improve-credentials-protection-a)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/001)

[LSASS Memory](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/001)

Consider disabling or restricting NTLM.[\[13\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/jj865668.aspx)Consider disabling WDigest authentication.[\[14\]](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2871997/microsoft-security-advisory-update-to-improve-credentials-protection-a)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/002)

[Security Account Manager](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/002)

Consider disabling or restricting NTLM.[\[13\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/jj865668.aspx)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/005)

[Cached Domain Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/005)

Consider limiting the number of cached credentials (HKLM\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\Windows NT\\Current Version\\Winlogon\\cachedlogonscountvalue)[\[15\]](https://www.first.org/resources/papers/conf2017/Windows-Credentials-Attacks-and-Mitigation-Techniques.pdf)

Enterprise

[T1542](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/005)

[Pre-OS Boot](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542):[TFTP Boot](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/005)

Follow vendor device hardening best practices to disable unnecessary and unused features and services, avoid using default configurations and passwords, and introduce logging and auditing for detection.

Enterprise

[T1563](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/002)

[Remote Service Session Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563):[RDP Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/002)

Change GPOs to define shorter timeouts sessions and maximum amount of time any single session can be active. Change GPOs to specify the maximum amount of time that a disconnected session stays active on the RD session host server.[\[16\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/cc754272(v=ws.11).aspx)

Enterprise

[T1021](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/001)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021):[Remote Desktop Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/001)

Change GPOs to define shorter timeouts sessions and maximum amount of time any single session can be active. Change GPOs to specify the maximum amount of time that a disconnected session stays active on the RD session host server.[\[16\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/cc754272(v=ws.11).aspx)

Enterprise

[T1053](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053)

[Scheduled Task/Job](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053)

Configure settings for scheduled tasks to force tasks to run under the context of the authenticated account instead of allowing them to run as SYSTEM. The associated Registry key is located at`HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\Lsa\SubmitControl`. The setting can be configured through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > Security Options: Domain Controller: Allow server operators to schedule tasks, set to disabled.[\[17\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/jj852168.aspx)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/002)

[At](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/002)

Configure settings for scheduled tasks to force tasks to run under the context of the authenticated account instead of allowing them to run as SYSTEM. The associated Registry key is located at`HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\Lsa\SubmitControl`. The setting can be configured through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > Security Options: Domain Controller: Allow server operators to schedule tasks, set to disabled.[\[17\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/jj852168.aspx)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/005)

[Scheduled Task](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/005)

Configure settings for scheduled tasks to force tasks to run under the context of the authenticated account instead of allowing them to run as SYSTEM. The associated Registry key is located at HKLM\\SYSTEM\\CurrentControlSet\\Control\\Lsa\\SubmitControl. The setting can be configured through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > Security Options: Domain Controller: Allow server operators to schedule tasks, set to disabled.[\[17\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/jj852168.aspx)

Enterprise

[T1553](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553)

[Subvert Trust Controls](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553)

Windows Group Policy can be used to manage root certificates and the`Flags`value of`HKLM\SOFTWARE\Policies\Microsoft\SystemCertificates\Root\ProtectedRoots`can be set to 1 to prevent non-administrator users from making further root installations into their own HKCU certificate store.[\[18\]](https://posts.specterops.io/code-signing-certificate-cloning-attacks-and-defenses-6f98657fc6ec)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/004)

[Install Root Certificate](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/004)

Windows Group Policy can be used to manage root certificates and the`Flags`value of`HKLM\SOFTWARE\Policies\Microsoft\SystemCertificates\Root\ProtectedRoots`can be set to 1 to prevent non-administrator users from making further root installations into their own HKCU certificate store.[\[18\]](https://posts.specterops.io/code-signing-certificate-cloning-attacks-and-defenses-6f98657fc6ec)

Enterprise

[T1552](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

[Unsecured Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

There are multiple methods of preventing a user's command history from being flushed to their .bash\_history file, including use of the following commands:`set` `+o history`and`set -o history`to start logging again;`unset HISTFILE`being added to a user's .bash\_rc file; and`ln -s /dev/null ~/.bash_history`to write commands to`/dev/null`instead.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/003)

[Bash History](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/003)

There are multiple methods of preventing a user's command history from being flushed to their .bash\_history file, including use of the following commands:`set` `+o history`and`set -o history`to start logging again;`unset HISTFILE`being added to a user's .bash\_rc file; and`ln -s /dev/null ~/.bash_history`to write commands to`/dev/null`instead.

Password Policies
=================

Set and enforce secure password policies for accounts.

ID:M1027

Version:1.0

Created:06 June 2019

Last Modified:21 October 2022

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1027/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

--------------------------------------

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/001)

[Password Guessing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/001)

Refer to NIST guidelines when creating password policies.[\[1\]](https://pages.nist.gov/800-63-3/sp800-63b.html)

Enterprise

[T1555](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555)

[Credentials from Password Stores](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555)

The password for the user's login keychain can be changed from the user's login password. This increases the complexity for an adversary because they need to know an additional password.

Organizations may consider weighing the risk of storing credentials in password stores and web browsers. If system, software, or web browser credential disclosure is a significant concern, technical controls, policy, and user training may be used to prevent storage of credentials in improper locations.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555/001)

[Keychain](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555/001)

The password for the user's login keychain can be changed from the user's login password. This increases the complexity for an adversary because they need to know an additional password.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555/003)

[Credentials from Web Browsers](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555/003)

Organizations may consider weighing the risk of storing credentials in web browsers. If web browser credential disclosure is a significant concern, technical controls, policy, and user training may be used to prevent storage of credentials in web browsers.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555/005)

[Password Managers](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555/005)

Refer to NIST guidelines when creating password policies for master passwords.[\[1\]](https://pages.nist.gov/800-63-3/sp800-63b.html)

Enterprise

[T1187](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1187)

[Forced Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1187)

Use strong passwords to increase the difficulty of credential hashes from being cracked if they are obtained.

Enterprise

[T1201](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1201)

[Password Policy Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1201)

Ensure only valid password filters are registered. Filter DLLs must be present in Windows installation directory (`C:\Windows\System32\`by default) of a domain controller and/or local computer with a corresponding entry in`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\Lsa\Notification Packages`.[\[3\]](https://msdn.microsoft.com/library/windows/desktop/ms721766.aspx)

[T1563](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563)

[Remote Service Session Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563)

Set and enforce secure password policies for accounts.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/001)

[SSH Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/001)

Ensure SSH key pairs have strong passwords and refrain from using key-store technologies such as ssh-agent unless they are properly protected.

Enterprise

[T1021](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021)

Do not reuse local administrator account passwords across systems. Ensure password complexity and uniqueness such that the passwords cannot be cracked or guessed.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/002)

[SMB/Windows Admin Shares](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/002)

Do not reuse local administrator account passwords across systems. Ensure password complexity and uniqueness such that the passwords cannot be cracked or guessed.

Enterprise

[T1072](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

[Software Deployment Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

Verify that account credentials that may be used to access deployment systems are unique and not used throughout the enterprise network.

Enterprise

[T1558](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558)

[Steal or Forge Kerberos Tickets](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558)

Ensure strong password length (ideally 25+ characters) and complexity for service accounts and that these passwords periodically expire.[\[4\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2293)Also consider using Group Managed Service Accounts or another third party product such as password vaulting.[\[4\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2293)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/002)

[Silver Ticket](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/002)

Ensure strong password length (ideally 25+ characters) and complexity for service accounts and that these passwords periodically expire.[\[4\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2293)Also consider using Group Managed Service Accounts or another third party product such as password vaulting.[\[4\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2293)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/003)

[Kerberoasting](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/003)

Ensure strong password length (ideally 25+ characters) and complexity for service accounts and that these passwords periodically expire.[\[4\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2293)Also consider using Group Managed Service Accounts or another third party product such as password vaulting.[\[4\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2293)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/004)

[AS-REP Roasting](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/004)

Ensure strong password length (ideally 25+ characters) and complexity for service accounts and that these passwords periodically expire. Also consider using Group Managed Service Accounts or another third party product such as password vaulting.[\[4\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2293)

Enterprise

[T1552](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

[Unsecured Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

Use strong passphrases for private keys to make cracking difficult. Do not store credentials within the Registry. Establish an organizational policy that prohibits password storage in files.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/001)

[Credentials In Files](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/001)

Establish an organizational policy that prohibits password storage in files.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/002)

[Credentials in Registry](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/002)

Do not store credentials within the Registry.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/004)

[Private Keys](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/004)

Use strong passphrases for private keys to make cracking difficult.

Enterprise

[T1550](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

[Use Alternate Authentication Material](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

Set and enforce secure password policies for accounts.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/003)

[Pass the Ticket](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/003)

Ensure that local administrator accounts have complex, unique passwords.

Enterprise

[T1078](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

[Valid Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

Applications and appliances that utilize default username and password should be changed immediately after the installation, and before deployment to a production environment.[\[5\]](https://www.us-cert.gov/ncas/alerts/TA13-175A)When possible, applications that use SSH keys should be updated periodically and properly secured.

Policies should minimize (if not eliminate) reuse of passwords between different user accounts, especially employees using the same credentials for personal accounts that may not be defended by enterprise security resources.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/001)

[Default Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/001)

Applications and appliances that utilize default username and password should be changed immediately after the installation, and before deployment to a production environment.[\[5\]](https://www.us-cert.gov/ncas/alerts/TA13-175A)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/003)

[Local Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/003)

Ensure that local administrator accounts have complex, unique passwords across all systems on the network.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/004)

[Cloud Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/004)

Ensure that cloud accounts, particularly privileged accounts, have complex, unique passwords across all systems on the network. Passwords and access keys should be rotated regularly. This limits the amount of time credentials can be used to access resources if a credential is compromised without your knowledge. Cloud service providers may track access key age to help audit and identify keys that may need to be rotated.[\[6\]](https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/security/newly-updated-features-in-the-aws-iam-console-help-you-adhere-to-iam-best-practices/)

3.  [Microsoft. (n.d.). Installing and Registering a Password Filter DLL. Retrieved November 21, 2017.](https://msdn.microsoft.com/library/windows/desktop/ms721766.aspx)

4.  [Metcalf, S. (2015, December 31). Cracking Kerberos TGS Tickets Using Kerberoast  Exploiting Kerberos to Compromise the Active Directory Domain. Retrieved March 22, 2018.](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2293)

Pre-compromise
==============

This category is used for any applicable mitigation activities that apply to techniques occurring before an adversary gains Initial Access, such as Reconnaissance and Resource Development techniques.

ID:M1056

Version:1.0

Created:19 October 2020

Last Modified:20 October 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1056/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**
