Privileged Account Management
=============================

Manage the creation, modification, use, and permissions associated to privileged accounts, including SYSTEM and root.

ID:M1026

Version:1.1

Created:06 June 2019

Last Modified:31 March 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1026/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1548](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

[Abuse Elevation Control Mechanism](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

Remove users from the local administrator group on systems.

By requiring a password, even if an adversary can get terminal access, they must know the password to run anything in the sudoers file. Setting the timestamp\_timeout to 0 will require the user to input their password every time sudo is executed.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/002)

[Bypass User Account Control](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/002)

Remove users from the local administrator group on systems.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/003)

[Sudo and Sudo Caching](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/003)

By requiring a password, even if an adversary can get terminal access, they must know the password to run anything in the sudoers file. Setting the`timestamp_timeout`to 0 will require the user to input their password every time`sudo`is executed.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/006)

[TCC Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/006)

Remove unnecessary users from the local administrator group on systems.

Enterprise

[T1134](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134)

[Access Token Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134)

Limit permissions so that users and user groups cannot create tokens. This setting should be defined for the local system account only. GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > User Rights Assignment: Create a token object.[\[1\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/device-security/security-policy-settings/create-a-token-object)Also define who can create a process level token to only the local and network service through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > User Rights Assignment: Replace a process level token.[\[2\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/device-security/security-policy-settings/replace-a-process-level-token)

Administrators should log in as a standard user but run their tools with administrator privileges using the built-in access token manipulation command`runas`.[\[3\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/bb490994.aspx)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/001)

[Token Impersonation/Theft](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/001)

Limit permissions so that users and user groups cannot create tokens. This setting should be defined for the local system account only. GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > User Rights Assignment: Create a token object.[\[1\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/device-security/security-policy-settings/create-a-token-object)Also define who can create a process level token to only the local and network service through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > User Rights Assignment: Replace a process level token.[\[2\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/device-security/security-policy-settings/replace-a-process-level-token)

Administrators should log in as a standard user but run their tools with administrator privileges using the built-in access token manipulation command`runas`.[\[3\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/bb490994.aspx)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/002)

[Create Process with Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/002)

Limit permissions so that users and user groups cannot create tokens. This setting should be defined for the local system account only. GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > User Rights Assignment: Create a token object.[\[1\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/device-security/security-policy-settings/create-a-token-object)Also define who can create a process level token to only the local and network service through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > User Rights Assignment: Replace a process level token.[\[2\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/device-security/security-policy-settings/replace-a-process-level-token)

Administrators should log in as a standard user but run their tools with administrator privileges using the built-in access token manipulation command`runas`.[\[3\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/bb490994.aspx)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/003)

[Make and Impersonate Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/003)

Limit permissions so that users and user groups cannot create tokens. This setting should be defined for the local system account only. GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > User Rights Assignment: Create a token object.[\[1\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/device-security/security-policy-settings/create-a-token-object)Also define who can create a process level token to only the local and network service through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > User Rights Assignment: Replace a process level token.[\[2\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/device-security/security-policy-settings/replace-a-process-level-token)

Administrators should log in as a standard user but run their tools with administrator privileges using the built-in access token manipulation command`runas`.[\[3\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/bb490994.aspx)

Enterprise

[T1098](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098)

[Account Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098)

Do not allow domain administrator accounts to be used for day-to-day operations that may expose them to potential adversaries on unprivileged systems.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/001)

[Additional Cloud Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/001)

Do not allow domain administrator or root accounts to be used for day-to-day operations that may expose them to potential adversaries on unprivileged systems.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/002)

[Additional Email Delegate Permissions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/002)

Do not allow domain administrator accounts to be used for day-to-day operations that may expose them to potential adversaries on unprivileged systems.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/003)

[Additional Cloud Roles](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/003)

Ensure that all accounts use the least privileges they require. In Azure AD environments, consider using Privileged Identity Management (PIM) to define roles that require two or more approvals before assignment to users.[\[4\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/active-directory/privileged-identity-management/azure-ad-pim-approval-workflow)

Enterprise

[T1547](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/006)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[Kernel Modules and Extensions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/006)

Limit access to the root account and prevent users from loading kernel modules and extensions through proper privilege separation and limiting Privilege Escalation opportunities.

Enterprise

[T1612](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1612)

[Build Image on Host](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1612)

Ensure containers are not running as root by default. In Kubernetes environments, consider defining Pod Security Standards that prevent pods from running privileged containers.[\[5\]](https://media.defense.gov/2022/Aug/29/2003066362/-1/-1/0/CTR_KUBERNETES_HARDENING_GUIDANCE_1.2_20220829.PDF)

Enterprise

[T1651](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1651)

[Cloud Administration Command](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1651)

Limit the number of cloud accounts with permissions to remotely execute commands on virtual machines, and ensure that these are not used for day-to-day operations. In Azure, limit the number of accounts with the roles Azure Virtual Machine Contributer and above, and consider using temporary Just-in-Time (JIT) roles to avoid permanently assigning privileged access to virtual machines.[\[6\]](https://www.mandiant.com/resources/blog/azure-run-command-dummies)

Enterprise

[T1059](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

[Command and Scripting Interpreter](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

When PowerShell is necessary, consider restricting PowerShell execution policy to administrators. Be aware that there are methods of bypassing the PowerShell execution policy, depending on environment configuration.[\[7\]](https://blog.netspi.com/15-ways-to-bypass-the-powershell-execution-policy/)

PowerShell JEA (Just Enough Administration) may also be used to sandbox administration and limit what commands admins/users can execute through remote PowerShell sessions.[\[8\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/powershell/scripting/learn/remoting/jea/overview?view=powershell-7.3)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/001)

[PowerShell](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/001)

When PowerShell is necessary, consider restricting PowerShell execution policy to administrators. Be aware that there are methods of bypassing the PowerShell execution policy, depending on environment configuration.[\[7\]](https://blog.netspi.com/15-ways-to-bypass-the-powershell-execution-policy/)

PowerShell JEA (Just Enough Administration) may also be used to sandbox administration and limit what commands admins/users can execute through remote PowerShell sessions.[\[8\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/powershell/scripting/learn/remoting/jea/overview?view=powershell-7.3)

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/008)

[Network Device CLI](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/008)

Use of Authentication, Authorization, and Accounting (AAA) systems will limit actions administrators can perform and provide a history of user actions to detect unauthorized use and abuse. TACACS+ can keep control over which commands administrators are permitted to use through the configuration of authentication and command authorization[\[9\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#38)[\[10\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#39)

[.009](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/009)

[Cloud API](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/009)

Use of proper Identity and Access Management (IAM) with Role Based Access Control (RBAC) policies to limit actions administrators can perform and provide a history of administrative actions to detect unauthorized use and abuse.

Enterprise

[T1609](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1609)

[Container Administration Command](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1609)

Ensure containers are not running as root by default. In Kubernetes environments, consider defining Pod Security Standards that prevent pods from running privileged containers and using the`NodeRestriction`admission controller to deny the kublet access to nodes and pods outside of the node it belongs to.[\[5\]](https://media.defense.gov/2022/Aug/29/2003066362/-1/-1/0/CTR_KUBERNETES_HARDENING_GUIDANCE_1.2_20220829.PDF)[\[11\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/reference/access-authn-authz/admission-controllers)

[T1555](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555)

[Cloud Secrets Management Stores](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555/006)

Enterprise

[T1559](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559)

[Inter-Process Communication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559)

Modify Registry settings (directly or using Dcomcnfg.exe) in`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Classes\\AppID\\{AppID_GUID}`associated with the process-wide security of individual COM applications.[\[15\]](https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/windows/desktop/ms687317(v=vs.85).aspx)

Modify Registry settings (directly or using Dcomcnfg.exe) in`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\Ole`associated with system-wide security defaults for all COM applications that do no set their own process-wide security.[\[16\]](https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/windows/desktop/ms694331(v=vs.85).aspx)[\[17\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/desktop/com/dcom-security-enhancements-in-windows-xp-service-pack-2-and-windows-server-2003-service-pack-1)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559/001)

[Component Object Model](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559/001)

Modify Registry settings (directly or using Dcomcnfg.exe) in`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Classes\\AppID\\{AppID_GUID}`associated with the process-wide security of individual COM applications.[\[15\]](https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/windows/desktop/ms687317(v=vs.85).aspx)

Modify Registry settings (directly or using Dcomcnfg.exe) in`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\Ole`associated with system-wide security defaults for all COM applications that do no set their own process-wide security.[\[16\]](https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/windows/desktop/ms694331(v=vs.85).aspx)[\[17\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/desktop/com/dcom-security-enhancements-in-windows-xp-service-pack-2-and-windows-server-2003-service-pack-1)

Enterprise

[T1556](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

[Modify Authentication Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

Audit domain and local accounts as well as their permission levels routinely to look for situations that could allow an adversary to gain wide access by obtaining credentials of a privileged account.[\[18\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn535501.aspx)[\[19\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn487450.aspx)These audits should also include if default accounts have been enabled, or if new local accounts are created that have not be authorized. Follow best practices for design and administration of an enterprise network to limit privileged account use across administrative tiers.[\[20\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/identity/securing-privileged-access/securing-privileged-access-reference-material#a-nameesaebmaesae-administrative-forest-design-approach)

Limit access to the root account and prevent users from modifying protected components through proper privilege separation (ex SELinux, grsecurity, AppArmor, etc.) and limiting Privilege Escalation opportunities.

Limit on-premises accounts with access to the hybrid identity solution in place. For example, limit Azure AD Global Administrator accounts to only those required, and ensure that these are dedicated cloud-only accounts rather than hybrid ones.[\[21\]](https://www.microsoft.com/security/blog/2022/08/24/magicweb-nobeliums-post-compromise-trick-to-authenticate-as-anyone/)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/001)

[Domain Controller Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/001)

Audit domain and local accounts as well as their permission levels routinely to look for situations that could allow an adversary to gain wide access by obtaining credentials of a privileged account.[\[18\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn535501.aspx)[\[19\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn487450.aspx)These audits should also include if default accounts have been enabled, or if new local accounts are created that have not be authorized. Follow best practices for design and administration of an enterprise network to limit privileged account use across administrative tiers.[\[20\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/identity/securing-privileged-access/securing-privileged-access-reference-material#a-nameesaebmaesae-administrative-forest-design-approach)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/003)

[Pluggable Authentication Modules](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/003)

Limit access to the root account and prevent users from modifying PAM components through proper privilege separation (ex SELinux, grsecurity, AppArmor, etc.) and limiting Privilege Escalation opportunities.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/004)

[Network Device Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/004)

Restrict administrator accounts to as few individuals as possible, following least privilege principles. Prevent credential overlap across systems of administrator and privileged accounts, particularly between network and non-network platforms, such as servers or endpoints.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/005)

[Reversible Encryption](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/005)

Audit domain and local accounts as well as their permission levels routinely to look for situations that could allow an adversary to gain wide access by obtaining credentials of a privileged account.[\[18\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn535501.aspx)[\[19\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn487450.aspx)These audits should also include if default accounts have been enabled, or if new local accounts are created that have not be authorized. Follow best practices for design and administration of an enterprise network to limit privileged account use across administrative tiers.[\[20\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/identity/securing-privileged-access/securing-privileged-access-reference-material#a-nameesaebmaesae-administrative-forest-design-approach)

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/007)

[Hybrid Identity](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/007)

Limit on-premises accounts with access to the hybrid identity solution in place. For example, limit Azure AD Global Administrator accounts to only those required, and ensure that these are dedicated cloud-only accounts rather than hybrid ones.[\[21\]](https://www.microsoft.com/security/blog/2022/08/24/magicweb-nobeliums-post-compromise-trick-to-authenticate-as-anyone/)

Enterprise

[T1003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

[OS Credential Dumping](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

Windows:Do not put user or admin domain accounts in the local administrator groups across systems unless they are tightly controlled, as this is often equivalent to having a local administrator account with the same password on all systems. Follow best practices for design and administration of an enterprise network to limit privileged account use across administrative tiers.[\[20\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/identity/securing-privileged-access/securing-privileged-access-reference-material#a-nameesaebmaesae-administrative-forest-design-approach)

Linux:Scraping the passwords from memory requires root privileges. Follow best practices in restricting access to privileged accounts to avoid hostile programs from accessing such sensitive regions of memory.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/005)

[TFTP Boot](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/005)

Use of Authentication, Authorization, and Accounting (AAA) systems will limit actions administrators can perform and provide a history of user actions to detect unauthorized use and abuse. TACACS+ can keep control over which commands administrators are permitted to use through the configuration of authentication and command authorization.[\[9\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#38)[\[10\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#39)

Enterprise

[T1055](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1055)

[Process Injection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1055)

Utilize Yama (ex: /proc/sys/kernel/yama/ptrace\_scope) to mitigate ptrace based process injection by restricting the use of ptrace to privileged users only. Other mitigation controls involve the deployment of security kernel modules that provide advanced access control and process restrictions such as SELinux, grsecurity, and AppArmor.

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1055/008)

[Ptrace System Calls](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1055/008)

Utilize Yama (ex: /proc/sys/kernel/yama/ptrace\_scope) to mitigate ptrace based process injection by restricting the use of ptrace to privileged users only. Other mitigation controls involve the deployment of security kernel modules that provide advanced access control and process restrictions such as SELinux, grsecurity, and AppArmor.

[Remote Service Session Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563)

Do not allow remote access to services as a privileged account unless necessary.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/001)

[SSH Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/001)

Do not allow remote access via SSH as root or other privileged accounts.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/002)

[RDP Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/002)

Enterprise

[T1021](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/001)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021):[Remote Desktop Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/001)

Consider removing the local Administrators group from the list of groups allowed to log in through RDP.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/002)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021):[SMB/Windows Admin Shares](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/002)

Deny remote use of local admin credentials to log into systems. Do not allow domain user accounts to be in the local Administrators group multiple systems.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/003)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021):[Distributed Component Object Model](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/003)

Modify Registry settings (directly or using Dcomcnfg.exe) in`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SOFTWARE\Classes\AppID\{{AppID_GUID}}`associated with the process-wide security of individual COM applications.[\[15\]](https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/windows/desktop/ms687317(v=vs.85).aspx)

Modify Registry settings (directly or using Dcomcnfg.exe) in`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Ole`associated with system-wide security defaults for all COM applications that do not set their own process-wide security.[\[16\]](https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/windows/desktop/ms694331(v=vs.85).aspx)[\[17\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/desktop/com/dcom-security-enhancements-in-windows-xp-service-pack-2-and-windows-server-2003-service-pack-1)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/006)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021):[Windows Remote Management](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/006)

If the service is necessary, lock down critical enclaves with separate WinRM accounts and permissions.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/007)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021):[Cloud Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/007)

Limit the number of high-privileged domain and cloud accounts, and ensure that these are not used for day-to-day operations. Ensure that on-premises accounts do not have privileged cloud permissions and that isolated, cloud-only accounts are used for managing cloud environments.[\[23\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/active-directory/fundamentals/protect-m365-from-on-premises-attacks)

Enterprise

[T1053](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053)

[Scheduled Task/Job](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053)

Configure the Increase Scheduling Priority option to only allow the Administrators group the rights to schedule a priority process. This can be can be configured through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > User Rights Assignment: Increase scheduling priority.[\[24\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/dn221960.aspx)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/002)

[At](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/002)

Configure the Increase Scheduling Priority option to only allow the Administrators group the rights to schedule a priority process. This can be configured through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > User Rights Assignment: Increase scheduling priority.[\[24\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/dn221960.aspx)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/005)

[Scheduled Task](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/005)

Configure the Increase Scheduling Priority option to only allow the Administrators group the rights to schedule a priority process. This can be configured through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > User Rights Assignment: Increase scheduling priority.[\[24\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/dn221960.aspx)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/006)

[Systemd Timers](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/006)

Limit access to the root account and prevent users from creating and/or modifying systemd timer unit files.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/007)

[Container Orchestration Job](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/007)

Ensure containers are not running as root by default. In Kubernetes environments, consider defining Pod Security Standards that prevent pods from running privileged containers.[\[5\]](https://media.defense.gov/2022/Aug/29/2003066362/-1/-1/0/CTR_KUBERNETES_HARDENING_GUIDANCE_1.2_20220829.PDF)

[T1552](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

[Unsecured Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

If it is necessary that software must store credentials in the Registry, then ensure the associated accounts have limited permissions so they cannot be abused if obtained by an adversary.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/002)

[Credentials in Registry](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/002)

If it is necessary that software must store credentials in the Registry, then ensure the associated accounts have limited permissions so they cannot be abused if obtained by an adversary.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/007)

[Container API](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/007)

Use the principle of least privilege for privileged accounts such as the service account in Kubernetes. For example, if a pod is not required to access the Kubernetes API, consider disabling the service account altogether.[\[26\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/tasks/configure-pod-container/configure-service-account/)

Enterprise

[T1078](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

[Valid Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

Audit domain and local accounts as well as their permission levels routinely to look for situations that could allow an adversary to gain wide access by obtaining credentials of a privileged account.[\[18\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn535501.aspx)[\[19\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn487450.aspx)These audits should also include if default accounts have been enabled, or if new local accounts are created that have not be authorized. Follow best practices for design and administration of an enterprise network to limit privileged account use across administrative tiers.[\[20\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/identity/securing-privileged-access/securing-privileged-access-reference-material#a-nameesaebmaesae-administrative-forest-design-approach)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/002)

[Domain Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/002)

Audit domain account permission levels routinely to look for situations that could allow an adversary to gain wide access by obtaining credentials of a privileged account. Do not put user or admin domain accounts in the local administrator groups across systems unless they are tightly controlled and use of accounts is segmented, as this is often equivalent to having a local administrator account with the same password on all systems. Follow best practices for design and administration of an enterprise network to limit privileged account use across administrative tiers. Limit credential overlap across systems to prevent access if account credentials are obtained.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/003)

[Local Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/003)

Audit local accounts permission levels routinely to look for situations that could allow an adversary to gain wide access by obtaining credentials of a privileged account.[\[18\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn535501.aspx)[\[19\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn487450.aspx)Limit the usage of local administrator accounts to be used for day-to-day operations that may expose them to potential adversaries.

For example, audit the use of service accounts in Kubernetes, and avoid automatically granting them access to the Kubernetes API if this is not required.[\[26\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/tasks/configure-pod-container/configure-service-account/)Implementing LAPS may also help prevent reuse of local administrator credentials across a domain.[\[28\]](https://blogs.technet.microsoft.com/secguide/2018/12/10/remote-use-of-local-accounts-laps-changes-everything/)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/004)

[Cloud Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/004)

Review privileged cloud account permission levels routinely to look for those that could allow an adversary to gain wide access, such as Global Administrator and Privileged Role Administrator in Azure AD.[\[18\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn535501.aspx)[\[19\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn487450.aspx)[\[29\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/security/benchmark/azure/baselines/aad-security-baseline)These reviews should also check if new privileged cloud accounts have been created that were not authorized. For example, in Azure AD environments configure alerts to notify when accounts have gone many days without using privileged roles, as these roles may be able to be removed.[\[30\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/security/benchmark/azure/baselines/aad-security-baseline)Consider using temporary, just-in-time (JIT) privileged access to Azure AD resources rather than permanently assigning privileged roles.[\[29\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/security/benchmark/azure/baselines/aad-security-baseline)

Enterprise

[T1047](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1047)

[Windows Management Instrumentation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1047)

Prevent credential overlap across systems of administrator and privileged accounts.[\[12\]](https://www.fireeye.com/content/dam/fireeye-www/global/en/current-threats/pdfs/wp-windows-management-instrumentation.pdf)

Privileged Process Integrity
============================

Protect processes with high privileges that can be used to interact with critical system components through use of protected process light, anti-process injection defenses, or other process integrity enforcement measures.

ID:M1025

Version:1.1

Created:06 June 2019

Last Modified:20 May 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1025/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1547](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/002)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[Authentication Package](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/002)

Windows 8.1, Windows Server 2012 R2, and later versions, may make LSA run as a Protected Process Light (PPL) by setting the Registry key`HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\Lsa\RunAsPPL`, which requires all DLLs loaded by LSA to be signed by Microsoft.[\[1\]](http://docplayer.net/20839173-Analysis-of-malicious-security-support-provider-dlls.html)[\[2\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn408187.aspx)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/005)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[Security Support Provider](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/005)

Windows 8.1, Windows Server 2012 R2, and later versions may make LSA run as a Protected Process Light (PPL) by setting the Registry key`HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\Lsa\RunAsPPL`, which requires all SSP DLLs to be signed by Microsoft.[\[1\]](http://docplayer.net/20839173-Analysis-of-malicious-security-support-provider-dlls.html)[\[2\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn408187.aspx)

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/008)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[LSASS Driver](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/008)

On Windows 8.1 and Server 2012 R2, enable LSA Protection by setting the Registry key`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\Lsa\RunAsPPL`to`dword:00000001`.[\[3\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/dn408187.aspx)LSA Protection ensures that LSA plug-ins and drivers are only loaded if they are digitally signed with a Microsoft signature and adhere to the Microsoft Security Development Lifecycle (SDL) process guidance.

Enterprise

[T1556](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

[Modify Authentication Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

Enabled features, such as Protected Process Light (PPL), for LSA.[\[4\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn408187.aspx)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/001)

[Domain Controller Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/001)

Enabled features, such as Protected Process Light (PPL), for LSA.[\[4\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn408187.aspx)

Enterprise

[T1003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

[OS Credential Dumping](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

On Windows 8.1 and Windows Server 2012 R2, enable Protected Process Light for LSA.[\[4\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn408187.aspx)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/001)

[LSASS Memory](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/001)

On Windows 8.1 and Windows Server 2012 R2, enable Protected Process Light for LSA.[\[4\]](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn408187.aspx)

**References**
--------------

1.  [Graeber, M. (2014, October). Analysis of Malicious Security Support Provider DLLs. Retrieved March 1, 2017.](http://docplayer.net/20839173-Analysis-of-malicious-security-support-provider-dlls.html)
2.  [Microsoft. (2013, July 31). Configuring Additional LSA Protection. Retrieved June 24, 2015.](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn408187.aspx)

3.  [Microsoft. (2014, March 12). Configuring Additional LSA Protection. Retrieved November 27, 2017.](https://technet.microsoft.com/library/dn408187.aspx)
4.  [Microsoft. (2013, July 31). Configuring Additional LSA Protection. Retrieved February 13, 2015.](https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn408187.aspx)

Remote Data Storage
===================

Use remote security log and sensitive file storage where access can be controlled better to prevent exposure of intrusion detection log data or sensitive information.

ID:M1029

Version:1.0

Created:06 June 2019

Last Modified:06 June 2019

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1029/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1119](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1119)

[Automated Collection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1119)

Encryption and off-system storage of sensitive information may be one way to mitigate collection of files, but may not stop an adversary from acquiring the information if an intrusion persists over a long period of time and the adversary is able to discover and access the data through other means.

Enterprise

[T1565](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565)

[Data Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565)

Consider implementing IT disaster recovery plans that contain procedures for taking regular data backups that can be used to restore organizational data.[\[1\]](https://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/IT)Ensure backups are stored off system and is protected from common methods adversaries may use to gain access and manipulate backups.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565/001)

[Stored Data Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565/001)

Consider implementing IT disaster recovery plans that contain procedures for taking regular data backups that can be used to restore organizational data.[\[1\]](https://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/IT)Ensure backups are stored off system and is protected from common methods adversaries may use to gain access and manipulate backups.

Enterprise

[T1070](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070)

[Indicator Removal](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070)

Automatically forward events to a log server or data repository to prevent conditions in which the adversary can locate and manipulate data on the local system. When possible, minimize time delay on event reporting to avoid prolonged storage on the local system.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/001)

[Clear Windows Event Logs](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/001)

Automatically forward events to a log server or data repository to prevent conditions in which the adversary can locate and manipulate data on the local system. When possible, minimize time delay on event reporting to avoid prolonged storage on the local system.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/002)

[Clear Linux or Mac System Logs](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/002)

Automatically forward events to a log server or data repository to prevent conditions in which the adversary can locate and manipulate data on the local system. When possible, minimize time delay on event reporting to avoid prolonged storage on the local system.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/003)

[Clear Command History](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/003)

Forward logging of historical data to remote data store and centralized logging solution to preserve historical command line log data.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/007)

[Clear Network Connection History and Configurations](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/007)

Automatically forward events to a log server or data repository to prevent conditions in which the adversary can locate and manipulate data on the local system. When possible, minimize time delay on event reporting to avoid prolonged storage on the local system.

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/008)

[Clear Mailbox Data](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/008)

Automatically forward mail data and events to a log server or data repository to prevent conditions in which the adversary can locate and manipulate data on the local system. When possible, minimize time delay on event reporting to avoid prolonged storage on the local system.

[.009](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/009)

[Clear Persistence](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/009)

Automatically forward events to a log server or data repository to prevent conditions in which the adversary can locate and manipulate data on the local system. When possible, minimize time delay on event reporting to avoid prolonged storage on the local system.

Enterprise

[T1072](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

[Software Deployment Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

If the application deployment system can be configured to deploy only signed binaries, then ensure that the trusted signing certificates are not co-located with the application deployment system and are instead located on a system that cannot be accessed remotely or to which remote access is tightly controlled.

**References**
--------------

1.  [Ready.gov. (n.d.). IT Disaster Recovery Plan. Retrieved March 15, 2019.](https://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/IT)

Restrict File and Directory Permissions
=======================================

Restrict access by setting directory and file permissions that are not specific to users or privileged accounts.

ID:M1022

Version:1.1

Created:06 June 2019

Last Modified:20 May 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1022/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1548](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

[Abuse Elevation Control Mechanism](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

The sudoers file should be strictly edited such that passwords are always required and that users can't spawn risky processes as users with higher privilege.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/003)

[Sudo and Sudo Caching](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/003)

The sudoers file should be strictly edited such that passwords are always required and that users can't spawn risky processes as users with higher privilege.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/006)

[TCC Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/006)

When using an MDM, ensure the permissions granted are specific to the requirements of the binary. Full Disk Access should be restricted to only necessary binaries in alignment with policy.

Enterprise

[T1098](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/004)

[Account Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098):[SSH Authorized Keys](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/004)

Restrict access to the`authorized_keys`file.

Enterprise

[T1547](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/003)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[Time Providers](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/003)

Consider using Group Policy to configure and block additions/modifications to W32Time DLLs.[\[1\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows-server/networking/windows-time-service/windows-time-service-tools-and-settings)

[.013](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/013)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[XDG Autostart Entries](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/013)

Restrict write access to XDG autostart entries to only select privileged users.

Enterprise

[T1037](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1037)

[Boot or Logon Initialization Scripts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1037)

Restrict write access to logon scripts to specific administrators.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1037/002)

[Login Hook](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1037/002)

Restrict write access to logon scripts to specific administrators.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1037/003)

[Network Logon Script](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1037/003)

Restrict write access to logon scripts to specific administrators.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1037/004)

[RC Scripts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1037/004)

Limit privileges of user accounts so only authorized users can edit the rc.common file.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1037/005)

[Startup Items](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1037/005)

Since StartupItems are deprecated, preventing all users from writing to the`/Library/StartupItems`directory would prevent any startup items from getting registered.

Enterprise

[T1543](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543)

[Create or Modify System Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543)

Restrict read/write access to system-level process files to only select privileged users who have a legitimate need to manage system services.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/001)

[Launch Agent](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/001)

Set group policies to restrict file permissions to the`~/launchagents`folder.[\[2\]](https://antman1p-30185.medium.com/defeating-malicious-launch-persistence-156e2b40fc67)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/002)

[Systemd Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/002)

Restrict read/write access to systemd unit files to only select privileged users who have a legitimate need to manage system services.

Enterprise

[T1530](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1530)

[Data from Cloud Storage](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1530)

Use access control lists on storage systems and objects.

Enterprise

[T1565](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565)

[Data Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565)

Ensure least privilege principles are applied to important information resources to reduce exposure to data manipulation risk.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565/001)

[Stored Data Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565/001)

Ensure least privilege principles are applied to important information resources to reduce exposure to data manipulation risk.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565/003)

[Runtime Data Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1565/003)

Prevent critical business and system processes from being replaced, overwritten, or reconfigured to load potentially malicious code.

Enterprise

[T1546](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/004)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546):[Unix Shell Configuration Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/004)

Making these files immutable and only changeable by certain administrators will limit the ability for adversaries to easily create user level persistence.

[.013](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/013)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546):[PowerShell Profile](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/013)

Making PowerShell profiles immutable and only changeable by certain administrators will limit the ability for adversaries to easily create user level persistence.

Enterprise

[T1048](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048)

[Exfiltration Over Alternative Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048)

Use access control lists on cloud storage systems and objects.

Enterprise

[T1222](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1222)

[File and Directory Permissions Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1222)

Applying more restrictive permissions to files and directories could prevent adversaries from modifying their access control lists. Additionally, ensure that user settings regarding local and remote symbolic links are properly set or disabled where unneeded.[\[3\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/threat-protection/security-policy-settings/create-symbolic-links)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1222/001)

[Windows File and Directory Permissions Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1222/001)

Applying more restrictive permissions to files and directories could prevent adversaries from modifying the access control lists.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1222/002)

[Linux and Mac File and Directory Permissions Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1222/002)

Applying more restrictive permissions to files and directories could prevent adversaries from modifying the access control lists.

Enterprise

[T1564](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/004)

[Hide Artifacts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564):[NTFS File Attributes](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/004)

Consider adjusting read and write permissions for NTFS EA, though this should be tested to ensure routine OS operations are not impeded.[\[4\]](https://blog.stealthbits.com/attack-step-3-persistence-ntfs-extended-attributes-file-system-attacks)

Enterprise

[T1574](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

[Hijack Execution Flow](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

Install software in write-protected locations. Set directory access controls to prevent file writes to the search paths for applications, both in the folders where applications are run from and the standard library folders.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/004)

[Dylib Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/004)

Set directory access controls to prevent file writes to the search paths for applications, both in the folders where applications are run from and the standard dylib folders.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/007)

[Path Interception by PATH Environment Variable](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/007)

Ensure that proper permissions and directory access control are set to deny users the ability to write files to the top-level directory`C:`and system directories, such as`C:\Windows\`, to reduce places where malicious files could be placed for execution. Require that all executables be placed in write-protected directories.

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/008)

[Path Interception by Search Order Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/008)

Ensure that proper permissions and directory access control are set to deny users the ability to write files to the top-level directory`C:`and system directories, such as`C:\Windows\`, to reduce places where malicious files could be placed for execution. Require that all executables be placed in write-protected directories.

[.009](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/009)

[Path Interception by Unquoted Path](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/009)

Ensure that proper permissions and directory access control are set to deny users the ability to write files to the top-level directory`C:`and system directories, such as`C:\Windows\`, to reduce places where malicious files could be placed for execution. Require that all executables be placed in write-protected directories.

[.014](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/014)

[AppDomainManager](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/014)

Install .NET applications and related software in write-protected locations. Set directory access controls to prevent file writes to the search paths for .NET applications, both in the folders where applications are run from and the standard resources folders.

Enterprise

[T1562](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562)

[Impair Defenses](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562)

Ensure proper process and file permissions are in place to prevent adversaries from disabling or interfering with security/logging services.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/001)

[Disable or Modify Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/001)

Ensure proper process and file permissions are in place to prevent adversaries from disabling or interfering with security services.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/002)

[Disable Windows Event Logging](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/002)

Ensure proper process and file permissions are in place to prevent adversaries from disabling or interfering with logging or deleting or modifying .evtx logging files. Ensure .evtx files, which are located at`C:\Windows\system32\Winevt\Logs`[\[5\]](https://forensicswiki.xyz/wiki/index.php?title=Windows_XML_Event_Log_(EVTX)), have the proper file permissions for limited, legitimate access and audit policies for detection.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/004)

[Disable or Modify System Firewall](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/004)

Ensure proper process and file permissions are in place to prevent adversaries from disabling or modifying firewall settings.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/006)

[Indicator Blocking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/006)

Ensure event tracers/forwarders[\[6\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/desktop/etw/event-tracing-portal), firewall policies, and other associated mechanisms are secured with appropriate permissions and access controls.

Enterprise

[T1070](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/002)

Protect generated event files that are stored locally with proper permissions and authentication and limit opportunities for adversaries to increase privileges by preventing Privilege Escalation opportunities.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/003)

[Clear Command History](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/003)

Preventing users from deleting or writing to certain files can stop adversaries from maliciously altering their`~/.bash_history`or`ConsoleHost_history.txt`files.

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/008)

[Clear Mailbox Data](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/008)

Protect generated event files that are stored locally with proper permissions and authentication and limit opportunities for adversaries to increase privileges by preventing Privilege Escalation opportunities.

Protect generated event files that are stored locally with proper permissions and authentication and limit opportunities for adversaries to increase privileges by preventing Privilege Escalation opportunities.

Enterprise

[T1036](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036)

[Masquerading](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036)

Use file system access controls to protect folders such as C:\\Windows\\System32.

Enterprise

[T1556](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

[Modify Authentication Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

Restrict write access to the`/Library/Security/SecurityAgentPlugins`directory.

Enterprise

[T1055](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1055)

[.009](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1055/009)

[Process Injection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1055):[Proc Memory](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1055/009)

Restrict the permissions on sensitive files such as`/proc/[pid]/maps`or`/proc/[pid]/mem`.

Enterprise

[T1563](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/001)

[Remote Service Session Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563):[SSH Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/001)

Ensure proper file permissions are set and harden system to prevent root privilege escalation opportunities.

Enterprise

[T1053](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053)

[Scheduled Task/Job](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053)

Restrict access by setting directory and file permissions that are not specific to users or privileged accounts.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/006)

[Systemd Timers](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/006)

Restrict read/write access to systemd`.timer`unit files to only select privileged users who have a legitimate need to manage system services.

Enterprise

[T1489](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1489)

[Service Stop](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1489)

Ensure proper process and file permissions are in place to inhibit adversaries from disabling or interfering with critical services.

Enterprise

[T1553](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/003)

[Subvert Trust Controls](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553):[SIP and Trust Provider Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/003)

Restrict storage and execution of SIP DLLs to protected directories, such as C:\\Windows, rather than user directories.

Enterprise

[T1218](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/002)

[System Binary Proxy Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218):[Control Panel](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/002)

Restrict storage and execution of Control Panel items to protected directories, such as`C:\Windows`, rather than user directories.

Enterprise

[T1569](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1569)

[System Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1569)

Ensure that high permission level service binaries cannot be replaced or modified by users with a lower permission level.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1569/002)

[Service Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1569/002)

Ensure that high permission level service binaries cannot be replaced or modified by users with a lower permission level.

Enterprise

[T1080](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1080)

[Taint Shared Content](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1080)

Protect shared folders by minimizing users who have write access.

Enterprise

[T1552](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

[Unsecured Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

Restrict file shares to specific directories with access only to necessary users.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/001)

[Credentials In Files](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/001)

Restrict file shares to specific directories with access only to necessary users.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/004)

[Private Keys](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/004)

Ensure permissions are properly set on folders containing sensitive private keys to prevent unintended access. Additionally, on Cisco devices, set the`nonexportable`flag during RSA key pair generation.[\[7\]](https://www.cisco.com/c/en/us/td/docs/ios-xml/ios/sec_conn_pki/configuration/xe-17/sec-pki-xe-17-book/sec-deploy-rsa-pki.html#GUID-1CB802D8-9DE3-447F-BECE-CF22F5E11436)

Restrict Library Loading
========================

Prevent abuse of library loading mechanisms in the operating system and software to load untrusted code by configuring appropriate library loading mechanisms and investigating potential vulnerable software.

ID:M1044

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:11 June 2019

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1044/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1547](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547)

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/008)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[LSASS Driver](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/008)

Ensure safe DLL search mode is enabled`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\System\CurrentControlSet\Control\Session Manager\SafeDllSearchMode`to mitigate risk that lsass.exe loads a malicious code library.[\[1\]](https://msdn.microsoft.com/library/windows/desktop/ff919712.aspx)

Enterprise

[T1574](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

[Hijack Execution Flow](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

Disallow loading of remote DLLs. This is included by default in Windows Server 2012+ and is available by patch for XP+ and Server 2003+.

Enable Safe DLL Search Mode to force search for system DLLs in directories with greater restrictions (e.g.`%SYSTEMROOT%)to` be used before local directory DLLs (e.g. a user's home directory)

The Safe DLL Search Mode can be enabled via Group Policy at Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Administrative Templates > MSS (Legacy): MSS: (SafeDllSearchMode) Enable Safe DLL search mode. The associated Windows Registry key for this is located at`HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\Session Manager\SafeDLLSearchMode`[\[2\]](https://msrc-blog.microsoft.com/2010/08/23/more-information-about-the-dll-preloading-remote-attack-vector/)[\[3\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/dlls/dynamic-link-library-search-order?redirectedfrom=MSDN)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/001)

[DLL Search Order Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/001)

Disallow loading of remote DLLs. This is included by default in Windows Server 2012+ and is available by patch for XP+ and Server 2003+.

Enable Safe DLL Search Mode to force search for system DLLs in directories with greater restrictions (e.g.`%SYSTEMROOT%)to` be used before local directory DLLs (e.g. a user's home directory)

The Safe DLL Search Mode can be enabled via Group Policy at Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Administrative Templates > MSS (Legacy): MSS: (SafeDllSearchMode) Enable Safe DLL search mode. The associated Windows Registry key for this is located at`HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\Session Manager\SafeDLLSearchMode`[\[2\]](https://msrc-blog.microsoft.com/2010/08/23/more-information-about-the-dll-preloading-remote-attack-vector/)[\[3\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/dlls/dynamic-link-library-search-order?redirectedfrom=MSDN)

**References**
--------------

1.  [Microsoft. (n.d.). Dynamic-Link Library Security. Retrieved November 27, 2017.](https://msdn.microsoft.com/library/windows/desktop/ff919712.aspx)
2.  [Microsoft. (2010, August 12). More information about the DLL Preloading remote attack vector. Retrieved December 5, 2014.](https://msrc-blog.microsoft.com/2010/08/23/more-information-about-the-dll-preloading-remote-attack-vector/)

3.  [Microsoft. (2018, May 31). Dynamic-Link Library Search Order. Retrieved November 30, 2014.](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/dlls/dynamic-link-library-search-order?redirectedfrom=MSDN)

Restrict Registry Permissions
=============================

Restrict the ability to modify certain hives or keys in the Windows Registry.

ID:M1024

Version:1.1

Created:06 June 2019

Last Modified:31 March 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1024/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1547](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/003)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[Time Providers](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/003)

Consider using Group Policy to configure and block modifications to W32Time parameters in the Registry.[\[1\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows-server/networking/windows-time-service/windows-time-service-tools-and-settings)

Enterprise

[T1037](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1037)

Enterprise

Ensure proper permissions are set for Registry hives to prevent users from modifying keys for system components that may lead to privilege escalation.

[Disable or Modify Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/001)

Ensure proper Registry permissions are in place to prevent adversaries from disabling or interfering with security services.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/002)

[Disable Windows Event Logging](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/002)

Ensure proper Registry permissions are in place to prevent adversaries from disabling or interfering logging. The addition of the MiniNT registry key disables Event Viewer.[\[2\]](https://www.hackingarticles.in/defense-evasion-windows-event-logging-t1562-002/)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/004)

[Indicator Removal](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070):[Clear Network Connection History and Configurations](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1070/007)

Protect generated event files and logs that are stored locally with proper permissions and authentication and limit opportunities for adversaries to increase privileges by preventing Privilege Escalation opportunities.

Enterprise

[T1556](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

[Modify Authentication Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

Restrict Registry permissions to disallow the modification of sensitive Registry keys such as`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\NetworkProvider\Order`.

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/008)

[Network Provider DLL](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/008)

Restrict Registry permissions to disallow the modification of sensitive Registry keys such as`HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\NetworkProvider\Order`.

Enterprise

[T1112](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1112)

[Modify Registry](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1112)

Ensure proper permissions are set for Registry hives to prevent users from modifying keys for system components that may lead to privilege escalation.

Enterprise

[T1505](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505)

[Server Software Component](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505)

Consider using Group Policy to configure and block modifications to service and other critical server parameters in the Registry.[\[3\]](https://social.technet.microsoft.com/wiki/contents/articles/12229.windows-system-services-fundamentals.aspx)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505/005)

[Terminal Services DLL](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505/005)

Consider using Group Policy to configure and block modifications to Terminal Services parameters in the Registry.[\[3\]](https://social.technet.microsoft.com/wiki/contents/articles/12229.windows-system-services-fundamentals.aspx)

Enterprise

[T1489](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1489)

[Service Stop](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1489)

Ensure proper registry permissions are in place to inhibit adversaries from disabling or interfering with critical services.

Enterprise

[T1553](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553)

[Subvert Trust Controls](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553)

Ensure proper permissions are set for Registry hives to prevent users from modifying keys related to SIP and trust provider components. Components may still be able to be hijacked to suitable functions already present on disk if malicious modifications to Registry keys are not prevented.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/003)

[SIP and Trust Provider Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/003)

Ensure proper permissions are set for Registry hives to prevent users from modifying keys related to SIP and trust provider components. Components may still be able to be hijacked to suitable functions already present on disk if malicious modifications to Registry keys are not prevented.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/006)

[Code Signing Policy Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/006)

Ensure proper permissions are set for the Registry to prevent users from modifying keys related to code signing policies.

Restrict Web-Based Content
==========================

Restrict use of certain websites, block downloads/attachments, block Javascript, restrict browser extensions, etc.

ID:M1021

Version:1.0

Created:06 June 2019

Last Modified:06 June 2019

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1021/)

**ATT&CK****Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1059](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

[Command and Scripting Interpreter](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

Script blocking extensions can help prevent the execution of scripts and HTA files that may commonly be used during the exploitation process. For malicious code served up through ads, adblockers can help prevent that code from executing in the first place.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/005)

[Visual Basic](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/005)

Script blocking extensions can help prevent the execution of scripts and HTA files that may commonly be used during the exploitation process. For malicious code served up through ads, adblockers can help prevent that code from executing in the first place.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/007)

[JavaScript](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/007)

Script blocking extensions can help prevent the execution of JavaScript and HTA files that may commonly be used during the exploitation process. For malicious code served up through ads, adblockers can help prevent that code from executing in the first place.

Enterprise

[T1659](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1659)

[Content Injection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1659)

Consider blocking download/transfer and execution of potentially uncommon file types known to be used in adversary campaigns.

Enterprise

[T1189](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1189)

[Drive-by Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1189)

For malicious code served up through ads, adblockers can help prevent that code from executing in the first place.

Script blocking extensions can help prevent the execution of JavaScript that may commonly be used during the exploitation process.

Enterprise

[T1568](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1568)

[Dynamic Resolution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1568)

In some cases a local DNS sinkhole may be used to help prevent behaviors associated with dynamic resolution.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1568/002)

[Domain Generation Algorithms](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1568/002)

In some cases a local DNS sinkhole may be used to help prevent DGA-based command and control at a reduced cost.

Enterprise

[T1567](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567)

[Exfiltration Over Web Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567)

Web proxies can be used to enforce an external network communication policy that prevents use of unauthorized external services.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567/001)

[Exfiltration to Code Repository](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567/001)

Web proxies can be used to enforce an external network communication policy that prevents use of unauthorized external services.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567/002)

[Exfiltration to Cloud Storage](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567/002)

Web proxies can be used to enforce an external network communication policy that prevents use of unauthorized external services.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567/003)

[Exfiltration to Text Storage Sites](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567/003)

Web proxies can be used to enforce an external network communication policy that prevents use of unauthorized external services.

Enterprise

[T1566](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566)

[Phishing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566)

Determine if certain websites or attachment types (ex: .scr, .exe, .pif, .cpl, etc.) that can be used for phishing are necessary for business operations and consider blocking access if activity cannot be monitored well or if it poses a significant risk.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/001)

[Spearphishing Attachment](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/001)

Block unknown or unused attachments by default that should not be transmitted over email as a best practice to prevent some vectors, such as .scr, .exe, .pif, .cpl, etc. Some email scanning devices can open and analyze compressed and encrypted formats, such as zip and rar that may be used to conceal malicious attachments.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/002)

[Spearphishing Link](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/002)

Determine if certain websites that can be used for spearphishing are necessary for business operations and consider blocking access if activity cannot be monitored well or if it poses a significant risk.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/003)

[Spearphishing via Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/003)

Determine if certain social media sites, personal webmail services, or other service that can be used for spearphishing is necessary for business operations and consider blocking access if activity cannot be monitored well or if it poses a significant risk.

Enterprise

[T1528](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1528)

[Steal Application Access Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1528)

Administrators can block end-user consent to OAuth applications, disabling users from authorizing third-party apps through OAuth 2.0 and forcing administrative consent for all requests. They can also block end-user registration of applications by their users, to reduce risk. A Cloud Access Security Broker can also be used to ban applications.

Azure offers a couple of enterprise policy settings in the Azure Management Portal that may help:

"Users -> User settings -> App registrations: Users can register applications" can be set to "no" to prevent users from registering new applications. "Enterprise applications -> User settings -> Enterprise applications: Users can consent to apps accessing company data on their behalf" can be set to "no" to prevent users from consenting to allow third-party multi-tenant applications

Enterprise

[T1218](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218)

[System Binary Proxy Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218)

Restrict use of certain websites, block downloads/attachments, block Javascript, restrict browser extensions, etc.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/001)

[Compiled HTML File](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/001)

Consider blocking download/transfer and execution of potentially uncommon file types known to be used in adversary campaigns, such as CHM files

Enterprise

[T1550](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/001)

[Use Alternate Authentication Material](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550):[Application Access Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/001)

Update corporate policies to restrict what types of third-party applications may be added to any online service or tool that is linked to the company's information, accounts or network (e.g., Google, Microsoft, Dropbox, Basecamp, GitHub). However, rather than providing high-level guidance on this, be extremely specificinclude a list of per-approved applications and deny all others not on the list. Administrators may also block end-user consent through administrative portals, such as the Azure Portal, disabling users from authorizing third-party apps through OAuth and forcing administrative consent.[\[1\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/security/fundamentals/steps-secure-identity#block-end-user-consent)

Enterprise

[T1204](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204)

[User Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204)

If a link is being visited by a user, block unknown or unused files in transit by default that should not be downloaded or by policy from suspicious sites as a best practice to prevent some vectors, such as .scr, .exe, .pif, .cpl, etc. Some download scanning devices can open and analyze compressed and encrypted formats, such as zip and rar that may be used to conceal malicious files.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/001)

[Malicious Link](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/001)

If a link is being visited by a user, block unknown or unused files in transit by default that should not be downloaded or by policy from suspicious sites as a best practice to prevent some vectors, such as .scr, .exe, .pif, .cpl, etc. Some download scanning devices can open and analyze compressed and encrypted formats, such as zip and rar that may be used to conceal malicious files.

Enterprise

[T1102](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1102)

[Web Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1102)

Web proxies can be used to enforce external network communication policy that prevents use of unauthorized external services.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1102/001)

[Dead Drop Resolver](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1102/001)

Web proxies can be used to enforce external network communication policy that prevents use of unauthorized external services.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1102/002)

[Bidirectional Communication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1102/002)

Web proxies can be used to enforce external network communication policy that prevents use of unauthorized external services.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1102/003)

[One-Way Communication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1102/003)

Web proxies can be used to enforce external network communication policy that prevents use of unauthorized external services.
