Software Configuration
======================

Implement configuration changes to software (other than the operating system) to mitigate security risks associated to how the software operates.

ID:M1054

Version:1.2

Created:19 July 2019

Last Modified:26 December 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1054/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1543](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543)

[Create or Modify System Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543)

Where possible, consider enforcing the use of container services in rootless mode to limit the possibility of privilege escalation or malicious effects on the host running the container.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/005)

[Container Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/005)

Where possible, consider enforcing the use of container services in rootless mode to limit the possibility of privilege escalation or malicious effects on the host running the container.

Enterprise

[T1555](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555/005)

[Credentials from Password Stores](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555):[Password Managers](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555/005)

Consider re-locking password managers after a short timeout to limit the time plaintext credentials live in memory from decrypted databases.

Enterprise

[T1602](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602)

[Data from Configuration Repository](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602)

Allowlist MIB objects and implement SNMP views.[\[1\]](https://www.cisco.com/c/en/us/support/docs/ip/simple-network-management-protocol-snmp/20370-snmpsecurity-20370.html)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/001)

[SNMP (MIB Dump)](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/001)

Allowlist MIB objects and implement SNMP views.[\[1\]](https://www.cisco.com/c/en/us/support/docs/ip/simple-network-management-protocol-snmp/20370-snmpsecurity-20370.html)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/002)

[Network Device Configuration Dump](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/002)

Allowlist MIB objects and implement SNMP views. Disable Smart Install (SMI) if not used.[\[1\]](https://www.cisco.com/c/en/us/support/docs/ip/simple-network-management-protocol-snmp/20370-snmpsecurity-20370.html)[\[2\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/TA18-106A)

Enterprise

[T1546](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546)

[.013](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/013)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546):[PowerShell Profile](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/013)

Avoid PowerShell profiles if not needed. Use the -No Profile flag with when executing PowerShell scripts remotely to prevent local profiles and scripts from being executed.

Enterprise

[T1606](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606)

[Forge Web Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606)

Configure browsers/applications to regularly delete persistent web credentials (such as cookies).

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606/001)

[Web Cookies](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606/001)

Configure browsers/applications to regularly delete persistent web cookies.

Enterprise

[T1562](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562)

[Impair Defenses](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562)

Consider implementing policies on internal web servers, such HTTP Strict Transport Security, that enforce the use of HTTPS/network traffic encryption to prevent insecure connections.[\[3\]](https://www.chromium.org/hsts/)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/006)

[Indicator Blocking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/006)

Consider automatically relaunching forwarding mechanisms at recurring intervals (ex: temporal, on-logon, etc.) as well as applying appropriate change management to firewall rules and other related system configurations.

[.009](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/009)

[Safe Mode Boot](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/009)

Ensure that endpoint defenses run in safe mode.[\[4\]](https://www.cyberark.com/resources/blog/cyberark-labs-from-safe-mode-to-domain-compromise)

[.010](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/010)

[Downgrade Attack](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/010)

Consider implementing policies on internal web servers, such HTTP Strict Transport Security, that enforce the use of HTTPS/network traffic encryption to prevent insecure connections.[\[3\]](https://www.chromium.org/hsts/)

Enterprise

[T1559](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559)

[Inter-Process Communication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559)

Consider disabling embedded files in Office programs, such as OneNote, that do not work with Protected View.[\[5\]](https://posts.specterops.io/reviving-dde-using-onenote-and-excel-for-code-execution-d7226864caee)[\[6\]](https://gist.github.com/wdormann/732bb88d9b5dd5a66c9f1e1498f31a1b)

Enterprise

[T1137](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137)

[Office Application Startup](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137)

For the Office Test method, create the Registry key used to execute it and set the permissions to "Read Control" to prevent easy access to the key without administrator permissions or requiring Privilege Escalation.[\[7\]](https://researchcenter.paloaltonetworks.com/2016/07/unit42-technical-walkthrough-office-test-persistence-method-used-in-recent-sofacy-attacks/)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137/002)

[Office Test](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137/002)

Enterprise

[T1566](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566)

[Phishing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566)

Use anti-spoofing and email authentication mechanisms to filter messages based on validity checks of the sender domain (using SPF) and integrity of messages (using DKIM). Enabling these mechanisms within an organization (through policies such as DMARC) may enable recipients (intra-org and cross domain) to perform similar message filtering and validation.[\[8\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365/security/office-365-security/anti-spoofing-protection?view=o365-worldwide)[\[9\]](https://www.cyber.gov.au/sites/default/files/2019-03/spoof_email_sender_policy_framework.pdf)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/001)

[Spearphishing Attachment](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/001)

Enabling these mechanisms within an organization (through policies such as DMARC) may enable recipients (intra-org and cross domain) to perform similar message filtering and validation.[\[8\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365/security/office-365-security/anti-spoofing-protection?view=o365-worldwide)[\[9\]](https://www.cyber.gov.au/sites/default/files/2019-03/spoof_email_sender_policy_framework.pdf)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/002)

[Spearphishing Link](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/002)

Use anti-spoofing and email authentication mechanisms to filter messages based on validity checks of the sender domain (using SPF) and integrity of messages (using DKIM). Enabling these mechanisms within an organization (through policies such as DMARC) may enable recipients (intra-org and cross domain) to perform similar message filtering and validation.[\[8\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365/security/office-365-security/anti-spoofing-protection?view=o365-worldwide)[\[9\]](https://www.cyber.gov.au/sites/default/files/2019-03/spoof_email_sender_policy_framework.pdf).

[Spearphishing Link](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1598/003)

Use anti-spoofing and email authentication mechanisms to filter messages based on validity checks of the sender domain (using SPF) and integrity of messages (using DKIM). Enabling these mechanisms within an organization (through policies such as DMARC) may enable recipients (intra-org and cross domain) to perform similar message filtering and validation.[\[8\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365/security/office-365-security/anti-spoofing-protection?view=o365-worldwide)[\[9\]](https://www.cyber.gov.au/sites/default/files/2019-03/spoof_email_sender_policy_framework.pdf)

Furthermore, policies may enforce / install browser extensions that protect against IDN and homograph attacks. Browser password managers may also be configured to only populate credential fields when the URL matches that of the original, legitimate site.

Enterprise

[T1539](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1539)

[Steal Web Session Cookie](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1539)

Configure browsers or tasks to regularly delete persistent cookies.

Additionally, minimize the length of time a web cookie is viable to potentially reduce the impact of stolen cookies while also increasing the needed frequency of cookie theft attempts  providing defenders with additional chances at detection.[\[10\]](https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/security/blog/2022/11/16/token-tactics-how-to-prevent-detect-and-respond-to-cloud-token-theft/)For example, use non-persistent cookies to limit the duration a session ID will remain on the web client cache where an attacker could obtain it.[\[11\]](https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Session_Management_Cheat_Sheet.html)

Enterprise

[T1553](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553)

[Subvert Trust Controls](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553)

HTTP Public Key Pinning (HPKP) is one method to mitigate potential[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)situations where and adversary uses a mis-issued or fraudulent certificate to intercept encrypted communications by enforcing use of an expected certificate.[\[12\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTTP_Public_Key_Pinning)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/004)

[Install Root Certificate](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1553/004)

HTTP Public Key Pinning (HPKP) is one method to mitigate potential[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)situations where and adversary uses a mis-issued or fraudulent certificate to intercept encrypted communications by enforcing use of an expected certificate.[\[12\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTTP_Public_Key_Pinning)

Enterprise

[T1537](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1537)

[Transfer Data to Cloud Account](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1537)

Configure appropriate data sharing restrictions in cloud services. For example, external sharing in Microsoft SharePoint and Google Drive can be turned off altogether, blocked for certain domains, or restricted to certain users.[\[13\]](https://support.google.com/a/answer/60781)[\[14\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/sharepoint/turn-external-sharing-on-or-off)

Enterprise

[T1535](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1535)

[Unused/Unsupported Cloud Regions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1535)

Cloud service providers may allow customers to deactivate unused regions.[\[15\]](https://medium.com/cloudsploit/the-danger-of-unused-aws-regions-af0bf1b878fc)

Enterprise

[T1550](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/004)

[Use Alternate Authentication Material](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550):[Web Session Cookie](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/004)

Configure browsers or tasks to regularly delete persistent cookies.

Update Software
===============

Perform regular software updates to mitigate exploitation risk.

ID:M1051

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:07 July 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1051/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1548](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

[Abuse Elevation Control Mechanism](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

Perform regular software updates to mitigate exploitation risk.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/002)

[Bypass User Account Control](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/002)

Consider updating Windows to the latest version and patch level to utilize the latest protective measures against UAC bypass.[\[1\]](https://github.com/hfiref0x/UACME)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/006)

[TCC Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/006)

Routinely update software. Where possible, ensure systems are macOS Sierra+ and SIP is enabled.[\[2\]](https://www.welivesecurity.com/2022/07/19/i-see-what-you-did-there-look-cloudmensis-macos-spyware/)

Enterprise

[T1176](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1176)

[Browser Extensions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1176)

Ensure operating systems and browsers are using the most current version.

Enterprise

[T1110](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/001)

[Brute Force](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110):[Password Guessing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/001)

Upgrade management services to the latest supported and compatible version. Specifically, any version providing increased password complexity or policy enforcement preventing default or weak passwords.

Enterprise

[T1555](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555)

[Credentials from Password Stores](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555)

Perform regular software updates to mitigate exploitation risk.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555/005)

[Password Managers](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1555/005)

Update password managers regularly by employing patch management for internal enterprise endpoints and servers.

Enterprise

[T1602](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602)

[Data from Configuration Repository](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602)

Keep system images and software updated and migrate to SNMPv3.[\[3\]](https://community.cisco.com/t5/security-blogs/attackers-continue-to-target-legacy-devices/ba-p/4169954)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/001)

[SNMP (MIB Dump)](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/001)

Keep system images and software updated and migrate to SNMPv3.[\[3\]](https://community.cisco.com/t5/security-blogs/attackers-continue-to-target-legacy-devices/ba-p/4169954)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/002)

[Network Device Configuration Dump](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1602/002)

Keep system images and software updated and migrate to SNMPv3.[\[3\]](https://community.cisco.com/t5/security-blogs/attackers-continue-to-target-legacy-devices/ba-p/4169954)

Enterprise

[T1189](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1189)

[Drive-by Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1189)

Ensure all browsers and plugins kept updated can help prevent the exploit phase of this technique. Use modern browsers with security features turned on.

Enterprise

[T1546](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546)

Perform regular software updates to mitigate exploitation risk.

[.010](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/010)

[AppInit DLLs](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/010)

Upgrade to Windows 8 or later and enable secure boot.

[.011](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/011)

[Application Shimming](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/011)

Microsoft released an optional patch update - KB3045645 - that will remove the "auto-elevate" flag within the sdbinst.exe. This will prevent use of application shimming to bypass UAC.

Enterprise

[T1190](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1190)

Enterprise

Enterprise

[T1574](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

[Hijack Execution Flow](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

Update software regularly to include patches that fix DLL side-loading vulnerabilities.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/002)

[DLL Side-Loading](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/002)

Update software regularly to include patches that fix DLL side-loading vulnerabilities.

Enterprise

[T1137](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137)

[Office Application Startup](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137)

For the Outlook methods, blocking macros may be ineffective as the Visual Basic engine used for these features is separate from the macro scripting engine.[\[4\]](https://sensepost.com/blog/2017/outlook-forms-and-shells/)Microsoft has released patches to try to address each issue. Ensure KB3191938 which blocks Outlook Visual Basic and displays a malicious code warning, KB4011091 which disables custom forms by default, and KB4011162 which removes the legacy Home Page feature, are applied to systems.[\[5\]](https://sensepost.com/blog/2017/outlook-home-page-another-ruler-vector/)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137/003)

[Outlook Forms](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137/003)

For the Outlook methods, blocking macros may be ineffective as the Visual Basic engine used for these features is separate from the macro scripting engine.[\[4\]](https://sensepost.com/blog/2017/outlook-forms-and-shells/)Microsoft has released patches to try to address each issue. Ensure KB3191938 which blocks Outlook Visual Basic and displays a malicious code warning, KB4011091 which disables custom forms by default, and KB4011162 which removes the legacy Home Page feature, are applied to systems.[\[5\]](https://sensepost.com/blog/2017/outlook-home-page-another-ruler-vector/)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137/004)

[Outlook Home Page](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137/004)

For the Outlook methods, blocking macros may be ineffective as the Visual Basic engine used for these features is separate from the macro scripting engine.[\[4\]](https://sensepost.com/blog/2017/outlook-forms-and-shells/)Microsoft has released patches to try to address each issue. Ensure KB3191938 which blocks Outlook Visual Basic and displays a malicious code warning, KB4011091 which disables custom forms by default, and KB4011162 which removes the legacy Home Page feature, are applied to systems.[\[5\]](https://sensepost.com/blog/2017/outlook-home-page-another-ruler-vector/)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137/005)

[Outlook Rules](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1137/005)

For the Outlook methods, blocking macros may be ineffective as the Visual Basic engine used for these features is separate from the macro scripting engine.[\[4\]](https://sensepost.com/blog/2017/outlook-forms-and-shells/)Microsoft has released patches to try to address each issue. Ensure KB3191938 which blocks Outlook Visual Basic and displays a malicious code warning, KB4011091 which disables custom forms by default, and KB4011162 which removes the legacy Home Page feature, are applied to systems.[\[5\]](https://sensepost.com/blog/2017/outlook-home-page-another-ruler-vector/)

Enterprise

[T1542](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542)

[Pre-OS Boot](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542)

Patch the BIOS and EFI as necessary.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/001)

[System Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/001)

Patch the BIOS and EFI as necessary.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/002)

[Component Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1542/002)

Perform regular firmware updates to mitigate risks of exploitation and/or abuse.

Enterprise

[T1072](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

[Software Deployment Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

Patch deployment systems regularly to prevent potential remote access through[Exploitation for Privilege Escalation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1068).

Enterprise

[T1195](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195)

[Supply Chain Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195)

A patch management process should be implemented to check unused dependencies, unmaintained and/or previously vulnerable dependencies, unnecessary features, components, files, and documentation.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/001)

[Compromise Software Dependencies and Development Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/001)

A patch management process should be implemented to check unused dependencies, unmaintained and/or previously vulnerable dependencies, unnecessary features, components, files, and documentation.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/002)

[Compromise Software Supply Chain](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/002)

A patch management process should be implemented to check unused applications, unmaintained and/or previously vulnerable software, unnecessary features, components, files, and documentation.

Enterprise

[T1552](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

[Unsecured Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

Apply patch KB2962486 which prevents credentials from being stored in GPPs.[\[6\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2288)[\[7\]](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2962486/ms14-025-vulnerability-in-group-policy-preferences-could-allow-elevati)

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/006)

[Group Policy Preferences](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/006)

Apply patch KB2962486 which prevents credentials from being stored in GPPs.[\[6\]](https://adsecurity.org/?p=2288)[\[7\]](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2962486/ms14-025-vulnerability-in-group-policy-preferences-could-allow-elevati)

Enterprise

[T1550](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/002)

[Use Alternate Authentication Material](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550):[Pass the Hash](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/002)

Apply patch KB2871997 to Windows 7 and higher systems to limit the default access of accounts in the local administrator group.[\[8\]](https://apps.nsa.gov/iaarchive/library/reports/spotting-the-adversary-with-windows-event-log-monitoring.cfm)

User Account Control
====================

Configure Windows User Account Control to mitigate risk of adversaries obtaining elevated process access.

ID:M1052

Version:1.1

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:31 March 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1052/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1548](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

[Abuse Elevation Control Mechanism](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

Although UAC bypass techniques exist, it is still prudent to use the highest enforcement level for UAC when possible and mitigate bypass opportunities that exist with techniques such as[DLL Search Order Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/001).

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/002)

[Bypass User Account Control](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/002)

Although UAC bypass techniques exist, it is still prudent to use the highest enforcement level for UAC when possible and mitigate bypass opportunities that exist with techniques such as[DLL Search Order Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/001).

Enterprise

[T1546](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546)

[.011](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/011)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546):[Application Shimming](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/011)

Changing UAC settings to "Always Notify" will give the user more visibility when UAC elevation is requested, however, this option will not be popular among users due to the constant UAC interruptions.

Enterprise

[T1574](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

[Hijack Execution Flow](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

Turn off UAC's privilege elevation for standard users`[HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System]`to automatically deny elevation requests, add:`"ConsentPromptBehaviorUser"=dword:00000000`. Consider enabling installer detection for all users by adding:`"EnableInstallerDetection"=dword:00000001`. This will prompt for a password for installation and also log the attempt. To disable installer detection, instead add:`"EnableInstallerDetection"=dword:00000000`. This may prevent potential elevation of privileges through exploitation during the process of UAC detecting the installer, but will allow the installation process to continue without being logged.[\[1\]](https://seclists.org/fulldisclosure/2015/Dec/34)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/005)

[Executable Installer File Permissions Weakness](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/005)

Turn off UAC's privilege elevation for standard users`[HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System]`to automatically deny elevation requests, add:`"ConsentPromptBehaviorUser"=dword:00000000`. Consider enabling installer detection for all users by adding:`"EnableInstallerDetection"=dword:00000001`. This will prompt for a password for installation and also log the attempt. To disable installer detection, instead add:`"EnableInstallerDetection"=dword:00000000`. This may prevent potential elevation of privileges through exploitation during the process of UAC detecting the installer, but will allow the installation process to continue without being logged.[\[1\]](https://seclists.org/fulldisclosure/2015/Dec/34)

[.010](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/010)

[Services File Permissions Weakness](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/010)

Turn off UAC's privilege elevation for standard users`[HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System]`to automatically deny elevation requests, add:`"ConsentPromptBehaviorUser"=dword:00000000`. Consider enabling installer detection for all users by adding:`"EnableInstallerDetection"=dword:00000001`. This will prompt for a password for installation and also log the attempt. To disable installer detection, instead add:`"EnableInstallerDetection"=dword:00000000`. This may prevent potential elevation of privileges through exploitation during the process of UAC detecting the installer, but will allow the installation process to continue without being logged.[\[1\]](https://seclists.org/fulldisclosure/2015/Dec/34)

Enterprise

[T1550](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/002)

[Use Alternate Authentication Material](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550):[Pass the Hash](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/002)

Enable pass the hash mitigations to apply UAC restrictions to local accounts on network logon. The associated Registry key is located`HKLM\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System\LocalAccountTokenFilterPolicy`.

Through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Administrative Templates > SCM: Pass the Hash Mitigations: Apply UAC restrictions to local accounts on network logons.[\[2\]](https://github.com/iadgov/Secure-Host-Baseline/blob/master/Windows/Group%20Policy%20Templates/en-US/SecGuide.adml)

**References**
--------------

1.  [Stefan Kanthak. (2015, December 8). Executable installers are vulnerable^WEVIL (case 7): 7z\*.exe allows remote code execution with escalation of privilege. Retrieved December 4, 2014.](https://seclists.org/fulldisclosure/2015/Dec/34)

2.  [NSA IAD. (2017, January 24). MS Security Guide. Retrieved December 18, 2017.](https://github.com/iadgov/Secure-Host-Baseline/blob/master/Windows/Group%20Policy%20Templates/en-US/SecGuide.adml)

User Account Management
=======================

Manage the creation, modification, use, and permissions associated to user accounts.

ID:M1018

Version:1.1

Created:06 June 2019

Last Modified:20 May 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1018/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1548](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

[Abuse Elevation Control Mechanism](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548)

Limit the privileges of cloud accounts to assume, create, or impersonate additional roles, policies, and permissions to only those required. Where just-in-time access is enabled, consider requiring manual approval for temporary elevation of privileges.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/005)

[Temporary Elevated Cloud Access](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/005)

Limit the privileges of cloud accounts to assume, create, or impersonate additional roles, policies, and permissions to only those required. Where just-in-time access is enabled, consider requiring manual approval for temporary elevation of privileges.

Enterprise

[T1134](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134)

[Access Token Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134)

An adversary must already have administrator level access on the local system to make full use of this technique; be sure to restrict users and accounts to the least privileges they require.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/001)

[Token Impersonation/Theft](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/001)

An adversary must already have administrator level access on the local system to make full use of this technique; be sure to restrict users and accounts to the least privileges they require.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/002)

[Create Process with Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/002)

An adversary must already have administrator level access on the local system to make full use of this technique; be sure to restrict users and accounts to the least privileges they require.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/003)

[Make and Impersonate Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1134/003)

An adversary must already have administrator level access on the local system to make full use of this technique; be sure to restrict users and accounts to the least privileges they require.

Enterprise

[T1087](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087)

[Account Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087)

Manage the creation, modification, use, and permissions associated to user accounts.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087/004)

[Cloud Account](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087/004)

Limit permissions to discover cloud accounts in accordance with least privilege. Organizations should limit the number of users within the organization with an IAM role that has administrative privileges, strive to reduce all permanent privileged role assignments, and conduct periodic entitlement reviews on IAM users, roles and policies.

Enterprise

[T1098](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098)

[Account Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098)

Ensure that low-privileged user accounts do not have permissions to modify accounts or account-related policies.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/001)

[Additional Cloud Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/001)

Ensure that low-privileged user accounts do not have permission to add access keys to accounts. In AWS environments, prohibit users from calling the`sts:GetFederationToken`API unless explicitly required.[\[1\]](https://www.crowdstrike.com/blog/how-adversaries-persist-with-aws-user-federation/)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/003)

[Additional Cloud Roles](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/003)

Ensure that low-privileged user accounts do not have permissions to add permissions to accounts or update IAM policies.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/004)

[SSH Authorized Keys](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/004)

In cloud environments, ensure that only users who explicitly require the permissions to update instance metadata or configurations can do so.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/006)

[Additional Container Cluster Roles](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/006)

Ensure that low-privileged accounts do not have permissions to add permissions to accounts or to update container cluster roles.

Enterprise

[T1020](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1020)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1020/001)

[Automated Exfiltration](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1020):[Traffic Duplication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1020/001)

In cloud environments, ensure that users are not granted permissions to create or modify traffic mirrors unless this is explicitly required.

Enterprise

[T1197](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1197)

[BITS Jobs](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1197)

Consider limiting access to the BITS interface to specific users or groups.[\[2\]](https://www.symantec.com/connect/blogs/malware-update-windows-update)

Enterprise

[T1547](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547)

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/004)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[Winlogon Helper DLL](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/004)

Limit the privileges of user accounts so that only authorized administrators can perform Winlogon helper changes.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/006)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[Kernel Modules and Extensions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/006)

Use MDM to disable user's ability to install or approve kernel extensions, and ensure all approved kernel extensions are in alignment with policies specified in`com.apple.syspolicy.kernel-extension-policy`.[\[3\]](https://developer.apple.com/library/archive/technotes/tn2459/_index.html)[\[4\]](https://developer.apple.com/business/documentation/Configuration-Profile-Reference.pdf)

[.009](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/009)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[Shortcut Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/009)

Limit permissions for who can create symbolic links in Windows to appropriate groups such as Administrators and necessary groups for virtualization. This can be done through GPO: Computer Configuration > \[Policies\] > Windows Settings > Security Settings > Local Policies > User Rights Assignment: Create symbolic links.[\[5\]](https://www.stigviewer.com/stig/windows_server_2008_r2_member_server/2015-06-25/finding/V-26482)

[.012](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/012)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[Print Processors](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/012)

Limit user accounts that can load or unload device drivers by disabling`SeLoadDriverPrivilege`.

[.013](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/013)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[XDG Autostart Entries](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/013)

Limit privileges of user accounts so only authorized privileged users can create and modify XDG autostart entries.

Enterprise

[T1185](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1185)

[Browser Session Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1185)

Since browser pivoting requires a high integrity process to launch from, restricting user permissions and addressing Privilege Escalation and[Bypass User Account Control](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1548/002)opportunities can limit the exposure to this technique.

Enterprise

[T1110](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110)

[Brute Force](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110)

Proactively reset accounts that are known to be part of breached credentials either immediately, or after detecting bruteforce attempts.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/004)

[Credential Stuffing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1110/004)

Proactively reset accounts that are known to be part of breached credentials either immediately, or after detecting bruteforce attempts.

Enterprise

[T1580](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1580)

[Cloud Infrastructure Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1580)

Limit permissions to discover cloud infrastructure in accordance with least privilege. Organizations should limit the number of users within the organization with an IAM role that has administrative privileges, strive to reduce all permanent privileged role assignments, and conduct periodic entitlement reviews on IAM users, roles and policies.

Enterprise

[T1538](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1538)

[Cloud Service Dashboard](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1538)

Enforce the principle of least-privilege by limiting dashboard visibility to only the resources required. This may limit the discovery value of the dashboard in the event of a compromised account.

Enterprise

[T1619](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1619)

[Cloud Storage Object Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1619)

Restrict granting of permissions related to listing objects in cloud storage to necessary accounts.

Enterprise

[T1059](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059)

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/008)

[Command and Scripting Interpreter](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059):[Network Device CLI](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/008)

Use of Authentication, Authorization, and Accounting (AAA) systems will limit actions users can perform and provide a history of user actions to detect unauthorized use and abuse. Ensure least privilege principles are applied to user accounts and groups so that only authorized users can perform configuration changes.[\[6\]](https://tools.cisco.com/security/center/resources/integrity_assurance.html#38)

Enterprise

[T1609](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1609)

[Container Administration Command](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1609)

Enforce authentication and role-based access control on the container service to restrict users to the least privileges required.[\[7\]](https://media.defense.gov/2022/Aug/29/2003066362/-1/-1/0/CTR_KUBERNETES_HARDENING_GUIDANCE_1.2_20220829.PDF)When using Kubernetes, avoid giving users wildcard permissions or adding users to the`system:masters`group, and use`RoleBindings`rather than`ClusterRoleBindings`to limit user privileges to specific namespaces.[\[8\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/security/rbac-good-practices/)

Enterprise

[T1613](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1613)

[Container and Resource Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1613)

Enforce the principle of least privilege by limiting dashboard visibility to only the required users. When using Kubernetes, avoid giving users wildcard permissions or adding users to the`system:masters`group, and use`RoleBindings`rather than`ClusterRoleBindings`to limit user privileges to specific namespaces.[\[8\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/security/rbac-good-practices/)

Enterprise

[T1543](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543)

[Create or Modify System Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543)

Limit privileges of user accounts and groups so that only authorized administrators can interact with system-level process changes and service configurations.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/002)

[Systemd Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/002)

Limit user access to system utilities such as`systemctl`to only users who have a legitimate need.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/003)

[Windows Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/003)

Limit privileges of user accounts and groups so that only authorized administrators can interact with service changes and service configurations.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/004)

[Launch Daemon](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/004)

Limit privileges of user accounts and remediate Privilege Escalation vectors so only authorized administrators can create new Launch Daemons.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/005)

[Container Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/005)

Limit access to utilities such as docker to only users who have a legitimate need, especially if using docker in rootful mode. In Kubernetes environments, only grant privileges to deploy pods to users that require it.

Enterprise

[T1530](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1530)

[Data from Cloud Storage](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1530)

Configure user permissions groups and roles for access to cloud storage.[\[9\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/storage/common/storage-security-guide)Implement strict Identity and Access Management (IAM) controls to prevent access to storage solutions except for the applications, users, and services that require access.[\[10\]](https://aws.amazon.com/premiumsupport/knowledge-center/secure-s3-resources/)Ensure that temporary access tokens are issued rather than permanent credentials, especially when access is being granted to entities outside of the internal security boundary.[\[11\]](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/id_credentials_temp.html)

Enterprise

[T1213](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213)

[Data from Information Repositories](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213)

Enforce the principle of least-privilege. Consider implementing access control mechanisms that include both authentication and authorization.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/001)

[Confluence](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/001)

Enforce the principle of least-privilege. Consider implementing access control mechanisms that include both authentication and authorization.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/002)

[Sharepoint](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/002)

Enforce the principle of least-privilege. Consider implementing access control mechanisms that include both authentication and authorization.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/003)

[Code Repositories](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/003)

Enforce the principle of least-privilege. Consider implementing access control mechanisms that include both authentication and authorization for code repositories.

Enterprise

[T1610](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1610)

[Deploy Container](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1610)

Enforce the principle of least privilege by limiting container dashboard access to only the necessary users. When using Kubernetes, avoid giving users wildcard permissions or adding users to the`system:masters`group, and use`RoleBindings`rather than`ClusterRoleBindings`to limit user privileges to specific namespaces.[\[8\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/security/rbac-good-practices/)

Enterprise

[T1006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1006)

[Direct Volume Access](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1006)

Ensure only accounts required to configure and manage backups have the privileges to do so. Monitor these accounts for unauthorized backup activity.

Enterprise

[T1484](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1484)

[Domain or Tenant Policy Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1484)

Consider implementing WMI and security filtering to further tailor which users and computers a GPO will apply to.[\[12\]](https://wald0.com/?p=179)[\[13\]](https://blogs.technet.microsoft.com/askds/2008/09/11/fun-with-wmi-filters-in-group-policy/)[\[14\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/windows/desktop/Policy/filtering-the-scope-of-a-gpo)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1484/001)

[Group Policy Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1484/001)

Consider implementing WMI and security filtering to further tailor which users and computers a GPO will apply to.[\[12\]](https://wald0.com/?p=179)[\[13\]](https://blogs.technet.microsoft.com/askds/2008/09/11/fun-with-wmi-filters-in-group-policy/)[\[14\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/windows/desktop/Policy/filtering-the-scope-of-a-gpo)

Enterprise

[T1546](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/003)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546):[Windows Management Instrumentation Event Subscription](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1546/003)

By default, only administrators are allowed to connect remotely using WMI; restrict other users that are allowed to connect, or disallow all users from connecting remotely to WMI.

Enterprise

[T1048](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048)

[Exfiltration Over Alternative Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048)

Configure user permissions groups and roles for access to cloud storage.[\[9\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/storage/common/storage-security-guide)Implement strict Identity and Access Management (IAM) controls to prevent access to storage solutions except for the applications, users, and services that require access.[\[10\]](https://aws.amazon.com/premiumsupport/knowledge-center/secure-s3-resources/)Ensure that temporary access tokens are issued rather than permanent credentials, especially when access is being granted to entities outside of the internal security boundary.[\[11\]](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/id_credentials_temp.html)

Enterprise

[T1657](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1657)

[Financial Theft](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1657)

Limit access/authority to execute sensitive transactions, and switch to systems and procedures designed to authenticate/approve payments and purchase requests outside of insecure communication lines such as email.

Enterprise

[T1606](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606)

[Forge Web Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606)

Ensure that user accounts with administrative rights follow best practices, including use of privileged access workstations, Just in Time/Just Enough Administration (JIT/JEA), and strong authentication. Reduce the number of users that are members of highly privileged Directory Roles.[\[15\]](https://msrc-blog.microsoft.com/2020/12/13/customer-guidance-on-recent-nation-state-cyber-attacks/)In AWS environments, prohibit users from calling the`sts:GetFederationToken`API unless explicitly required.[\[1\]](https://www.crowdstrike.com/blog/how-adversaries-persist-with-aws-user-federation/)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606/002)

[SAML Tokens](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1606/002)

Ensure that user accounts with administrative rights follow best practices, including use of privileged access workstations, Just in Time/Just Enough Administration (JIT/JEA), and strong authentication. Reduce the number of users that are members of highly privileged Directory Roles.[\[15\]](https://msrc-blog.microsoft.com/2020/12/13/customer-guidance-on-recent-nation-state-cyber-attacks/)

Enterprise

[T1574](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

[Hijack Execution Flow](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

Limit privileges of user accounts and groups so that only authorized administrators can interact with service changes and service binary target path locations. Deny execution from user directories such as file download directories and temp directories where able.

Ensure that proper permissions and directory access control are set to deny users the ability to write files to the top-level directory`C:`and system directories, such as`C:\Windows\`, to reduce places where malicious files could be placed for execution.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/005)

[Executable Installer File Permissions Weakness](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/005)

Limit privileges of user accounts and groups so that only authorized administrators can interact with service changes and service binary target path locations. Deny execution from user directories such as file download directories and temp directories where able.

[.010](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/010)

[Services File Permissions Weakness](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/010)

Limit privileges of user accounts and groups so that only authorized administrators can interact with service changes and service binary target path locations. Deny execution from user directories such as file download directories and temp directories where able.

[.012](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/012)

[COR\_PROFILER](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/012)

Limit the privileges of user accounts so that only authorized administrators can edit system environment variables.

Enterprise

[T1562](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562)

[Impair Defenses](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562)

Ensure proper user permissions are in place to prevent adversaries from disabling or interfering with security/logging services.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/001)

[Disable or Modify Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/001)

Ensure proper user permissions are in place to prevent adversaries from disabling or interfering with security services.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/002)

[Disable Windows Event Logging](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/002)

Ensure proper user permissions are in place to prevent adversaries from disabling or interfering with logging.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/004)

[Disable or Modify System Firewall](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/004)

Ensure proper user permissions are in place to prevent adversaries from disabling or modifying firewall settings.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/006)

[Indicator Blocking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/006)

Ensure event tracers/forwarders[\[16\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/desktop/etw/event-tracing-portal), firewall policies, and other associated mechanisms are secured with appropriate permissions and access controls and cannot be manipulated by user accounts.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/007)

[Disable or Modify Cloud Firewall](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/007)

Ensure least privilege principles are applied to Identity and Access Management (IAM) security policies.[\[17\]](https://expel.io/blog/finding-evil-in-aws/)

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/008)

[Disable or Modify Cloud Logs](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/008)

Configure default account policy to enable logging. Manage policies to ensure only necessary users have permissions to make changes to logging policies.

[.012](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/012)

[Disable or Modify Linux Audit System](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/012)

An adversary must already have root level access on the local system to make full use of this technique; be sure to restrict users and accounts to the least privileges they require.

Enterprise

[T1490](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1490)

[Inhibit System Recovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1490)

Limit the user accounts that have access to backups to only those required.

Enterprise

[T1654](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1654)

[Log Enumeration](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1654)

Limit the ability to access and export sensitive logs to privileged accounts where possible.

Enterprise

[T1556](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

[Modify Authentication Process](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556)

Ensure that proper policies are implemented to dictate the the secure enrollment and deactivation of authentication mechanisms, such as MFA, for user accounts.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/006)

[Multi-Factor Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/006)

Ensure that proper policies are implemented to dictate the secure enrollment and deactivation of MFA for user accounts.

[.009](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/009)

[Conditional Access Policies](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1556/009)

Limit permissions to modify conditional access policies to only those required.

Enterprise

[T1578](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1578)

[Modify Cloud Compute Infrastructure](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1578)

Limit permissions for creating, deleting, and otherwise altering compute components in accordance with least privilege. Organizations should limit the number of users within the organization with an IAM role that has administrative privileges, strive to reduce all permanent privileged role assignments, and conduct periodic entitlement reviews on IAM users, roles and policies.[\[18\]](https://content.fireeye.com/m-trends/rpt-m-trends-2020)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1578/001)

[Create Snapshot](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1578/001)

Limit permissions for creating snapshots or backups in accordance with least privilege. Organizations should limit the number of users within the organization with an IAM role that has administrative privileges, strive to reduce all permanent privileged role assignments, and conduct periodic entitlement reviews on IAM users, roles and policies.[\[18\]](https://content.fireeye.com/m-trends/rpt-m-trends-2020)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1578/002)

[Create Cloud Instance](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1578/002)

Limit permissions for creating new instances in accordance with least privilege. Organizations should limit the number of users within the organization with an IAM role that has administrative privileges, strive to reduce all permanent privileged role assignments, and conduct periodic entitlement reviews on IAM users, roles and policies.[\[18\]](https://content.fireeye.com/m-trends/rpt-m-trends-2020)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1578/003)

[Delete Cloud Instance](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1578/003)

Limit permissions for deleting new instances in accordance with least privilege. Organizations should limit the number of users within the organization with an IAM role that has administrative privileges, strive to reduce all permanent privileged role assignments, and conduct periodic entitlement reviews on IAM users, roles and policies.[\[18\]](https://content.fireeye.com/m-trends/rpt-m-trends-2020)

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1578/005)

[Modify Cloud Compute Configurations](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1578/005)

Limit permissions to request quotas adjustments or modify tenant-level compute setting to only those required.

Enterprise

[T1040](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1040)

[Network Sniffing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1040)

In cloud environments, ensure that users are not granted permissions to create or modify traffic mirrors unless this is explicitly required.

Enterprise

[T1566](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/002)

[Phishing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566):[Spearphishing Link](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/002)

Azure AD Administrators apply limitations upon the ability for users to grant consent to unfamiliar or unverified third-party applications.

Enterprise

[T1563](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563)

[Remote Service Session Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563)

Limit remote user permissions if remote access is necessary.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/002)

[RDP Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1563/002)

Limit remote user permissions if remote access is necessary.

Enterprise

[T1021](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021)

Limit the accounts that may use remote services. Limit the permissions for accounts that are at higher risk of compromise; for example, configure SSH so users can only run specific programs.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/001)

[Remote Desktop Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/001)

Limit remote user permissions if remote access is necessary.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/004)

[SSH](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/004)

Limit which user accounts are allowed to login via SSH.

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/008)

[Direct Cloud VM Connections](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/008)

Limit which users are allowed to access compute infrastructure via cloud native methods.

Enterprise

[T1053](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053)

[Scheduled Task/Job](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053)

Limit privileges of user accounts and remediate Privilege Escalation vectors so only authorized administrators can create scheduled tasks on remote systems.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/002)

[At](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/002)

Limit privileges of user accounts and remediate Privilege Escalation vectors so only authorized administrators can create scheduled tasks on remote systems. In Linux environments, users account-level access to`[at](https://attack.mitre.org/software/S0110)`can be managed using`at.allow`and`at.deny`files. Users listed in the at.allow are enabled to schedule actions using at, whereas users listed in at.deny file disabled from the utility.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/003)

[Cron](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/003)

`cron`permissions are controlled by`/etc/cron.allow and /etc/cron.deny`. If there is a`cron.allow`file, then the user or users that need to use`cron`will need to be listed in the file.`cron.deny`is used to explicitly disallow users from using cron. If neither files exist, then only the super user is allowed to run cron.

[.005](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/005)

[Scheduled Task](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/005)

Limit privileges of user accounts and remediate Privilege Escalation vectors so only authorized administrators can create scheduled tasks on remote systems.

[.006](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/006)

[Systemd Timers](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/006)

Limit user access to system utilities such as 'systemctl' or 'systemd-run' to users who have a legitimate need.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/007)

[Container Orchestration Job](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/007)

Limit privileges of user accounts and remediate privilege escalation vectors so only authorized administrators can create container orchestration jobs.

Enterprise

[T1505](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505)

[Server Software Component](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505)

Enforce the principle of least privilege by limiting privileges of user accounts so only authorized accounts can modify and/or add server software components.[\[19\]](https://media.defense.gov/2020/Jun/09/2002313081/-1/-1/0/CSI-DETECT-AND-PREVENT-WEB-SHELL-MALWARE-20200422.PDF)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505/003)

[Web Shell](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1505/003)

Enforce the principle of least privilege by limiting privileges of user accounts so only authorized accounts can modify the web directory.[\[19\]](https://media.defense.gov/2020/Jun/09/2002313081/-1/-1/0/CSI-DETECT-AND-PREVENT-WEB-SHELL-MALWARE-20200422.PDF)

Enterprise

[T1648](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1648)

[Serverless Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1648)

Remove permissions to create, modify, or run serverless resources from users that do not explicitly require them.

Enterprise

[T1489](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1489)

[Service Stop](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1489)

Limit privileges of user accounts and groups so that only authorized administrators can interact with service changes and service configurations.

Enterprise

[T1072](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

[Software Deployment Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

Ensure that any accounts used by third-party providers to access these systems are traceable to the third-party and are not used throughout the network or used by other third-party providers in the same environment. Ensure there are regular reviews of accounts provisioned to these systems to verify continued business need, and ensure there is governance to trace de-provisioning of access that is no longer required. Ensure proper system and access isolation for critical network systems through use of account privilege separation.

Enterprise

[T1528](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1528)

[Steal Application Access Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1528)

Enforce role-based access control to limit accounts to the least privileges they require. A Cloud Access Security Broker (CASB) can be used to set usage policies and manage user permissions on cloud applications to prevent access to application access tokens. In Kubernetes applications, set "automountServiceAccountToken: false" in the YAML specification of pods that do not require access to service account tokens.[\[7\]](https://media.defense.gov/2022/Aug/29/2003066362/-1/-1/0/CTR_KUBERNETES_HARDENING_GUIDANCE_1.2_20220829.PDF)

Enterprise

[T1569](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1569)

[System Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1569)

Prevent users from installing their own launch agents or launch daemons.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1569/001)

[Launchctl](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1569/001)

Prevent users from installing their own launch agents or launch daemons.

Enterprise

[T1537](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1537)

[Transfer Data to Cloud Account](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1537)

Limit user account and IAM policies to the least privileges required.

Enterprise

[T1199](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1199)

[Trusted Relationship](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1199)

Properly manage accounts and permissions used by parties in trusted relationships to minimize potential abuse by the party and if the party is compromised by an adversary. In Office 365 environments, partner relationships and roles can be viewed under the "Partner Relationships" page.[\[20\]](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365/commerce/manage-partners?view=o365-worldwide)

Enterprise

[T1552](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/007)

[Unsecured Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552):[Container API](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/007)

Enforce authentication and role-based access control on the container API to restrict users to the least privileges required.[\[7\]](https://media.defense.gov/2022/Aug/29/2003066362/-1/-1/0/CTR_KUBERNETES_HARDENING_GUIDANCE_1.2_20220829.PDF)When using Kubernetes, avoid giving users wildcard permissions or adding users to the`system:masters`group, and use`RoleBindings`rather than`ClusterRoleBindings`to limit user privileges to specific namespaces.[\[8\]](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/security/rbac-good-practices/)

Enterprise

[T1550](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

[Use Alternate Authentication Material](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

Enforce the principle of least-privilege. Do not allow a domain user to be in the local administrator group on multiple systems.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/002)

[Pass the Hash](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/002)

Do not allow a domain user to be in the local administrator group on multiple systems.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/003)

[Pass the Ticket](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/003)

Do not allow a user to be a local administrator for multiple systems.

Enterprise

[T1078](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

[Valid Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

Regularly audit user accounts for activity and deactivate or remove any that are no longer needed.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/004)

[Cloud Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/004)

Periodically review user accounts and remove those that are inactive or unnecessary. Limit the ability for user accounts to create additional accounts.

Enterprise

[T1047](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1047)

[Windows Management Instrumentation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1047)

By default, only administrators are allowed to connect remotely using WMI. Restrict other users who are allowed to connect, or disallow all users to connect remotely to WMI.

User Training
=============

Train users to be aware of access or manipulation attempts by an adversary to reduce the risk of successful spearphishing, social engineering, and other techniques that involve user interaction.

ID:M1017

Version:1.2

Created:06 June 2019

Last Modified:21 October 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1017/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1557](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)

[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557)

Train users to be suspicious about certificate errors. Adversaries may use their own certificates in an attempt to intercept HTTPS traffic. Certificate errors may arise when the applications certificate does not match the one expected by the host.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/002)

[ARP Cache Poisoning](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/002)

Train users to be suspicious about certificate errors. Adversaries may use their own certificates in an attempt to intercept HTTPS traffic. Certificate errors may arise when the applications certificate does not match the one expected by the host.

Enterprise

[T1547](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547)

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/007)

[Boot or Logon Autostart Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547):[Re-opened Applications](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1547/007)

Holding the Shift key while logging in prevents apps from opening automatically.[\[1\]](https://support.apple.com/en-us/HT204005)

Enterprise

[T1176](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1176)

[Browser Extensions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1176)

Close out all browser sessions when finished using them to prevent any potentially malicious extensions from continuing to run.

Enterprise

[T1185](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1185)

[Browser Session Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1185)

Close all browser sessions regularly and when they are no longer needed.

Enterprise

[T1213](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213)

[Data from Information Repositories](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213)

Develop and publish policies that define acceptable information to be stored in repositories.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/001)

[Confluence](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/001)

Develop and publish policies that define acceptable information to be stored in Confluence repositories.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/002)

[Sharepoint](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/002)

Develop and publish policies that define acceptable information to be stored in SharePoint repositories.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/003)

[Code Repositories](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1213/003)

Develop and publish policies that define acceptable information to be stored in code repositories.

Enterprise

[T1657](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1657)

[Financial Theft](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1657)

Train and encourage users to identify social engineering techniques used to enable financial theft. Also consider training users on procedures to prevent and respond to swatting and doxing, acts increasingly deployed by financially motivated groups to further coerce victims into satisfying ransom/extortion demands.[\[2\]](https://www.cisa.gov/sites/default/files/2023-08/CSRB_Lapsus%24_508c.pdf)[\[3\]](https://www.beckershospitalreview.com/cybersecurity/hackers-threaten-to-send-swat-teams-to-fred-hutch-patients-homes.html)

Enterprise

[T1656](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1656)

[Impersonation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1656)

Train users to be aware of impersonation tricks and how to counter them, for example confirming incoming requests through an independent platform like a phone call or in-person, to reduce risk.

Enterprise

[T1056](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1056)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1056/002)

[Input Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1056):[GUI Input Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1056/002)

Use user training as a way to bring awareness and raise suspicion for potentially malicious events and dialog boxes (ex: Office documents prompting for credentials).

Enterprise

[T1036](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036)

[Masquerading](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036)

Train users not to open email attachments or click unknown links (URLs). Such training fosters more secure habits within your organization and will limit many of the risks.

[.007](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036/007)

[Double File Extension](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1036/007)

Train users to look for double extensions in filenames, and in general use training as a way to bring awareness to common phishing and spearphishing techniques and how to raise suspicion for potentially malicious events.

Enterprise

[T1111](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1111)

[Multi-Factor Authentication Interception](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1111)

Remove smart cards when not in use.

Enterprise

[T1621](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1621)

[Multi-Factor Authentication Request Generation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1621)

Train users to only accept 2FA/MFA requests from login attempts they initiated, to review source location of the login attempt prompting the 2FA/MFA requests, and to report suspicious/unsolicited prompts.

Enterprise

[T1027](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1027)

[Obfuscated Files or Information](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1027)

Ensure that a finite amount of ingress points to a software deployment system exist with restricted access for those required to allow and enable newly deployed software.

Enterprise

[T1003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

[OS Credential Dumping](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003)

Limit credential overlap across accounts and systems by training users and administrators not to use the same password for multiple accounts.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/001)

[LSASS Memory](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/001)

Limit credential overlap across accounts and systems by training users and administrators not to use the same password for multiple accounts.

[Security Account Manager](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/002)

Limit credential overlap across accounts and systems by training users and administrators not to use the same password for multiple accounts.

[NTDS](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/003)

Limit credential overlap across accounts and systems by training users and administrators not to use the same password for multiple accounts.

Limit credential overlap across accounts and systems by training users and administrators not to use the same password for multiple accounts.

[Cached Domain Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/005)

Limit credential overlap across accounts and systems by training users and administrators not to use the same password for multiple accounts.

Enterprise

[T1566](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566)

[Phishing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566)

Users can be trained to identify social engineering techniques and phishing emails.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/001)

[Spearphishing Attachment](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/001)

Users can be trained to identify social engineering techniques and spearphishing emails.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/002)

[Spearphishing Link](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/002)

Users can be trained to identify social engineering techniques and spearphishing emails with malicious links which includes phishing for consent with OAuth 2.0. Additionally, users may perform visual checks of the domains they visit; however, homographs in ASCII and in IDN domains and URL schema obfuscation may render manual checks difficult. Phishing training and other cybersecurity training may raise awareness to check URLs before visiting the sites.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/003)

[Spearphishing via Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/003)

Users can be trained to identify social engineering techniques and spearphishing messages with malicious links.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/004)

[Spearphishing Voice](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/004)

Users can be trained to identify and report social engineering techniques and spearphishing attempts, while also being suspicious of and verifying the identify of callers.[\[4\]](https://www.cisa.gov/news-events/news/avoiding-social-engineering-and-phishing-attacks)

Enterprise

[T1598](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1598)

[Phishing for Information](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1598)

Users can be trained to identify social engineering techniques and spearphishing attempts.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1598/001)

[Spearphishing Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1598/001)

Users can be trained to identify social engineering techniques and spearphishing attempts.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1598/002)

[Spearphishing Attachment](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1598/002)

Users can be trained to identify social engineering techniques and spearphishing attempts.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1598/003)

[Spearphishing Link](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1598/003)

Users can be trained to identify social engineering techniques and spearphishing attempts. Additionally, users may perform visual checks of the domains they visit; however, homographs in ASCII and in IDN domains and URL schema obfuscation may render manual checks difficult.
