[Spearphishing Voice](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1598/004)

Users can be trained to identify and report social engineering techniques and spearphishing attempts, while also being suspicious of and verifying the identify of callers.[\[4\]](https://www.cisa.gov/news-events/news/avoiding-social-engineering-and-phishing-attacks)

Enterprise

[T1072](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

[Software Deployment Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1072)

Have a strict approval policy for use of deployment systems.

Enterprise

[T1528](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1528)

[Steal Application Access Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1528)

Users need to be trained to not authorize third-party applications they dont recognize. The user should pay particular attention to the redirect URL: if the URL is a misspelled or convoluted sequence of words related to an expected service or SaaS application, the website is likely trying to spoof a legitimate service. Users should also be cautious about the permissions they are granting to apps. For example, offline access and access to read emails should excite higher suspicions because adversaries can utilize SaaS APIs to discover credentials and other sensitive communications.

Enterprise

[T1539](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1539)

[Steal Web Session Cookie](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1539)

Train users to identify aspects of phishing attempts where they're asked to enter credentials into a site that has the incorrect domain for the application they are logging into. Additionally, train users not to run untrusted JavaScript in their browser, such as by copying and pasting code or dragging and dropping bookmarklets.

Enterprise

[T1221](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1221)

[Template Injection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1221)

Train users to identify social engineering techniques and spearphishing emails that could be used to deliver malicious documents.

Enterprise

[T1552](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

[Unsecured Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552)

Ensure that developers and system administrators are aware of the risk associated with having plaintext passwords in software configuration files that may be left on endpoint systems or servers.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/001)

[Credentials In Files](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/001)

Ensure that developers and system administrators are aware of the risk associated with having plaintext passwords in software configuration files that may be left on endpoint systems or servers.

[.008](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/008)

[Chat Messages](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1552/008)

Ensure that developers and system administrators are aware of the risk associated with sharing unsecured passwords across communication services.

Enterprise

[T1204](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204)

[User Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204)

Use user training as a way to bring awareness to common phishing and spearphishing techniques and how to raise suspicion for potentially malicious events.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/001)

[Malicious Link](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/001)

Use user training as a way to bring awareness to common phishing and spearphishing techniques and how to raise suspicion for potentially malicious events.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/002)

[Malicious File](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/002)

Use user training as a way to bring awareness to common phishing and spearphishing techniques and how to raise suspicion for potentially malicious events.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/003)

[Malicious Image](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/003)

Train users to be aware of the existence of malicious images and how to avoid deploying instances and containers from them.

Enterprise

[T1078](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

[Valid Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

Applications may send push notifications to verify a login as a form of multi-factor authentication (MFA). Train users to only accept valid push notifications and to report suspicious push notifications.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/002)

[Domain Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/002)

Applications may send push notifications to verify a login as a form of multi-factor authentication (MFA). Train users to only accept valid push notifications and to report suspicious push notifications.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/004)

[Cloud Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/004)

Applications may send push notifications to verify a login as a form of multi-factor authentication (MFA). Train users to only accept valid push notifications and to report suspicious push notifications.

Vulnerability Scanning
======================

Vulnerability scanning is used to find potentially exploitable software vulnerabilities to remediate them.

ID:M1016

Version:1.1

Created:06 June 2019

Last Modified:14 July 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1016/)

**ATT&CK****Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1190](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1190)

[Exploit Public-Facing Application](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1190)

Regularly scan externally facing systems for vulnerabilities and establish procedures to rapidly patch systems when critical vulnerabilities are discovered through scanning and through public disclosure.[\[1\]](https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Category:OWASP_Top_Ten_Project)

Enterprise

[T1210](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1210)

[Exploitation of Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1210)

Regularly scan the internal network for available services to identify new and potentially vulnerable services.

Enterprise

[T1195](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195)

[Supply Chain Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195)

Continuous monitoring of vulnerability sources and the use of automatic and manual code review tools should also be implemented as well.[\[1\]](https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Category:OWASP_Top_Ten_Project)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/001)

[Compromise Software Dependencies and Development Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/001)

Continuous monitoring of vulnerability sources and the use of automatic and manual code review tools should also be implemented as well.[\[1\]](https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Category:OWASP_Top_Ten_Project)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/002)

[Compromise Software Supply Chain](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/002)

Continuous monitoring of vulnerability sources and the use of automatic and manual code review tools should also be implemented as well.[\[1\]](https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Category:OWASP_Top_Ten_Project)

--------------

1.  [OWASP. (2018, February 23). OWASP Top Ten Project. Retrieved April 3, 2018.](https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Category:OWASP_Top_Ten_Project)

Mobile Mitigations
==================

Mitigations represent security concepts and classes of technologies that can be used to prevent a technique or sub-technique from being successfully executed.

###### Mitigations: 13

**ID**

**Name**

**Description**

[M1058](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1058)

[Antivirus/Antimalware](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1058)

Mobile security products, such as Mobile Threat Defense (MTD), offer various device-based mitigations against certain behaviors.

[M1013](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1013)

[Application Developer Guidance](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1013)

This mitigation describes any guidance or training given to developers of applications to avoid introducing security weaknesses that an adversary may be able to take advantage of.

[M1002](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1002)

[Attestation](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1002)

Enable remote attestation capabilities when available (such as Android SafetyNet or Samsung Knox TIMA Attestation) and prohibit devices that fail the attestation from accessing enterprise resources.

[M1010](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1010)

[Deploy Compromised Device Detection Method](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1010)

A variety of methods exist that can be used to enable enterprises to identify compromised (e.g. rooted/jailbroken) devices, whether using security mechanisms built directly into the device, third-party mobile security applications, enterprise mobility management (EMM)/mobile device management (MDM) capabilities, or other methods. Some methods may be trivial to evade while others may be more sophisticated.

[M1059](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1059)

[Do Not Mitigate](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1059)

This category is to associate techniques that mitigation might increase risk of compromise and therefore mitigation is not recommended.

[M1009](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1009)

[Encrypt Network Traffic](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1009)

Application developers should encrypt all of their application network traffic using the Transport Layer Security (TLS) protocol to ensure protection of sensitive data and deter network-based attacks. If desired, application developers could perform message-based encryption of data before passing it for TLS encryption.

[M1012](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1012)

[Enterprise Policy](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1012)

An enterprise mobility management (EMM), also known as mobile device management (MDM), system can be used to provision policies to mobile devices to control aspects of their allowed behavior.

[M1014](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1014)

[Interconnection Filtering](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1014)

In order to mitigate Signaling System 7 (SS7) exploitation, the Communications, Security, Reliability, and Interoperability Council (CSRIC) describes filtering interconnections between network operators to block inappropriate requests .

[M1003](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1003)

[Lock Bootloader](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1003)

On devices that provide the capability to unlock the bootloader (hence allowing any operating system code to be flashed onto the device), perform periodic checks to ensure that the bootloader is locked.

[M1001](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1001)

[Security Updates](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1001)

Install security updates in response to discovered vulnerabilities.

[M1004](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1004)

[System Partition Integrity](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1004)

Ensure that Android devices being used include and enable the Verified Boot capability, which cryptographically ensures the integrity of the system partition.

[M1006](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1006)

[Use Recent OS Version](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1006)

New mobile operating system versions bring not only patches against discovered vulnerabilities but also often bring security architecture improvements that provide resilience against potential vulnerabilities or weaknesses that have not yet been discovered. They may also bring improvements that block use of observed adversary techniques.

[M1011](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1011)

[User Guidance](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1011)

Describes any guidance or training given to users to set particular configuration settings or avoid specific potentially risky behaviors.

Antivirus/Antimalware
=====================

Mobile security products, such as Mobile Threat Defense (MTD), offer various device-based mitigations against certain behaviors.

ID:M1058

Version:1.0

Created:21 September 2023

Last Modified:21 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1058/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Mobile

[T1664](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1664)

[Exploitation for Initial Access](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1664)

Mobile security products can potentially detect if a device is vulnerable to a known exploit and can alert the user to update their device.

Mobile

[T1660](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1660)

[Phishing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1660)

Some mobile security products offer a loopback VPN used for inspecting traffic. This could proactively block traffic to websites that are known for phishing or appear to be conducting a phishing attack.

Application Developer Guidance
==============================

This mitigation describes any guidance or training given to developers of applications to avoid introducing security weaknesses that an adversary may be able to take advantage of.

ID:M1013

Version:1.1

Created:25 October 2017

Last Modified:27 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1013/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Enterprise

[T1212](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1212)

[Exploitation for Credential Access](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1212)

Application developers should consider taking measures to validate authentication requests by enabling one-time passwords, providing timestamps or sequence numbers for messages sent, using digital signatures, and/or using random session keys.[\[1\]](https://www.comparitech.com/blog/information-security/what-is-a-replay-attack/)[\[2\]](https://www.bugcrowd.com/glossary/replay-attack/)

Enterprise

[T1564](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564)

[Hide Artifacts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564)

Application developers should consider limiting the requirements for custom or otherwise difficult to manage file/folder exclusions. Where possible, install applications to trusted system folder paths that are already protected by restricted file and directory permissions.

[.009](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/009)

[Resource Forking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/009)

Configure applications to use the application bundle structure which leverages the`/Resources`folder location.[\[3\]](https://support.apple.com/guide/security/app-security-overview-sec35dd877d0/1/web/1)

[.012](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/012)

[File/Path Exclusions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/012)

Application developers should consider limiting the requirements for custom or otherwise difficult to manage file/folder exclusions. Where possible, install applications to trusted system folder paths that are already protected by restricted file and directory permissions.

Enterprise

[T1574](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

[Hijack Execution Flow](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574)

When possible, include hash values in manifest files to help prevent side-loading of malicious libraries.[\[4\]](https://www.fireeye.com/content/dam/fireeye-www/global/en/current-threats/pdfs/rpt-dll-sideloading.pdf)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/002)

[DLL Side-Loading](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1574/002)

When possible, include hash values in manifest files to help prevent side-loading of malicious libraries.[\[4\]](https://www.fireeye.com/content/dam/fireeye-www/global/en/current-threats/pdfs/rpt-dll-sideloading.pdf)

Enterprise

[T1559](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559)

[Inter-Process Communication](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559)

Enable the Hardened Runtime capability when developing applications. Do not include the`com.apple.security.get-task-allow`entitlement with the value set to any variation of true.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559/003)

[XPC Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1559/003)

Enable the Hardened Runtime capability when developing applications. Do not include the`com.apple.security.get-task-allow`entitlement with the value set to any variation of true.

Enterprise

[T1647](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1647)

[Plist File Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1647)

Ensure applications are using Apple's developer guidance which enables hardened runtime.[\[5\]](https://developer.apple.com/documentation/security/hardened_runtime)

Enterprise

[T1593](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1593)

[Search Open Websites/Domains](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1593)

Application developers uploading to public code repositories should be careful to avoid publishing sensitive information such as credentials and API keys.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1593/003)

[Code Repositories](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1593/003)

Application developers uploading to public code repositories should be careful to avoid publishing sensitive information such as credentials and API keys.

Enterprise

[T1195](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195)

[Supply Chain Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195)

Application developers should be cautious when selecting third-party libraries to integrate into their application. Additionally, where possible, developers should lock software dependencies to specific versions rather than pulling the latest version on build.[\[6\]](https://www.cidersecurity.io/top-10-cicd-security-risks/)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/001)

[Compromise Software Dependencies and Development Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/001)

Application developers should be cautious when selecting third-party libraries to integrate into their application. Additionally, where possible, developers should lock software dependencies to specific versions rather than pulling the latest version on build.[\[6\]](https://www.cidersecurity.io/top-10-cicd-security-risks/)

Enterprise

[T1550](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

[Use Alternate Authentication Material](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550)

Consider implementing token binding strategies, such as Azure AD token protection or OAuth Proof of Possession, that cryptographically bind a token to a secret. This may prevent the token from being used without knowledge of the secret or possession of the device the token is tied to.[\[7\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/entra/identity/conditional-access/concept-token-protection)[\[8\]](https://www.okta.com/blog/2023/06/a-leap-forward-in-token-security-okta-adds-support-for-dpop/)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/001)

[Application Access Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1550/001)

Consider implementing token binding strategies, such as Azure AD token protection or OAuth Proof of Possession, that cryptographically bind a token to a secret. This may prevent the token from being used without knowledge of the secret or possession of the device the token is tied to.[\[7\]](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/entra/identity/conditional-access/concept-token-protection)[\[8\]](https://www.okta.com/blog/2023/06/a-leap-forward-in-token-security-okta-adds-support-for-dpop/)

Enterprise

[T1078](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

[Valid Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078)

Ensure that applications do not store sensitive data or credentials insecurely. (e.g. plaintext credentials in code, published credentials in repositories, or credentials in public cloud storage).

Mobile

[T1626](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1626)

[Abuse Elevation Control Mechanism](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1626)

Applications very rarely require administrator permission. Developers should be cautioned against using this higher degree of access to avoid being flagged as a potentially malicious application.

Mobile

[T1517](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1517)

[Access Notifications](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1517)

Application developers could be encouraged to avoid placing sensitive data in notification text.

Mobile

[T1513](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1513)

[Screen Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1513)

Application developers can apply the`FLAG_SECURE`property to sensitive screens within their apps to make it more difficult for the screen contents to be captured.[\[9\]](https://wwws.nightwatchcybersecurity.com/2016/04/13/research-securing-android-applications-from-screen-capture/)

Mobile

[T1635](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635)

[Steal Application Access Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635)

Developers should use Android App Links[\[10\]](https://developer.android.com/training/app-links/verify-site-associations)and iOS Universal Links[\[11\]](https://developer.apple.com/ios/universal-links/)to provide a secure binding between URIs and applications, preventing malicious applications from intercepting redirections. Additionally, for OAuth use cases, PKCE[\[12\]](https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7636)should be used to prevent use of stolen authorization codes.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635/001)

[URI Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635/001)

Developers should use Android App Links[\[10\]](https://developer.android.com/training/app-links/verify-site-associations)and iOS Universal Links[\[11\]](https://developer.apple.com/ios/universal-links/)to provide a secure binding between URIs and applications, preventing malicious applications from intercepting redirections. Additionally, for OAuth use cases, PKCE[\[12\]](https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7636)should be used to prevent use of stolen authorization codes.

Mobile

[T1474](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1474)

[Supply Chain Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1474)

Application developers should be cautious when selecting third-party libraries to integrate into their application.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1474/001)

[Compromise Software Dependencies and Development Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1474/001)

Application developers should be cautious when selecting third-party libraries to integrate into their application.

Attestation
===========

Enable remote attestation capabilities when available (such as Android SafetyNet or Samsung Knox TIMA Attestation) and prohibit devices that fail the attestation from accessing enterprise resources.

Deploy Compromised Device Detection Method
==========================================

A variety of methods exist that can be used to enable enterprises to identify compromised (e.g. rooted/jailbroken) devices, whether using security mechanisms built directly into the device, third-party mobile security applications, enterprise mobility management (EMM)/mobile device management (MDM) capabilities, or other methods. Some methods may be trivial to evade while others may be more sophisticated.

Encrypt Network Traffic
=======================

Application developers should encrypt all of their application network traffic using the Transport Layer Security (TLS) protocol to ensure protection of sensitive data and deter network-based attacks. If desired, application developers could perform message-based encryption of data before passing it for TLS encryption.

iOS's App Transport Security feature can be used to help ensure that all application network traffic is appropriately protected. Apple intends to mandate use of App Transport Security[\[1\]](https://techcrunch.com/2016/06/14/apple-will-require-https-connections-for-ios-apps-by-the-end-of-2016/)for all apps in the Apple App Store unless appropriate justification is given.

Android's Network Security Configuration feature similarly can be used by app developers to help ensure that all of their application network traffic is appropriately protected[\[2\]](https://developer.android.com/training/articles/security-config.html).

Use of Virtual Private Network (VPN) tunnels, e.g. using the IPsec protocol, can help mitigate some types of network attacks as well.

ID:M1009

Version:1.0

Created:25 October 2017

Last Modified:17 October 2018

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1009/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Mobile

[T1638](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1638)

[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1638)

Applications that properly encrypt network traffic may evade some forms of AiTM behavior.

Mobile

[T1422](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1422)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1422/001)

[System Network Configuration Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1422):[Internet Connection Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1422/001)

Ensure that traffic is encrypted to reduce adversaries ability to intercept, decrypt and manipulate traffic.

2.  [Google. (n.d.). Network Security Configuration. Retrieved December 19, 2016.](https://developer.android.com/training/articles/security-config.html)

Enterprise Policy
=================

An enterprise mobility management (EMM), also known as mobile device management (MDM), system can be used to provision policies to mobile devices to control aspects of their allowed behavior.

ID:M1012

Version:1.0

Created:25 October 2017

Last Modified:24 June 2020

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1012/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Mobile

[T1517](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1517)

[Access Notifications](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1517)

On Android devices with a work profile, the`DevicePolicyManager.setPermittedCrossProfileNotificationListeners`method can be used to manage the list of applications running within the personal profile that can access notifications generated within the work profile. This policy would not affect notifications generated by the rest of the device. The`DevicePolicyManager.setApplicationHidden`method can be used to disable notification access for unwanted applications, but this method would also block that entire application from running.[\[1\]](https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/admin/DevicePolicyManager#setPermittedCrossProfileNotificationListeners(android.content.ComponentName,%20java.util.List%3Cjava.lang.String%3E))

Mobile

[T1661](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1661)

[Application Versioning](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1661)

Enterprises can provision policies to mobile devices for application allow-listing, ensuring only approved applications are installed onto mobile devices.

Mobile

[T1521](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1521)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1521/003)

[Encrypted Channel](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1521):[SSL Pinning](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1521/003)

Certain enterprise policies can be applied to prevent users from adding certificates to the device and to prevent applications from being able to install their own certificates.

Mobile

[T1428](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1428)

[Exploitation of Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1428)

Configuration of per-app VPN policies instead of device-wide VPN can restrict access to internal enterprise resource access via VPN to only enterprise-approved applications

Mobile

[T1629](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629)

[Impair Defenses](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629)

An EMM/MDM can use the Android`DevicePolicyManager.setPermittedAccessibilityServices`method to set an explicit list of applications that are allowed to use Android's accessibility features.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629/001)

[Prevent Application Removal](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629/001)

An EMM/MDM can use the Android`DevicePolicyManager.setPermittedAccessibilityServices`method to set an explicit list of applications that are allowed to use Android's accessibility features.

Mobile

[T1417](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417)

[Input Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417)

When using Samsung Knox, third-party keyboards must be explicitly added to an allow list in order to be available to the end-user.[\[2\]](https://support.samsungknox.com/hc/en-us/articles/360001485027-3rd-party-keyboards-must-be-whitelisted-)An EMM/MDM can use the Android`DevicePolicyManager.setPermittedAccessibilityServices`method to set an explicit list of applications that are allowed to use Android's accessibility features.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417/001)

[Keylogging](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417/001)

When using Samsung Knox, third-party keyboards must be explicitly added to an allow list in order to be available to the end-user.[\[2\]](https://support.samsungknox.com/hc/en-us/articles/360001485027-3rd-party-keyboards-must-be-whitelisted-)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417/002)

[GUI Input Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417/002)

An EMM/MDM can use the Android`DevicePolicyManager.setPermittedAccessibilityServices`method to set an explicit list of applications that are allowed to use Android's accessibility features.

Mobile

[T1516](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1516)

[Input Injection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1516)

An EMM/MDM can use the Android`DevicePolicyManager.setPermittedAccessibilityServices`method to set an explicit list of applications that are allowed to use Android's accessibility features.

Mobile

[T1430](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1430)

[Location Tracking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1430)

If devices are enrolled using Apple User Enrollment or using a profile owner enrollment mode for Android, device controls prevent the enterprise from accessing the devices physical location. This is typically used for a Bring Your Own Device (BYOD) deployment.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1430/001)

[Remote Device Management Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1430/001)

If devices are enrolled using Apple User Enrollment or using a profile owner enrollment mode for Android, device controls prevent the enterprise from accessing the devices physical location. This is typically used for a Bring Your Own Device (BYOD) deployment.

Mobile

[T1461](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1461)

[Lockscreen Bypass](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1461)

Enterprises can provision policies to mobile devices that require a minimum complexity (length, character requirements, etc.) for the device passcode, and cause the device to wipe all data if an incorrect passcode is entered too many times. Both policies would mitigate brute-force, guessing, or shoulder surfing of the device passcode. Enterprises can also provision policies to disable biometric authentication, however, biometric authentication can help make using a longer, more complex passcode more practical because it does not need to be entered as frequently.

Mobile

[T1663](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1663)

[Remote Access Software](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1663)

When devices are enrolled in an EMM/MDM using device owner (iOS) or fully managed (Android) mode, the EMM/MDM can collect a list of installed applications on the device. An administrator can then act on, for example blocking, specific remote access applications from being installed on managed devices.

Mobile

[T1458](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1458)

[Replication Through Removable Media](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1458)

Enterprise policies should prevent enabling USB debugging on Android devices unless specifically needed (e.g., if the device is used for application development).

Mobile

[T1513](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1513)

[Screen Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1513)

Enterprise policies should block access to the Android Debug Bridge (ADB) by preventing users from enabling USB debugging on Android devices unless specifically needed (e.g., if the device is used for application development). An EMM/MDM can use the Android`DevicePolicyManager.setPermittedAccessibilityServices`method to set an explicit list of applications that are allowed to use Android's accessibility features.

Mobile

[T1632](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1632)

[Subvert Trust Controls](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1632)

On iOS, the`allowEnterpriseAppTrust`and`allowEnterpriseAppTrustModification`configuration profile restrictions can be used to prevent users from installing apps signed using enterprise distribution keys.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1632/001)

[Code Signing Policy Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1632/001)

On iOS, the`allowEnterpriseAppTrust`and`allowEnterpriseAppTrustModification`configuration profile restrictions can be used to prevent users from installing apps signed using enterprise distribution keys.

Interconnection Filtering
=========================

In order to mitigate Signaling System 7 (SS7) exploitation, the Communications, Security, Reliability, and Interoperability Council (CSRIC) describes filtering interconnections between network operators to block inappropriate requests[\[1\]](https://web.archive.org/web/20200330012714/https:/www.fcc.gov/files/csric5-wg10-finalreport031517pdf).

Version:1.0

**Use**

[Location Tracking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1430)

Filtering requests by checking request origin information may provide some defense against spurious operators.[\[1\]](https://web.archive.org/web/20200330012714/https:/www.fcc.gov/files/csric5-wg10-finalreport031517pdf)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1430/002)

[Impersonate SS7 Nodes](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1430/002)

Filtering requests by checking request origin information may provide some defense against spurious operators.\[2\]

Lock Bootloader
===============

On devices that provide the capability to unlock the bootloader (hence allowing any operating system code to be flashed onto the device), perform periodic checks to ensure that the bootloader is locked.

ID:M1003

Version:1.0

Created:25 October 2017

Last Modified:17 October 2018

**Name**

**Use**

Mobile

[T1398](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1398)

[Boot or Logon Initialization Scripts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1398)

A locked bootloader could prevent unauthorized modifications to protected operating system files.

Mobile

[T1645](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1645)

[Compromise Client Software Binary](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1645)

A locked bootloader could prevent unauthorized modifications of protected operating system files.

Mobile

[T1458](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1458)

[Replication Through Removable Media](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1458)

Users should ensure bootloaders are locked to prevent arbitrary operating system code from being flashed onto the device.

Security Updates
================

Install security updates in response to discovered vulnerabilities.

Purchase devices with a vendor and/or mobile carrier commitment to provide security updates in a prompt manner for a set period of time.

Decommission devices that will no longer receive security updates.

Limit or block access to enterprise resources from devices that have not installed recent security updates.

On Android devices, access can be controlled based on each device's security patch level. On iOS devices, access can be controlled based on the iOS version.

Security updates may contain patches that inhibit system software compromises.

System Partition Integrity
==========================

Ensure that Android devices being used include and enable the Verified Boot capability, which cryptographically ensures the integrity of the system partition.

ID:M1004

Version:1.0

Created:25 October 2017

Last Modified:17 October 2018

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1004/)

**ATT&CK****Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Mobile

[T1398](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1398)

[Boot or Logon Initialization Scripts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1398)

Android and iOS include system partition integrity mechanisms that could detect unauthorized modifications.

Mobile

[T1645](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1645)

[Compromise Client Software Binary](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1645)

Android includes system partition integrity mechanisms that could detect unauthorized modifications.

Mobile

[T1625](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1625)

[Hijack Execution Flow](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1625)

Android Verified Boot can detect unauthorized modifications made to the system partition, which could lead to execution flow hijacking.[\[1\]](https://source.android.com/security/verifiedboot/)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1625/001)

[System Runtime API Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1625/001)

Android Verified Boot can detect unauthorized modifications made to the system partition, which could lead to execution flow hijacking.[\[1\]](https://source.android.com/security/verifiedboot/)

Mobile

[T1629](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629)

[Impair Defenses](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629)

System partition integrity mechanisms, such as Verified Boot, can detect the unauthorized modification of system files.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629/003)

[Disable or Modify Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629/003)

System partition integrity mechanisms, such as Verified Boot, can detect the unauthorized modification of system files.

Mobile

[T1474](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1474)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1474/003)

[Supply Chain Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1474):[Compromise Software Supply Chain](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1474/003)

Ensure Verified Boot is enabled on devices with that capability.

**References**
--------------

1.  [Android. (n.d.). Verified Boot. Retrieved December 21, 2016.](https://source.android.com/security/verifiedboot/)

Use Recent OS Version
=====================

New mobile operating system versions bring not only patches against discovered vulnerabilities but also often bring security architecture improvements that provide resilience against potential vulnerabilities or weaknesses that have not yet been discovered. They may also bring improvements that block use of observed adversary techniques.

ID:M1006

Version:1.0

Created:25 October 2017

Last Modified:17 October 2018

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1006/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Mobile

[T1626](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1626)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1626/001)

[Abuse Elevation Control Mechanism](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1626):[Device Administrator Permissions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1626/001)

Changes were introduced in Android 7 to make abuse of device administrator permissions more difficult.[\[1\]](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XZzLjllizYs)

Mobile

[T1638](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1638)

[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1638)

Recent OS versions have made it more difficult for applications to register as VPN providers.

Mobile

[T1661](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1661)

[Application Versioning](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1661)

Android 11 and above implement application hibernation, which can hibernate an application that has not been used for a few months and can reset the applications permission requests.[\[2\]](https://developer.android.com/topic/performance/app-hibernation)

Mobile

[T1429](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1429)

[Audio Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1429)

Android 9 and above restricts access to microphone, camera, and other sensors from background applications.[\[3\]](https://developer.android.com/about/versions/pie/android-9.0-changes-all#bg-sensor-access)

Mobile

[T1414](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1414)

[Clipboard Data](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1414)

Android 10 introduced changes to prevent applications from accessing clipboard data if they are not in the foreground or set as the devices default IME.[\[4\]](https://developer.android.com/about/versions/10/privacy/changes#clipboard-data)

Mobile

[T1577](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1577)

[Compromise Application Executable](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1577)

Many vulnerabilities related to injecting code into existing applications have been patched in previous Android releases.

Mobile

[T1641](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1641)

[Data Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1641)

Recent OS versions have limited access to certain APIs unless certain conditions are met, making[Data Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1641)more difficult

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1641/001)

[Transmitted Data Manipulation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1641/001)

Android 10 prevents applications from accessing clipboard data unless the application is on the foreground or is set as the devices default input method editor (IME).[\[4\]](https://developer.android.com/about/versions/10/privacy/changes#clipboard-data)

Mobile

[T1407](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1407)

[Download New Code at Runtime](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1407)

Applications that target Android API level 29 or higher cannot execute native code stored in the application's internal data storage directory, limiting the ability of applications to download and execute native code at runtime.[\[5\]](https://developer.android.com/about/versions/10/behavior-changes-all#execute-permission)

Mobile

[T1642](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1642)

[Endpoint Denial of Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1642)

Android 7 changed how the Device Administrator password APIs function.

Mobile

[T1624](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1624)

[Event Triggered Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1624)

Android 8 introduced additional limitations on the implicit intents that an application can register for.[\[6\]](https://developer.android.com/guide/components/broadcasts#changes-system-broadcasts)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1624/001)

[Broadcast Receivers](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1624/001)

Android 8 introduced additional limitations on the implicit intents that an application can register for.[\[6\]](https://developer.android.com/guide/components/broadcasts#changes-system-broadcasts)

Mobile

[T1627](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1627)

[Execution Guardrails](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1627)

New OS releases frequently contain additional limitations or controls around device location access.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1627/001)

[Geofencing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1627/001)

New OS releases frequently contain additional limitations or controls around device location access.

Mobile

[T1420](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1420)

[File and Directory Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1420)

Security architecture improvements in each new version of Android and iOS make it more difficult to escalate privileges. Additionally, newer versions of Android have strengthened the sandboxing applied to applications, restricting their ability to enumerate file system contents.

Mobile

[T1628](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1628)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1628/001)

[Hide Artifacts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1628):[Suppress Application Icon](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1628/001)

Android 10 introduced changes to prevent malicious applications from fully suppressing their icon in the launcher.[\[7\]](https://source.android.com/setup/start/android-10-release#limitations_to_hiding_app_icons)[\[8\]](https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/android/content/pm/LauncherApps#getactivitylist)

Mobile

[T1629](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629/001)

[Impair Defenses](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629):[Prevent Application Removal](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629/001)

Recent versions of Android modified how device administrator applications are uninstalled, making it easier for the user to remove them.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629/002)

[Impair Defenses](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629):[Device Lockout](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629/002)

Recent versions of Android modified how device administrator applications are uninstalled, making it easier for the user to remove them. Android 7 introduced updates that revoke standard device administrators ability to reset the devices passcode.

Mobile

[T1417](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417)

[Input Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417)

The`HIDE_OVERLAY_WINDOWS`permission was introduced in Android 12 allowing apps to hide overlay windows of type`TYPE_APPLICATION_OVERLAY`drawn by other apps with the`SYSTEM_ALERT_WINDOW`permission, preventing other applications from creating overlay windows on top of the current application.[\[9\]](https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417/002)

[GUI Input Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417/002)

The`HIDE_OVERLAY_WINDOWS`permission was introduced in Android 12 allowing apps to hide overlay windows of type`TYPE_APPLICATION_OVERLAY`drawn by other apps with the`SYSTEM_ALERT_WINDOW`permission, preventing other applications from creating overlay windows on top of the current application.[\[9\]](https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features)

Mobile

[T1430](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1430)

[Location Tracking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1430)

On Android 11 and up, users are not prompted with the option to select "Allow all the time" and must navigate to the settings page to manually select this option. On iOS 14 and up, users can select whether to provide Precise Location for each installed application.

Mobile

[T1424](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1424)

[Process Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1424)

Android 7 and later iOS versions introduced changes that prevent applications from performing Process Discovery without elevated privileges.

Mobile

[T1636](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1636)

[Protected User Data](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1636)

OS feature updates often enhance security and privacy around permissions.

Mobile

[T1458](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1458)

[Replication Through Removable Media](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1458)

iOS 11.4.1 and higher introduce USB Restricted Mode, which disables data access through the device's charging port under certain conditions (making the port only usable for power), likely preventing this technique from working.[\[10\]](https://blog.elcomsoft.com/2018/09/ios-12-enhances-usb-restricted-mode/)

Mobile

[T1418](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1418)

[Software Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1418)

Android 11 introduced privacy enhancements to package visibility, filtering results that are returned from the package manager. iOS 12 removed the private API that could previously be used to list installed applications on non-app store applications.[\[11\]](https://developer.android.com/training/package-visibility)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1418/001)

[Security Software Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1418/001)

Android 11 introduced privacy enhancements to package visibility, filtering results that are returned from the package manager. iOS 12 removed the private API that could previously be used to list installed applications on non-app store applications.[\[11\]](https://developer.android.com/training/package-visibility)

Mobile

[T1635](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635)

[Steal Application Access Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635)

iOS 11 introduced a first-come-first-served principle for URIs, allowing only the prior installed app to be launched via the URI.[\[12\]](https://blog.trendmicro.com/trendlabs-security-intelligence/ios-url-scheme-susceptible-to-hijacking/)Android 6 introduced App Links.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635/001)

[URI Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635/001)

iOS 11 introduced a first-come-first-served principle for URIs, allowing only the prior installed app to be launched via the URI.[\[12\]](https://blog.trendmicro.com/trendlabs-security-intelligence/ios-url-scheme-susceptible-to-hijacking/)Android 6 introduced App Links.

Mobile

[T1409](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1409)

[Stored Application Data](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1409)

Android 9 introduced a new security policy that prevents applications from reading or writing data to other applications internal storage directories, regardless of permissions.

Mobile

[T1632](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1632)

[Subvert Trust Controls](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1632)

Mobile OSes have implemented measures to make it more difficult to trick users into installing untrusted certificates and configurations. iOS 10.3 and higher add an additional step for users to install new trusted CA certificates and configuration profiles. On Android, apps that target compatibility with Android 7 and higher (API Level 24) default to only trusting CA certificates that are bundled with the operating system, not CA certificates that are added by the user or administrator, hence decreasing their susceptibility to successful adversary-in-the-middle attack.[\[13\]](https://www.symantec.com/connect/blogs/apple-ios-103-finally-battles-malicious-profiles)[\[14\]](https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2016/07/changes-to-trusted-certificate.html)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1632/001)

[Code Signing Policy Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1632/001)

Mobile OSes have implemented measures to make it more difficult to trick users into installing untrusted certificates and configurations. iOS 10.3 and higher add an additional step for users to install new trusted CA certificates and configuration profiles. On Android, apps that target compatibility with Android 7 and higher (API Level 24) default to only trusting CA certificates that are bundled with the operating system, not CA certificates that are added by the user or administrator, hence decreasing their susceptibility to successful adversary-in-the-middle attack.[\[13\]](https://www.symantec.com/connect/blogs/apple-ios-103-finally-battles-malicious-profiles)[\[14\]](https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2016/07/changes-to-trusted-certificate.html)

Mobile

[T1422](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1422)

[System Network Configuration Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1422)

Android 10 introduced changes that prevent normal applications from accessing sensitive device identifiers.[\[15\]](https://developer.android.com/reference/android/telephony/TelephonyManager.html)

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1422/002)

[Wi-Fi Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1422/002)

Android 10 introduced changes that prevent normal applications from accessing sensitive device identifiers.[\[15\]](https://developer.android.com/reference/android/telephony/TelephonyManager.html)

Mobile

[T1512](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1512)

[Video Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1512)

Android 9 and above restricts access to the mic, camera, and other device sensors from applications running in the background. iOS 14 and Android 12 introduced a visual indicator on the status bar (green dot) when an application is accessing the devices camera.[\[3\]](https://developer.android.com/about/versions/pie/android-9.0-changes-all#bg-sensor-access)

User Guidance
=============

Describes any guidance or training given to users to set particular configuration settings or avoid specific potentially risky behaviors.

ID:M1011

Version:1.0

Created:18 October 2019

Last Modified:18 October 2019

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M1011/)

**ATT&CK****Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

Mobile

[T1626](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1626)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1626/001)

[Abuse Elevation Control Mechanism](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1626):[Device Administrator Permissions](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1626/001)

Users should scrutinize every device administration permission request. If the request is not expected or the user does not recognize the application, the application should be uninstalled immediately.

Mobile

[T1517](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1517)

[Access Notifications](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1517)

Users should be wary of granting applications dangerous or privacy-intrusive permissions, such as access to notifications.

Mobile

[T1640](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1640)

[Account Access Removal](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1640)

Users should be taught that Device Administrator permissions are very dangerous, and very few applications need it.

Mobile

[T1429](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1429)

[Audio Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1429)

Users should be wary of granting applications dangerous or privacy-intrusive permissions, such as access to microphone or audio output.

Mobile

[T1616](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1616)

[Call Control](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1616)

Users should be encouraged to be very careful with what applications they grant phone call-based permissions to. Further, users should not change their default call handler to applications they do not recognize.

Mobile

[T1662](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1662)

[Data Destruction](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1662)

Users should be trained on what device administrator permission request prompts look like, and how to avoid granting permissions on phishing popups.

Mobile

[T1521](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1521)

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1521/003)

[Encrypted Channel](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1521):[SSL Pinning](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1521/003)

Users should be advised to not trust or install self-signed certificates.

Mobile

[T1642](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1642)

[Endpoint Denial of Service](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1642)

Users should be cautioned against granting administrative access to applications.

Mobile

[T1627](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1627)

[Execution Guardrails](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1627)

Users should be advised to be extra scrutinous of applications that request location or sensitive phone information permissions, and to deny any permissions requests for applications they do not recognize.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1627/001)

[Geofencing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1627/001)

Users should be advised to be extra scrutinous of applications that request location, and to deny any permissions requests for applications they do not recognize.

Mobile

[T1658](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1658)

[Exploitation for Client Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1658)

Users should be wary of iMessages from unknown senders. Additionally, users should be instructed not to open unrecognized links or other attachments in text messages.

Mobile

[T1541](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1541)

[Foreground Persistence](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1541)

If a user sees a persistent notification they do not recognize, they should uninstall the source application and look for other unwanted applications or anomalies.

Mobile

[T1643](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1643)

[Generate Traffic from Victim](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1643)

Users should be advised that applications generally do not require permission to send SMS messages.

Mobile

[T1628](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1628)

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1628/001)

[Hide Artifacts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1628):[Suppress Application Icon](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1628/001)

Users should be shown what a synthetic activity looks like so they can scrutinize them in the future.

Mobile

[T1629](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629)

[Impair Defenses](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629)

Providing user guidance around commonly abused features, such as the modal that requests for administrator permissions, should aid in preventing impairing defenses.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629/001)

[Prevent Application Removal](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629/001)

Users should be warned against granting access to accessibility features and device administration services, and to carefully scrutinize applications that request these dangerous permissions. Users should be taught how to boot into safe mode to uninstall malicious applications that may be interfering with the uninstallation process.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629/003)

[Disable or Modify Tools](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1629/003)

Users should be taught the dangers of rooting or jailbreaking their device.

Mobile

[T1630](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1630)

[Indicator Removal on Host](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1630)

Inform users that device rooting or granting unnecessary access to the accessibility service presents security risks that could be taken advantage of without their knowledge.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1630/001)

[Uninstall Malicious Application](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1630/001)

Inform users that device rooting or granting unnecessary access to the accessibility service presents security risks that could be taken advantage of without their knowledge.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1630/002)

[File Deletion](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1630/002)

Users should be trained on what device administrator permission request prompts look like, and how to avoid granting permissions on phishing popups.

Mobile

[T1417](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417)

[Input Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417)

Users should be wary of granting applications dangerous or privacy-intrusive permissions, such as keyboard registration or accessibility service access.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417/001)

[Keylogging](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1417/001)

Users should be wary of granting applications dangerous or privacy-intrusive permissions, such as keyboard registration or accessibility service access.

Mobile

[T1516](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1516)

[Input Injection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1516)

Users should be warned against granting access to accessibility features, and to carefully scrutinize applications that request this dangerous permission.

Mobile

[T1430](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1430)

[Location Tracking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1430)

Users should be wary of granting applications dangerous or privacy-intrusive permissions, such as access to location information. Users should also protect their account credentials and enable multi-factor authentication options when available.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1430/001)

[Remote Device Management Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1430/001)

Users should protect their account credentials and enable multi-factor authentication options when available.

Mobile

[T1655](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1655)

[Masquerading](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1655)

Users should be encouraged to only install apps from authorized app stores, which are less likely to contain malicious repackaged apps.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1655/001)

[Match Legitimate Name or Location](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1655/001)

Users should be encouraged to only install apps from authorized app stores, which are less likely to contain malicious repackaged apps.

Mobile

[T1644](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1644)

[Out of Band Data](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1644)

Users should be instructed to not grant applications unexpected or unnecessary permissions.

Mobile

[T1660](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1660)

[Phishing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1660)

Users can be trained to identify social engineering techniques and phishing emails.

Mobile

[T1636](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1636)

[Protected User Data](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1636)

Users should be taught the danger behind granting unnecessary permissions to an application and should be advised to use extra scrutiny when an application requests them.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1636/001)

[Calendar Entries](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1636/001)

Calendar access is an uncommonly needed permission, so users should be instructed to use extra scrutiny when granting access to their device calendar.

[.002](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1636/002)

[Call Log](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1636/002)

Call Log access an uncommonly needed permission, so users should be instructedto use extra scrutiny when granting access to their call logs.

[.003](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1636/003)

[Contact List](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1636/003)

Contact list access is an uncommonly needed permission, so users should be instructed to use extra scrutiny when granting access to their contact list.

[.004](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1636/004)

[SMS Messages](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1636/004)

Access to SMS messages is an uncommonly needed permission, so users should be instructed to use extra scrutiny when granting access to their SMS messages.

Mobile

[T1663](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1663)

[Remote Access Software](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1663)

Users should be encouraged to be very careful with granting dangerous permissions, such as device administrator or access to device accessibility.

Mobile

[T1458](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1458)

[Replication Through Removable Media](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1458)

Users should be advised not to use public charging stations or computers to charge their devices. Instead, users should be issued a charger acquired from a trustworthy source. Users should be advised not to click on device prompts to trust attached computers unless absolutely necessary.

Mobile

[T1513](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1513)

[Screen Capture](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1513)

Users should be advised not to grant consent for screen captures to occur unless expected. Users should avoid enabling USB debugging (Android Debug Bridge) unless explicitly required.

Mobile

[T1582](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1582)

[SMS Control](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1582)

Users should be encouraged to be very careful with what applications they grant SMS access to. Further, users should not change their default SMS handler to applications they do not recognize.[\[1\]](https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2013/10/getting-your-sms-apps-ready-for-kitkat.html)

Mobile

[T1418](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1418)

[Software Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1418)

iOS users should be instructed to not download applications from unofficial sources, as applications distributed via the Apple App Store cannot list installed applications on a device.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1418/001)

[Security Software Discovery](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1418/001)

iOS users should be instructed to not download applications from unofficial sources, as applications distributed via the Apple App Store cannot list installed applications on a device.

Mobile

[T1635](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635)

[Steal Application Access Token](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635)

Users should be instructed to not open links in applications they dont recognize.

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635/001)

[URI Hijacking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1635/001)

Users should be instructed to not open links in applications they dont recognize.

Mobile

[T1632](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1632)

[Subvert Trust Controls](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1632)

Typically, insecure or malicious configuration settings are not installed without the user's consent. Users should be advised not to install unexpected configuration settings (CA certificates, iOS Configuration Profiles, Mobile Device Management server provisioning).

[.001](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1632/001)

[Code Signing Policy Modification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1632/001)

Typically, insecure or malicious configuration settings are not installed without the user's consent. Users should be advised not to install unexpected configuration settings (CA certificates, iOS Configuration Profiles, Mobile Device Management server provisioning).
