ICS Mitigations
===============

Mitigations represent security concepts and classes of technologies that can be used to prevent a technique or sub-technique from being successfully executed.

###### Mitigations: 52

**ID**

**Name**

**Description**

[M0801](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0801)

[Access Management](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0801)

Access Management technologies can be used to enforce authorization polices and decisions, especially when existing field devices do not provided sufficient capabilities to support user identification and authentication. These technologies typically utilize an in-line network device or gateway system to prevent access to unauthenticated users, while also integrating with an authentication service to first verify user credentials.

[M0936](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0936)

[Account Use Policies](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0936)

Configure features related to account use like login attempt lockouts, specific login times, etc.

[M0915](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0915)

[Active Directory Configuration](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0915)

Configure Active Directory to prevent use of certain techniques; use security identifier (SID) Filtering, etc.

[M0949](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0949)

[Antivirus/Antimalware](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0949)

Use signatures or heuristics to detect malicious software. Within industrial control environments, antivirus/antimalware installations should be limited to assets that are not involved in critical or real-time operations. To minimize the impact to system availability, all products should first be validated within a representative test environment before deployment to production systems.

[M0913](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0913)

[Application Developer Guidance](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0913)

This mitigation describes any guidance or training given to developers of applications to avoid introducing security weaknesses that an adversary may be able to take advantage of.

[M0948](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0948)

[Application Isolation and Sandboxing](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0948)

Restrict the execution of code to a virtual environment on or in-transit to an endpoint system.

[M0947](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0947)

[Audit](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0947)

Perform audits or scans of systems, permissions, insecure software, insecure configurations, etc. to identify potential weaknesses. Perform periodic integrity checks of the device to validate the correctness of the firmware, software, programs, and configurations. Integrity checks, which typically include cryptographic hashes or digital signatures, should be compared to those obtained at known valid states, especially after events like device reboots, program downloads, or program restarts.

[M0800](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0800)

[Authorization Enforcement](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0800)

The device or system should restrict read, manipulate, or execute privileges to only authenticated users who require access based on approved security policies. Role-based Access Control (RBAC) schemes can help reduce the overhead of assigning permissions to the large number of devices within an ICS. For example, IEC 62351 provides examples of roles used to support common system operations within the electric power sector , while IEEE 1686 defines standard permissions for users of IEDs.

[M0946](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0946)

[Boot Integrity](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0946)

Use secure methods to boot a system and verify the integrity of the operating system and loading mechanisms.

[M0945](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0945)

[Code Signing](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0945)

Enforce binary and application integrity with digital signature verification to prevent untrusted code from executing.

[M0802](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0802)

[Communication Authenticity](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0802)

When communicating over an untrusted network, utilize secure network protocols that both authenticate the message sender and can verify its integrity. This can be done either through message authentication codes (MACs) or digital signatures, to detect spoofed network messages and unauthorized connections.

[M0953](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0953)

[Data Backup](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0953)

Take and store data backups from end user systems and critical servers. Ensure backup and storage systems are hardened and kept separate from the corporate network to prevent compromise. Maintain and exercise incident response plans , including the management of 'gold-copy' back-up images and configurations for key systems to enable quick recovery and response from adversarial activities that impact control, view, or availability.

[M0803](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0803)

[Data Loss Prevention](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0803)

Data Loss Prevention (DLP) technologies can be used to help identify adversarial attempts to exfiltrate operational information, such as engineering plans, trade secrets, recipes, intellectual property, or process telemetry. DLP functionality may be built into other security products such as firewalls or standalone suites running on the network and host-based agents. DLP may be configured to prevent the transfer of information through corporate resources such as email, web, and physical media such as USB for host-based solutions.

[M0942](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0942)

[Disable or Remove Feature or Program](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0942)

Remove or deny access to unnecessary and potentially vulnerable software to prevent abuse by adversaries.

[M0808](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0808)

[Encrypt Network Traffic](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0808)

Utilize strong cryptographic techniques and protocols to prevent eavesdropping on network communications.

[M0941](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0941)

[Encrypt Sensitive Information](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0941)

Protect sensitive data-at-rest with strong encryption.

[M0938](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0938)

[Execution Prevention](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0938)

Block execution of code on a system through application control, and/or script blocking.

[M0950](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0950)

[Exploit Protection](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0950)

Use capabilities to detect and block conditions that may lead to or be indicative of a software exploit occurring.

[M0937](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0937)

[Filter Network Traffic](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0937)

Use network appliances to filter ingress or egress traffic and perform protocol-based filtering. Configure software on endpoints to filter network traffic. Perform inline allow/denylisting of network messages based on the application layer (OSI Layer 7) protocol, especially for automation protocols. Application allowlists are beneficial when there are well-defined communication sequences, types, rates, or patterns needed during expected system operations. Application denylists may be needed if all acceptable communication sequences cannot be defined, but instead a set of known malicious uses can be denied (e.g., excessive communication attempts, shutdown messages, invalid commands). Devices performing these functions are often referred to as deep-packet inspection (DPI) firewalls, context-aware firewalls, or firewalls blocking specific automation/SCADA protocol aware firewalls.

[M0804](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0804)

[Human User Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0804)

Require user authentication before allowing access to data or accepting commands to a device. While strong multi-factor authentication is preferable, it is not always feasible within ICS environments. Performing strong user authentication also requires additional security controls and processes which are often the target of related adversarial techniques (e.g., Valid Accounts, Default Credentials). Therefore, associated ATT&CK mitigations should be considered in addition to this, including[Multi-factor Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0932),[Account Use Policies](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0936),[Password Policies](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0927),[User Account Management](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0918),[Privileged Account Management](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0926), and[User Account Control](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1052).

[M0935](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0935)

[Limit Access to Resource Over Network](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0935)

Prevent access to file shares, remote access to systems, unnecessary services. Mechanisms to limit access may include use of network concentrators, RDP gateways, etc.

[M0934](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0934)

[Limit Hardware Installation](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0934)

Block users or groups from installing or using unapproved hardware on systems, including USB devices.

[M0805](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0805)

[Mechanical Protection Layers](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0805)

Utilize a layered protection design based on physical or mechanical protection systems to prevent damage to property, equipment, human safety, or the environment. Examples include interlocks, rupture disk, release values, etc.

[M0806](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0806)

[Minimize Wireless Signal Propagation](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0806)

Wireless signals frequently propagate outside of organizational boundaries, which provide opportunities for adversaries to monitor or gain unauthorized access to the wireless network. To minimize this threat, organizations should implement measures to detect, understand, and reduce unnecessary RF propagation.

[M0816](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0816)

[Mitigation Limited or Not Effective](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0816)

This type of attack technique cannot be easily mitigated with preventative controls since it is based on the abuse of system features.

[M0932](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0932)

[Multi-factor Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0932)

Use two or more pieces of evidence to authenticate to a system; such as username and password in addition to a token from a physical smart card or token generator. Within industrial control environments assets such as low-level controllers, workstations, and HMIs have real-time operational control and safety requirements which may restrict the use of multi-factor.

[M0807](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0807)

[Network Allowlists](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0807)

Network allowlists can be implemented through either host-based files or system hosts files to specify what connections (e.g., IP address, MAC address, port, protocol) can be made from a device. Allowlist techniques that operate at the application layer (e.g., DNP3, Modbus, HTTP) are addressed in[Filter Network Traffic](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0937)mitigation.

[M0931](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0931)

[Network Intrusion Prevention](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0931)

Use intrusion detection signatures to block traffic at network boundaries. In industrial control environments, network intrusion prevention should be configured so it will not disrupt protocols and communications responsible for real-time functions related to control or safety.

[M0930](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0930)

[Network Segmentation](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0930)

Architect sections of the network to isolate critical systems, functions, or resources. Use physical and logical segmentation to prevent access to potentially sensitive systems and information. Use a DMZ to contain any internet-facing services that should not be exposed from the internal network. Restrict network access to only required systems and services. In addition, prevent systems from other networks or business functions (e.g., enterprise) from accessing critical process control systems. For example, in IEC 62443, systems within the same secure level should be grouped into a zone, and access to that zone is restricted by a conduit, or mechanism to restrict data flows between zones by segmenting the network.

[M0928](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0928)

[Operating System Configuration](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0928)

Make configuration changes related to the operating system or a common feature of the operating system that result in system hardening against techniques.

[M0809](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0809)

[Operational Information Confidentiality](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0809)

Deploy mechanisms to protect the confidentiality of information related to operational processes, facility locations, device configurations, programs, or databases that may have information that can be used to infer organizational trade-secrets, recipes, and other intellectual property (IP).

[M0810](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0810)

[Out-of-Band Communications Channel](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0810)

Have alternative methods to support communication requirements during communication failures and data integrity attacks.

[M0927](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0927)

[Password Policies](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0927)

Set and enforce secure password policies for accounts.

[M0926](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0926)

[Privileged Account Management](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0926)

Manage the creation, modification, use, and permissions associated to privileged accounts, including SYSTEM and root.

[M0811](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0811)

[Redundancy of Service](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0811)

Redundancy could be provided for both critical ICS devices and services, such as back-up devices or hot-standbys.

[M0922](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0922)

[Restrict File and Directory Permissions](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0922)

Restrict access by setting directory and file permissions that are not specific to users or privileged accounts.

[M0944](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0944)

[Restrict Library Loading](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0944)

Prevent abuse of library loading mechanisms in the operating system and software to load untrusted code by configuring appropriate library loading mechanisms and investigating potential vulnerable software.

[M0924](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0924)

[Restrict Registry Permissions](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0924)

Restrict the ability to modify certain hives or keys in the Windows Registry.

[M0921](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0921)

[Restrict Web-Based Content](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0921)

Restrict use of certain websites, block downloads/attachments, block Javascript, restrict browser extensions, etc.

[M0812](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0812)

[Safety Instrumented Systems](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0812)

Utilize Safety Instrumented Systems (SIS) to provide an additional layer of protection to hazard scenarios that may cause property damage. A SIS will typically include sensors, logic solvers, and a final control element that can be used to automatically respond to an hazardous condition . Ensure that all SISs are segmented from operational networks to prevent them from being targeted by additional adversarial behavior.

[M0954](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0954)

[Software Configuration](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0954)

Implement configuration changes to software (other than the operating system) to mitigate security risks associated with how the software operates.

[M0813](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0813)

[Software Process and Device Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0813)

Require the authentication of devices and software processes where appropriate. Devices that connect remotely to other systems should require strong authentication to prevent spoofing of communications. Furthermore, software processes should also require authentication when accessing APIs.

[M0920](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0920)

[SSL/TLS Inspection](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0920)

Break and inspect SSL/TLS sessions to look at encrypted web traffic for adversary activity.

[M0814](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0814)

[Static Network Configuration](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0814)

Configure hosts and devices to use static network configurations when possible, protocols that require dynamic discovery/addressing (e.g., ARP, DHCP, DNS) can be used to manipulate network message forwarding and enable various AiTM attacks. This mitigation may not always be usable due to limited device features or challenges introduced with different network configurations.

[M0817](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0817)

[Supply Chain Management](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0817)

Implement a supply chain management program, including policies and procedures to ensure all devices and components originate from a trusted supplier and are tested to verify their integrity.

[M0919](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0919)

[Threat Intelligence Program](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0919)

A threat intelligence program helps an organization generate their own threat intelligence information and track trends to inform defensive priorities to mitigate risk.

[M0951](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0951)

[Update Software](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0951)

Perform regular software updates to mitigate exploitation risk. Software updates may need to be scheduled around operational down times.

[M0918](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0918)

[User Account Management](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0918)

Manage the creation, modification, use, and permissions associated to user accounts.

[M0917](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0917)

[User Training](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0917)

Train users to be aware of access or manipulation attempts by an adversary to reduce the risk of successful spearphishing, social engineering, and other techniques that involve user interaction.

[M0818](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0818)

[Validate Program Inputs](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0818)

Devices and programs designed to interact with control system parameters should validate the format and content of all user inputs and actions to ensure the values are within intended operational ranges. These values should be evaluated and further enforced through the program logic running on the field controller. If a problematic or invalid input is identified, the programs should either utilize a predetermined safe value or enter a known safe state, while also logging or alerting on the event.

[M0916](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0916)

[Vulnerability Scanning](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0916)

Vulnerability scanning is used to find potentially exploitable software vulnerabilities to remediate them.

[M0815](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0815)

[Watchdog Timers](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0815)

Utilize watchdog timers to ensure devices can quickly detect whether a system is unresponsive.

Access Management
=================

Access Management technologies can be used to enforce authorization polices and decisions, especially when existing field devices do not provided sufficient capabilities to support user identification and authentication.[\[1\]](https://doi.org/10.6028/NIST.SP.1800-2)These technologies typically utilize an in-line network device or gateway system to prevent access to unauthenticated users, while also integrating with an authentication service to first verify user credentials.[\[2\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/sites/default/files/recommended_practices/RP_Managing_Remote_Access_S508NC.pdf)

ID:M0801

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 2.1, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 2.1, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - AC-3

Version:1.0

Created:11 September 2020

Last Modified:19 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0801/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

ICS

[T0800](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0800)

[Activate Firmware Update Mode](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0800)

All devices or systems changes, including all administrative functions, should require authentication. Consider using access management technologies to enforce authorization on all management interface access attempts, especially when the device does not inherently provide strong authentication and authorization functions.

ICS

[T0858](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0858)

[Change Operating Mode](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0858)

Authenticate all access to field controllers before authorizing access to, or modification of, a device's state, logic, or programs. Centralized authentication techniques can help manage the large number of field controller accounts needed across the ICS.

ICS

[T0812](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0812)

[Default Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0812)

Ensure embedded controls and network devices are protected through access management, as these devices often have unknown default accounts which could be used to gain unauthorized access.

ICS

[T0868](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0868)

[Detect Operating Mode](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0868)

Authenticate all access to field controllers before authorizing access to, or modification of, a device's state, logic, or programs. Centralized authentication techniques can help manage the large number of field controller accounts needed across the ICS.

ICS

[T0816](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0816)

[Device Restart/Shutdown](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0816)

All devices or systems changes, including all administrative functions, should require authentication. Consider using access management technologies to enforce authorization on all management interface access attempts, especially when the device does not inherently provide strong authentication and authorization functions.

ICS

[T0871](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0871)

[Execution through API](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0871)

Access Management technologies can be used to enforce authorization policies and decisions, especially when existing field devices do not provide capabilities to support user identification and authentication.[\[1\]](https://doi.org/10.6028/NIST.SP.1800-2)These technologies typically utilize an in-line network device or gateway system to prevent access to unauthenticated users, while also integrating with an authentication service to first verify user credentials.

ICS

[T0891](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0891)

[Hardcoded Credentials](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0891)

Ensure embedded controls and network devices are protected through access management, as these devices often have unknown hardcoded accounts which could be used to gain unauthorized access.

ICS

[T0838](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0838)

[Modify Alarm Settings](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0838)

All devices or systems changes, including all administrative functions, should require authentication. Consider using access management technologies to enforce authorization on all management interface access attempts, especially when the device does not inherently provide strong authentication and authorization functions.

ICS

[T0839](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

[Module Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

All devices or systems changes, including all administrative functions, should require authentication. Consider using access management technologies to enforce authorization on all management interface access attempts, especially when the device does not inherently provide strong authentication and authorization functions.

ICS

[T0861](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0861)

[Point & Tag Identification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0861)

Authenticate all access to field controllers before authorizing access to, or modification of, a device's state, logic, or programs. Centralized authentication techniques can help manage the large number of field controller accounts needed across the ICS.

ICS

[T0843](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0843)

[Program Download](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0843)

Authenticate all access to field controllers before authorizing access to, or modification of, a device's state, logic, or programs. Centralized authentication techniques can help manage the large number of field controller accounts needed across the ICS.

ICS

[T0845](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0845)

[Program Upload](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0845)

Authenticate all access to field controllers before authorizing access to, or modification of, a device's state, logic, or programs. Centralized authentication techniques can help manage the large number of field controller accounts needed across the ICS.

ICS

[T0886](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0886)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0886)

Access Management technologies can help enforce authentication on critical remote service, examples include, but are not limited to, device management services (e.g., telnet, SSH), data access servers (e.g., HTTP, Historians), and HMI sessions (e.g., RDP, VNC).

ICS

[T0857](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0857)

[System Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0857)

All devices or systems changes, including all administrative functions, should require authentication. Consider using access management technologies to enforce authorization on all management interface access attempts, especially when the device does not inherently provide strong authentication and authorization functions.

ICS

[T0859](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0859)

[Valid Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0859)

Authenticate all access to field controllers before authorizing access to, or modification of, a device's state, logic, or programs. Centralized authentication techniques can help manage the large number of field controller accounts needed across the ICS.

Antivirus/Antimalware
=====================

Use signatures or heuristics to detect malicious software. Within industrial control environments, antivirus/antimalware installations should be limited to assets that are not involved in critical or real-time operations. To minimize the impact to system availability, all products should first be validated within a representative test environment before deployment to production systems.[\[1\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/sites/default/files/recommended_practices/Recommended%20Practice%20Updating%20Antivirus%20in%20an%20Industrial%20Control%20System_S508C.pdf)

ID:M0949

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 3.2, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 3.2, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 4 - SI-3, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - SI-3

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:19 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0949/)

[T0864](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0864)

[Transient Cyber Asset](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0864)

Application Isolation and Sandboxing
====================================

Restrict the execution of code to a virtual environment on or in-transit to an endpoint system.

ID:M0948

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 5.4, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 5.4, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - SI-3

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:19 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0948/)

**ATT&CK****Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

ICS

[T0817](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0817)

[Drive-by Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0817)

Built-in browser sandboxes and application isolation may be used to contain web-based malware.

ICS

[T0819](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0819)

[Exploit Public-Facing Application](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0819)

Application isolation will limit the other processes and system features an exploited target can access. Examples of built in features are software restriction policies, AppLocker for Windows, and SELinux or AppArmor for Linux.

ICS

[T0820](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0820)

[Exploitation for Evasion](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0820)

Make it difficult for adversaries to advance their operation through exploitation of undiscovered or unpatched vulnerabilities by using sandboxing. Other types of virtualization and application microsegmentation may also mitigate the impact of some types of exploitation. Risks of additional exploits and weaknesses in these systems may still exist.[\[1\]](https://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2017/03/hack-that-escapes-vm-by-exploiting-edge-browser-fetches-105000-at-pwn2own/)

ICS

[T0890](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0890)

[Exploitation for Privilege Escalation](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0890)

Make it difficult for adversaries to advance their operation through exploitation of undiscovered or unpatched vulnerabilities by using sandboxing. Other types of virtualization and application microsegmentation may also mitigate the impact of some types of exploitation. Risks of additional exploits and weaknesses in these systems may still exist.[\[1\]](https://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2017/03/hack-that-escapes-vm-by-exploiting-edge-browser-fetches-105000-at-pwn2own/)

ICS

[T0866](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0866)

[Exploitation of Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0866)

Make it difficult for adversaries to advance their operation through exploitation of undiscovered or unpatched vulnerabilities by using sandboxing. Other types of virtualization and application microsegmentation may also mitigate the impact of some types of exploitation. Risks of additional exploits and weaknesses in these systems may still exist.[\[1\]](https://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2017/03/hack-that-escapes-vm-by-exploiting-edge-browser-fetches-105000-at-pwn2own/)

ICS

[T0853](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0853)

[Scripting](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0853)

Consider the use of application isolation and sandboxing to restrict specific operating system interactions such as access through user accounts, services, system calls, registry, and network access. This may be even more useful in cases where the source of the executed script is unknown.

Audit
=====

Perform audits or scans of systems, permissions, insecure software, insecure configurations, etc. to identify potential weaknesses. Perform periodic integrity checks of the device to validate the correctness of the firmware, software, programs, and configurations. Integrity checks, which typically include cryptographic hashes or digital signatures, should be compared to those obtained at known valid states, especially after events like device reboots, program downloads, or program restarts.

ID:M0947

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 3.4, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 3.4, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 4 - SI-7, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - SI-7

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:19 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0947/)

--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

ICS

[T0830](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0830)

[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0830)

Limit access to network infrastructure and resources that can be used to reshape traffic or otherwise produce AiTM conditions.

ICS

[T0811](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0811)

[Data from Information Repositories](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0811)

Consider periodic reviews of accounts and privileges for critical and sensitive repositories.

ICS

[T0874](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0874)

[Hooking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0874)

Perform audits or scans of systems, permissions, insecure software, insecure configurations, etc. to identify potential weaknesses. Perform periodic integrity checks of the device to validate the correctness of the firmware, software, programs, and configurations. Integrity checks, which typically include cryptographic hashes or digital signatures, should be compared to those obtained at known valid states, especially after events like device reboots, program downloads, or program restarts.

ICS

[T0821](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0821)

[Modify Controller Tasking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0821)

Provide the ability to verify the integrity of controller tasking. While techniques like CRCs and checksums are commonly used, they are not cryptographically secure and can be vulnerable to collisions. Preferably cryptographic hash functions (e.g., SHA-2, SHA-3) should be used.[\[1\]](https://webstore.iec.ch/publication/34421)

ICS

[T0836](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0836)

[Modify Parameter](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0836)

Provide the ability to verify the integrity and authenticity of changes to parameter values.

ICS

[T0889](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0889)

[Modify Program](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0889)

Provide the ability to verify the integrity of control logic or programs loaded on a controller. While techniques like CRCs and checksums are commonly used, they are not cryptographically strong and can be vulnerable to collisions. Preferably cryptographic hash functions (e.g., SHA-2, SHA-3) should be used.[\[1\]](https://webstore.iec.ch/publication/34421)

ICS

[T0839](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

[Module Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

Perform integrity checks of firmware before uploading it on a device. Utilize cryptographic hashes to verify the firmware has not been tampered with by comparing it to a trusted hash of the firmware. This could be from trusted data sources (e.g., vendor site) or through a third-party verification service.

ICS

[T0843](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0843)

[Program Download](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0843)

Provide the ability to verify the integrity of programs downloaded on a controller. While techniques like CRCs and checksums are commonly used, they are not cryptographically secure and can be vulnerable to collisions. Preferably cryptographic hash functions (e.g., SHA-2, SHA-3) should be used.[\[1\]](https://webstore.iec.ch/publication/34421)

ICS

[T0873](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0873)

[Project File Infection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0873)

Review the integrity of project files to verify they have not been modified by adversary behavior. Verify a cryptographic hash for the file with a known trusted version, or look for other indicators of modification (e.g., timestamps).

ICS

[T0851](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0851)

[Rootkit](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0851)

Audit the integrity of PLC system and application code functionality, such as the manipulation of standard function blocks (e.g., Organizational Blocks) that manage the execution of application logic programs.[\[1\]](https://webstore.iec.ch/publication/34421)

ICS

[T0862](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0862)

[Supply Chain Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0862)

Perform audits or scans of systems, permissions, insecure software, insecure configurations, etc. to identify potential weaknesses. Perform periodic integrity checks of the device to validate the correctness of the firmware, software, programs, and configurations. Integrity checks, which typically include cryptographic hashes or digital signatures, should be compared to those obtained at known valid states, especially after events like device reboots, program downloads, or program restarts.

ICS

[T0857](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0857)

[System Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0857)

Perform integrity checks of firmware before uploading it on a device. Utilize cryptographic hashes to verify the firmware has not been tampered with by comparing it to a trusted hash of the firmware. This could be from trusted data sources (e.g., vendor site) or through a third-party verification service.

ICS

[T0864](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0864)

[Transient Cyber Asset](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0864)

Integrity checking of transient assets can include performing the validation of the booted operating system and programs using TPM-based technologies, such as Secure Boot and Trusted Boot.[\[2\]](https://emersonexchange365.com/products/control-safety-systems/f/plc-pac-systems-industrial-computing-forum/8383/increase-security-with-tpm-secure-boot-and-trusted-boot)It can also include verifying filesystem changes, such as programs and configuration files stored on the system, executing processes, libraries, accounts, and open ports.[\[3\]](https://apps.nsa.gov/iaarchive/library/ia-guidance/security-configuration/industrial-control-systems/position-zero-integrity-checking-windows-based-ics-scada-systems.cfm)

ICS

[T0859](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0859)

[Valid Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0859)

Routinely audit source code, application configuration files, open repositories, and public cloud storage for insecure use and storage of credentials.

1.  [IEC 2019, February Security for industrial automation and control systems - Part 4-2: Technical security requirements for IACS components Retrieved. 2020/09/25](https://webstore.iec.ch/publication/34421)

Authorization Enforcement
=========================

The device or system should restrict read, manipulate, or execute privileges to only authenticated users who require access based on approved security policies. Role-based Access Control (RBAC) schemes can help reduce the overhead of assigning permissions to the large number of devices within an ICS. For example, IEC 62351 provides examples of roles used to support common system operations within the electric power sector[\[1\]](https://webstore.iec.ch/publication/6912), while IEEE 1686 defines standard permissions for users of IEDs.[\[2\]](https://standards.ieee.org/standard/1686-2013.html)

ID:M0800

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 2.1, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 2.1, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - AC-3

Version:1.1

Created:11 September 2020

Last Modified:20 October 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0800/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

ICS

[T0800](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0800)

[Activate Firmware Update Mode](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0800)

Restrict configurations changes and firmware updating abilities to only authorized individuals.

ICS

[T0858](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0858)

[Change Operating Mode](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0858)

All field controllers should restrict operating mode changes to only required authenticated users (e.g., engineers, field technicians), preferably through implementing a role-based access mechanism. Further, physical mechanisms (e.g., keys) can also be used to limit unauthorized operating mode changes.

ICS

[T0868](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0868)

[Detect Operating Mode](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0868)

All field controllers should restrict the modification of programs to only certain users (e.g., engineers, field technician), preferably through implementing a role-based access mechanism.

ICS

[T0816](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0816)

[Device Restart/Shutdown](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0816)

All field controllers should restrict the modification of programs to only certain users (e.g., engineers, field technician), preferably through implementing a role-based access mechanism.

ICS

[T0871](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0871)

[Execution through API](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0871)

All APIs used to perform execution, especially those hosted on embedded controllers (e.g., PLCs), should provide adequate authorization enforcement of user access. Minimize user's access to only required API calls.[\[3\]](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/227.html)

ICS

[T0838](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0838)

[Modify Alarm Settings](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0838)

Only authorized personnel should be able to change settings for alarms.

ICS

[T0821](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0821)

[Modify Controller Tasking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0821)

All field controllers should restrict the modification of controller tasks to only certain users (e.g., engineers, field technician), preferably through implementing a role-based access mechanism.

ICS

[T0836](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0836)

[Modify Parameter](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0836)

All field controllers should restrict the modification of parameter values to only certain users (e.g., engineers, field technician), preferably through implementing a role-based access mechanism. They should also restrict online edits and enable write protection for parameters.

ICS

[T0889](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0889)

[Modify Program](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0889)

All field controllers should restrict the modification of programs to only certain users (e.g., engineers, field technician), preferably through implementing a role-based access mechanism.

ICS

[T0861](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0861)

[Point & Tag Identification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0861)

Systems and devices should restrict access to any data with potential confidentiality concerns, including point and tag information.

ICS

[T0843](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0843)

[Program Download](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0843)

All field controllers should restrict the download of programs, including online edits and program appends, to only certain users (e.g., engineers, field technician), preferably through implementing a role-based access mechanism.

ICS

[T0845](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0845)

[Program Upload](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0845)

All field controllers should restrict program uploads to only certain users (e.g., engineers, field technician), preferably through implementing a role-based access mechanism.

ICS

[T0886](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0886)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0886)

Provide privileges corresponding to the restriction of a GUI session to control system operations (examples include HMI read-only vs. read-write modes). Ensure local users, such as operators and engineers, are giving prioritization over remote sessions and have the authority to regain control over a remote session if needed. Prevent remote access sessions (e.g., RDP, VNC) from taking over local sessions, especially those used for ICS control, especially HMIs.

**References**
--------------

1.  [International Electrotechnical Commission 2020, July 17 IEC 62351 - Power systems management and associated information exchange - Data and communications security Retrieved. 2020/09/17](https://webstore.iec.ch/publication/6912)
2.  [Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers 2014, January 1686-2013 - IEEE Standard for Intelligent Electronic Devices Cyber Security Capabilities Retrieved. 2020/09/17](https://standards.ieee.org/standard/1686-2013.html)

Boot Integrity
==============

Use secure methods to boot a system and verify the integrity of the operating system and loading mechanisms.

ID:M0946

Security Controls:IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 3.14, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - SI-7

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

**ID**

**Name**

ICS

[T0839](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

[Module Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

Check the integrity of the existing BIOS or EFI to determine if it is vulnerable to modification. Use Trusted Platform Module technology.[\[1\]](https://www.trustedcomputinggroup.org/wp-content/uploads/Trusted-Platform-Module-Summary_04292008.pdf)Move system's root of trust to hardware to prevent tampering with the SPI flash memory.[\[2\]](https://www.welivesecurity.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/ESET-LoJax.pdf)Technologies such as Intel Boot Guard can assist with this.[\[3\]](https://www.intel.com/content/dam/www/public/us/en/documents/white-papers/security-technologies-4th-gen-core-retail-paper.pdf)

ICS

[T0857](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0857)

[System Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0857)

Check the integrity of the existing BIOS or EFI to determine if it is vulnerable to modification. Use Trusted Platform Module technology.[\[1\]](https://www.trustedcomputinggroup.org/wp-content/uploads/Trusted-Platform-Module-Summary_04292008.pdf)Move system's root of trust to hardware to prevent tampering with the SPI flash memory.[\[2\]](https://www.welivesecurity.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/ESET-LoJax.pdf)Technologies such as Intel Boot Guard can assist with this.[\[3\]](https://www.intel.com/content/dam/www/public/us/en/documents/white-papers/security-technologies-4th-gen-core-retail-paper.pdf)

Code Signing
============

Enforce binary and application integrity with digital signature verification to prevent untrusted code from executing.

ID:M0945

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 3.4, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 3.4, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - SI-7

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:19 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0945/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

ICS

[T0849](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0849)

[Masquerading](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0849)

Require signed binaries.

ICS

[T0821](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0821)

[Modify Controller Tasking](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0821)

Utilize code signatures to verify the integrity and authenticity of programs installed on safety or control assets, including the associated controller tasking.

ICS

[T0889](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0889)

[Modify Program](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0889)

Utilize code signatures to verify the integrity and authenticity of programs installed on safety or control assets.

ICS

[T0839](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

[Module Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

Devices should verify that firmware has been properly signed by the vendor before allowing installation.

ICS

[T0843](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0843)

[Program Download](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0843)

Utilize code signatures to verify the integrity and authenticity of programs downloaded to the device.

ICS

[T0873](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0873)

[Project File Infection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0873)

Allow for code signing of any project files stored at rest to prevent unauthorized tampering. Ensure the signing keys are not easily accessible on the same system.

ICS

[T0851](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0851)

[Rootkit](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0851)

Digital signatures may be used to ensure application DLLs are authentic prior to execution.

ICS

[T0862](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0862)

[Supply Chain Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0862)

When available utilize hardware and software root-of-trust to verify the authenticity of a system. This may be achieved through cryptographic means, such as digital signatures or hashes, of critical software and firmware throughout the supply chain.

ICS

[T0857](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0857)

[System Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0857)

Devices should verify that firmware has been properly signed by the vendor before allowing installation.

ICS

[T0863](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0863)

[User Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0863)

Prevent the use of unsigned executables, such as installers and scripts.

Communication Authenticity
==========================

When communicating over an untrusted network, utilize secure network protocols that both authenticate the message sender and can verify its integrity. This can be done either through message authentication codes (MACs) or digital signatures, to detect spoofed network messages and unauthorized connections.

ID:M0802

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 3.1, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 3.1, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - SC-8; SC-23

Version:1.0

Created:11 September 2020

Last Modified:19 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0802/)

**ATT&CK****Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

ICS

[T0800](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0800)

[Activate Firmware Update Mode](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0800)

Protocols used for device management should authenticate all network messages to prevent unauthorized system changes.

ICS

[T0830](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0830)

[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0830)

Communication authenticity will ensure that any messages tampered with through AiTM can be detected, but cannot prevent eavesdropping on these. In addition, providing communication authenticity around various discovery protocols, such as DNS, can be used to prevent various AiTM procedures.

ICS

[T0858](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0858)

[Change Operating Mode](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0858)

Protocols used for device management should authenticate all network messages to prevent unauthorized system changes.

ICS

[T0868](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0868)

[Detect Operating Mode](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0868)

Protocols used for control functions should provide authenticity through MAC functions or digital signatures. If not, utilize bump-in-the-wire devices or VPNs to enforce communication authenticity between devices that are not capable of supporting this (e.g., legacy controllers, RTUs).

ICS

[Spoof Reporting Message](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0856)

[T0855](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0855)

[Unauthorized Command Message](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0855)

Protocols used for control functions should provide authenticity through MAC functions or digital signatures. If not, utilize bump-in-the-wire devices or VPNs to enforce communication authenticity between devices that are not capable of supporting this (e.g., legacy controllers, RTUs).

ICS

[T0860](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0860)

[Wireless Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0860)

Do not inherently rely on the authenticity provided by the network/link layer (e.g., 802.11, LTE, 802.15.4), as link layer equipment may have long lifespans and protocol vulnerabilities may not be easily patched. Provide defense-in-depth by implementing authenticity within the associated application-layer protocol, or through a network-layer VPN.[\[1\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/tips/ST05-003)Furthermore, ensure communication schemes provide strong replay protection, employing techniques such as timestamps or cryptographic nonces.

**References**
--------------

1.  [CISA 2010, March 11 https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/tips/ST05-003 Retrieved. 2020/09/25](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/tips/ST05-003)

Data Backup
===========

Take and store data backups from end user systems and critical servers. Ensure backup and storage systems are hardened and kept separate from the corporate network to prevent compromise. Maintain and exercise incident response plans[\[1\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/sites/default/files/recommended_practices/final-RP_ics_cybersecurity_incident_response_100609.pdf), including the management of 'gold-copy' back-up images and configurations for key systems to enable quick recovery and response from adversarial activities that impact control, view, or availability.

ID:M0953

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 7.3, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 7.3, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - CP-9

Version:1.0

Created:19 July 2019

Last Modified:19 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0953/)

Data Loss Prevention
====================

Data Loss Prevention (DLP) technologies can be used to help identify adversarial attempts to exfiltrate operational information, such as engineering plans, trade secrets, recipes, intellectual property, or process telemetry. DLP functionality may be built into other security products such as firewalls or standalone suites running on the network and host-based agents. DLP may be configured to prevent the transfer of information through corporate resources such as email, web, and physical media such as USB for host-based solutions.

ID:M0803

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 4.1, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 4.1

Version:1.0

Created:11 September 2020

Last Modified:30 March 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0803/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

ICS

[T0893](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0893)

[Data from Local System](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0893)

Data loss prevention can restrict access to sensitive data and detect sensitive data that is unencrypted.

ICS

[T0882](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0882)

[Theft of Operational Information](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0882)

Apply DLP to protect the confidentiality of information related to operational processes, facility locations, device configurations, programs, or databases that may have information that can be used to infer organizational trade-secrets, recipes, and other intellectual property (IP).

Disable or Remove Feature or Program
====================================

Remove or deny access to unnecessary and potentially vulnerable software to prevent abuse by adversaries.

ID:M0942

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 7.7, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 7.7, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - CM-7

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:19 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0942/)

**ATT&CK****Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

ICS

[T0830](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0830)

[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0830)

Disable unnecessary legacy network protocols that may be used for AiTM if applicable.

ICS

[T0807](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0807)

[Command-Line Interface](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0807)

Consider removing or restricting features that are unnecessary to an asset's intended function within the control environment.

ICS

[T0885](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0885)

[Commonly Used Port](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0885)

Ensure that unnecessary ports and services are closed to prevent risk of discovery and potential exploitation.

ICS

[T0816](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0816)

[Device Restart/Shutdown](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0816)

Ensure remote commands that enable device shutdown are disabled if they are not necessary. Examples include DNP3's 0x0D function code or unnecessary device management functions.

ICS

[T0866](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0866)

[Exploitation of Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0866)

Ensure that unnecessary ports and services are closed to prevent risk of discovery and potential exploitation.

ICS

[T0822](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0822)

[External Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0822)

Consider removal of remote services which are not regularly in use, or only enabling them when required (e.g., vendor remote access). Ensure all external remote access point (e.g., jump boxes, VPN concentrator) are configured with least functionality, especially the removal of unnecessary services.[\[1\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/sites/default/files/recommended_practices/NCCIC_ICS-CERT_Defense_in_Depth_2016_S508C.pdf)

ICS

[T0847](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0847)

[Replication Through Removable Media](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0847)

Consider the disabling of features such as AutoRun.

ICS

[T0853](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0853)

[Scripting](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0853)

Consider removal or disabling of programs and features which may be used to run malicious scripts (e.g., scripting language IDEs, PowerShell, visual studio).

Encrypt Network Traffic
=======================

Utilize strong cryptographic techniques and protocols to prevent eavesdropping on network communications.

ID:M0808

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 4.1, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 4.1, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - SC-8

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

ICS

[T0839](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

[Module Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

The encryption of firmware should be considered to prevent adversaries from identifying possible vulnerabilities within the firmware.

ICS

[T0842](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0842)

[Network Sniffing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0842)

Ensure that wired and/or wireless traffic is encrypted when feasible. Use best practices for authentication protocols, such as Kerberos, and ensure web traffic that may contain credentials is protected by SSL/TLS.[\[1\]](https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.800-82r2.pdf)

[T0857](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0857)

Encrypt Sensitive Information
=============================

Protect sensitive data-at-rest with strong encryption.

ID:M0941

[T0811](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0811)

[Data from Information Repositories](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0811)

Information which is sensitive to the operation and architecture of the process environment may be encrypted to ensure confidentiality and restrict access to only those who need to know.[\[1\]](https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.800-82r2.pdf)[\[2\]](https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.800-53r4.pdf)

ICS

[T0893](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0893)

[Data from Local System](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0893)

Information which is sensitive to the operation and architecture of the process environment may be encrypted to ensure confidentiality and restrict access to only those who need to know.[\[1\]](https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.800-82r2.pdf)[\[2\]](https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.800-53r4.pdf)

ICS

[T0839](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

[Module Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

The encryption of firmware should be considered to prevent adversaries from identifying possible vulnerabilities within the firmware.

ICS

[T0873](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0873)

[Project File Infection](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0873)

When at rest, project files should be encrypted to prevent unauthorized changes.[\[2\]](https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.800-53r4.pdf)

ICS

[T0857](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0857)

[System Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0857)

The encryption of firmware should be considered to prevent adversaries from identifying possible vulnerabilities within the firmware.

ICS

[T0882](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0882)

[Theft of Operational Information](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0882)

Encrypt any operational data with strong confidentiality requirements, including organizational trade-secrets, recipes, and other intellectual property (IP).

ICS

[T0864](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0864)

[Transient Cyber Asset](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0864)

Consider implementing full disk encryption, especially if engineering workstations are transient assets that are more likely to be lost, stolen, or tampered with.[\[2\]](https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.800-53r4.pdf)

====================

==================

ICS

[T0820](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0820)

[Exploitation for Evasion](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0820)

Security applications that look for behavior used during exploitation such as Windows Defender Exploit Guard (WDEG) and the Enhanced Mitigation Experience Toolkit (EMET) can be used to mitigate some exploitation behavior.[\[2\]](https://msrc-blog.microsoft.com/2017/08/09/moving-beyond-emet-ii-windows-defender-exploit-guard/)Control flow integrity checking is another way to potentially identify and stop a software exploit from occurring.[\[3\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control-flow_integrity)Many of these protections depend on the architecture and target application binary for compatibility and may not work for all software or services targeted.

Filter Network Traffic
======================

Use network appliances to filter ingress or egress traffic and perform protocol-based filtering. Configure software on endpoints to filter network traffic. Perform inline allow/denylisting of network messages based on the application layer (OSI Layer 7) protocol, especially for automation protocols. Application allowlists are beneficial when there are well-defined communication sequences, types, rates, or patterns needed during expected system operations. Application denylists may be needed if all acceptable communication sequences cannot be defined, but instead a set of known malicious uses can be denied (e.g., excessive communication attempts, shutdown messages, invalid commands). Devices performing these functions are often referred to as deep-packet inspection (DPI) firewalls, context-aware firewalls, or firewalls blocking specific automation/SCADA protocol aware firewalls.[\[1\]](https://www.energy.gov/sites/prod/files/Good%20Practices%20Guide%20for%20Firewall%20Deployment.pdf)

ID:M0937

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 5.1, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 5.1, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - AC-3; SC-7

Version:1.0

Created:11 June 2019

Last Modified:19 September 2023

Human User Authentication
=========================

Require user authentication before allowing access to data or accepting commands to a device. While strong multi-factor authentication is preferable, it is not always feasible within ICS environments. Performing strong user authentication also requires additional security controls and processes which are often the target of related adversarial techniques (e.g., Valid Accounts, Default Credentials). Therefore, associated ATT&CK mitigations should be considered in addition to this, including[Multi-factor Authentication](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0932),[Account Use Policies](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0936),[Password Policies](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0927),[User Account Management](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0918),[Privileged Account Management](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0926), and[User Account Control](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M1052).

ID:M0804

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 1.1, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 1.1, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - IA-2

Version:1.1

Created:11 September 2020

Last Modified:20 October 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0804/)

Mechanical Protection Layers
============================

Utilize a layered protection design based on physical or mechanical protection systems to prevent damage to property, equipment, human safety, or the environment. Examples include interlocks, rupture disk, release values, etc.[\[1\]](https://www.icheme.org/media/9906/xviii-paper-23.pdf)

ID:M0805

Version:1.0

Created:11 September 2020

Last Modified:24 October 2022

**Name**

[Damage to Property](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0879)

Protection devices should have minimal digital components to prevent exposure to related adversarial techniques. Examples include interlocks, rupture disks, release valves, etc.[\[1\]](https://www.icheme.org/media/9906/xviii-paper-23.pdf)

Minimize Wireless Signal Propagation
====================================

Wireless signals frequently propagate outside of organizational boundaries, which provide opportunities for adversaries to monitor or gain unauthorized access to the wireless network.[\[1\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/tips/ST05-003)To minimize this threat, organizations should implement measures to detect, understand, and reduce unnecessary RF propagation.[\[2\]](https://www.dhs.gov/sites/default/files/saver-msr-rf-detection_cod-508_10july2019.pdf)

ID:M0806

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 1.6, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 1.6, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - SC-40

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

ICS

[T0860](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0860)

[Wireless Compromise](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0860)

Techniques can include (i) reducing transmission power on wireless signals, (ii) adjusting antenna gain to prevent extensions beyond organizational boundaries, and (iii) employing RF shielding techniques to block excessive signal propagation.[\[2\]](https://www.dhs.gov/sites/default/files/saver-msr-rf-detection_cod-508_10july2019.pdf)

ICS

[T0887](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0887)

[Wireless Sniffing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0887)

Reduce the range of RF communications to their intended operating range when possible. Propagation reduction methods may include (i) reducing transmission power on wireless signals, (ii) adjusting antenna gain to prevent extensions beyond organizational boundaries, and (iii) employing RF shielding techniques to block excessive signal propagation.[\[2\]](https://www.dhs.gov/sites/default/files/saver-msr-rf-detection_cod-508_10july2019.pdf)

**References**
--------------

1.  [CISA 2010, March Securing Wireless Networks Retrieved. 2020/09/17](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/tips/ST05-003)

2.  [DHS National Urban Security Technology Laboratory 2019, April Radio Frequency Detection, Spectrum Analysis, and Direction Finding Equipment Retrieved. 2020/09/17](https://www.dhs.gov/sites/default/files/saver-msr-rf-detection_cod-508_10july2019.pdf)

Mitigation Limited or Not Effective
===================================

This type of attack technique cannot be easily mitigated with preventative controls since it is based on the abuse of system features.

ID:M0816

Version:1.0

Created:11 September 2020

Last Modified:24 October 2022

Multi-factor Authentication
===========================

Use two or more pieces of evidence to authenticate to a system; such as username and password in addition to a token from a physical smart card or token generator. Within industrial control environments assets such as low-level controllers, workstations, and HMIs have real-time operational control and safety requirements which may restrict the use of multi-factor.

ID:M0932

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 1.7, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 1.7, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - IA-2

Version:1.0

Created:10 June 2019

Last Modified:19 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0932/)

**ATT&CK********Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

ICS

[T0822](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0822)

[External Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0822)

Use strong multi-factor authentication for remote service accounts to mitigate an adversary's ability to leverage stolen credentials. Be aware of multi-factor authentication interception techniques for some implementations.

ICS

[T0842](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0842)

[Network Sniffing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0842)

Use multi-factor authentication wherever possible.

ICS

[T0859](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0859)

[Valid Accounts](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0859)

Integrating multi-factor authentication (MFA) as part of organizational policy can greatly reduce the risk of an adversary gaining access to valid credentials that may be used for additional tactics such as initial access, lateral movement, and collecting information. MFA can also be used to restrict access to cloud resources and APIs.

Network Allowlists
==================

Network allowlists can be implemented through either host-based files or system hosts files to specify what connections (e.g., IP address, MAC address, port, protocol) can be made from a device. Allowlist techniques that operate at the application layer (e.g., DNP3, Modbus, HTTP) are addressed in[Filter Network Traffic](https://attack.mitre.org/mitigations/M0937)mitigation.

ID:M0807

Security Controls:NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - AC-3

Version:1.0

Created:10 June 2019

Last Modified:19 September 2023

Network Intrusion Prevention
============================

Use intrusion detection signatures to block traffic at network boundaries. In industrial control environments, network intrusion prevention should be configured so it will not disrupt protocols and communications responsible for real-time functions related to control or safety.

ID:M0931

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 6.2, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 6.2, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - SI-4

Version:1.0

Created:10 June 2019

Last Modified:19 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0931/)

**ATT&CK****Navigator Layers**

**Techniques Addressed by Mitigation**
--------------------------------------

**Domain**

**ID**

**Name**

**Use**

ICS

[T0830](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0830)

[Adversary-in-the-Middle](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0830)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that can identify traffic patterns indicative of AiTM activity can be used to mitigate activity at the network level.

ICS

[T0885](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0885)

[Commonly Used Port](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0885)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that use network signatures to identify traffic for specific adversary malware can be used to mitigate activity at the network level. Signatures are often for unique indicators within protocols and may be based on the specific protocol used by a particular adversary or tool and will likely be different across various malware families and versions. Adversaries will likely change tool C2 signatures over time or construct protocols in such a way as to avoid detection by common defensive tools.[\[1\]](https://arxiv.org/ftp/arxiv/papers/1408/1408.1136.pdf)

ICS

[T0884](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0884)

[Connection Proxy](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0884)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that use network signatures to identify traffic for specific adversary malware can be used to mitigate activity at the network level. Signatures are often for unique indicators within protocols and may be based on the specific C2 protocol used by a particular adversary or tool and will likely be different across various malware families and versions. Adversaries will likely change tool C2 signatures over time or construct protocols in such a way as to avoid detection by common defensive tools.[\[1\]](https://arxiv.org/ftp/arxiv/papers/1408/1408.1136.pdf)

ICS

[T0867](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0867)

[Lateral Tool Transfer](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0867)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that use network signatures to identify traffic for specific adversary malware or unusual data transfer over known tools and protocols like FTP can be used to mitigate activity at the network level. Signatures are often for unique indicators within protocols and may be based on the specific obfuscation technique used by a particular adversary or tool and will likely be different across various malware families and versions. Adversaries will likely change tool C2 signatures over time or construct protocols in such a way as to avoid detection by common defensive tools.[\[1\]](https://arxiv.org/ftp/arxiv/papers/1408/1408.1136.pdf)

ICS

[T0865](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0865)

[Spearphishing Attachment](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0865)

Network intrusion prevention systems and systems designed to scan and remove malicious email attachments can be used to block activity.

ICS

[T0869](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0869)

[Standard Application Layer Protocol](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0869)

Network intrusion detection and prevention systems that use network signatures to identify traffic for specific adversary malware can be used to mitigate activity at the network level.

ICS

[T0863](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0863)

[User Execution](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0863)

If a link is being visited by a user, network intrusion prevention systems and systems designed to scan and remove malicious downloads can be used to block activity.

1.  [Gardiner, J., Cova, M., Nagaraja, S 2014, February Command & Control Understanding, Denying and Detecting Retrieved. 2016/04/20](https://arxiv.org/ftp/arxiv/papers/1408/1408.1136.pdf)

Network Segmentation
====================

Architect sections of the network to isolate critical systems, functions, or resources. Use physical and logical segmentation to prevent access to potentially sensitive systems and information. Use a DMZ to contain any internet-facing services that should not be exposed from the internal network. Restrict network access to only required systems and services. In addition, prevent systems from other networks or business functions (e.g., enterprise) from accessing critical process control systems. For example, in IEC 62443, systems within the same secure level should be grouped into a zone, and access to that zone is restricted by a conduit, or mechanism to restrict data flows between zones by segmenting the network.[\[1\]](https://webstore.iec.ch/publication/34421)[\[2\]](https://webstore.iec.ch/publication/7033)

ID:M0930

Security Controls:IEC 62443-3-3:2013 - SR 5.1, IEC 62443-4-2:2019 - CR 5.1, NIST SP 800-53 Rev. 5 - AC-3

Version:1.0

Created:10 June 2019

Last Modified:19 September 2023

[Version Permalink](https://attack.mitre.org/versions/v15/mitigations/M0930/)

Leverage this DMZ or corporate resources for vendor access.[\[5\]](https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.800-82r2.pdf)

[T0838](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0838)

[Modify Alarm Settings](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0838)

Segment operational network and systems to restrict access to critical system functions to predetermined management systems.[\[3\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/sites/default/files/recommended_practices/NCCIC_ICS-CERT_Defense_in_Depth_2016_S508C.pdf)[\[7\]](https://www.exida.com/images/uploads/18492275-Alarm-Management-for-Process-Control.pdf)

ICS

[T0839](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

[Module Firmware](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0839)

Segment operational network and systems to restrict access to critical system functions to predetermined management systems.[\[3\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/sites/default/files/recommended_practices/NCCIC_ICS-CERT_Defense_in_Depth_2016_S508C.pdf)

ICS

[T0842](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0842)

[Network Sniffing](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0842)

Segment networks and systems appropriately to reduce access to critical system and services communications.

ICS

[T0861](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0861)

[Point & Tag Identification](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0861)

Segment operational assets and their management devices based on their functional role within the process. Enabling more strict isolation to more critical control and operational information within the control environment.[\[4\]](https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/Legacy/SP/nistspecialpublication800-41r1.pdf)[\[5\]](https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.800-82r2.pdf)[\[3\]](https://us-cert.cisa.gov/sites/default/files/recommended_practices/NCCIC_ICS-CERT_Defense_in_Depth_2016_S508C.pdf)[\[6\]](https://www.sans.org/reading-room/whitepapers/ICS/protect-critical-infrastructure-systems-whitelisting-35312)

ICS

[T0886](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0886)

[Remote Services](https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T0886)

Segment and control software movement between business and OT environments by way of one directional DMZs. Web access should be restricted from the OT environment. Engineering workstations, including transient cyber assets (TCAs) should have minimal connectivity to external networks, including Internet and email, further limit the extent to which these devices are dual-homed to multiple networks.[\[8\]](https://www.natf.net/docs/natf/documents/resources/security/natf-transient-cyber-asset-guidance.pdf)
